Defining the Common Hireling (Ajir Mushtarak) and His Liability
Defines the common laborer and begins discussion of his liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definition of the common hireling according to the Hanafi school and state the default rule for his liability for goods in his custody.

Core Idea
The common hireling is defined by his capacity to work for multiple employers, and he is not liable for goods that perish by his act — even with transgression — according to the text.

This passage from the chapter on the liability of the hireling presents the definition of the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) and an initial statement on his liability. The text distinguishes the common hireling from the special hireling based on the object of the contract: work vs. benefits. The ruling on liability is stated as an agreement of the three Imams, but note that this assertion is controversial and requires careful reading within the full Hanafi framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the definition
The passage opens by defining 'al-ajir al-mushtarak' as one who works for more than one person, giving examples like the dyer and washerman. Identify what is being defined and the context (chapter on liability).
The term 'ajir' here means hireling, and 'mushtarak' indicates commonality.
2
Analyze the defining elements
The definition contains two key features: (1) the hireling works for multiple persons (or is not exclusive to one), and (2) he does not earn the wage until he actually performs the work. Understand why these are defining.
The wage entitlement condition distinguishes from the special hireling.
3
Examine the commentary on the definition
The commentary clarifies that actual work for multiple persons is not a strict condition; rather, the crucial point is that the hireling is not obligated to be exclusive to one employer. Even if he works for only one, he is considered common if he could take work from others.
This nuance comes from al-Zayla'i and avoids circularity in the definition.
4
Extract the liability rule
The passage divides the loss of goods: (a) perishes by the hireling's act, (b) perishes without his act. For category (a), the text states that the hireling does not guarantee 'whether with or without transgression' by agreement of the three Imams. Note this explicitly.
This statement appears to contradict standard Hanafi rulings where transgression (ta'addi) creates liability. The passage may be incomplete or requires further qualification.
5
Consider the scope and caution
Recognize that this is an opening statement. The full discussion likely covers nuances: if the hireling transgresses, he may become liable. The source itself flags that the text ends abruptly. For now, note the stated position as a foundation to be refined later.
Check the review note for this chunk for more context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ضمان الأجير
الأجير المشترك من يعمل لغير واحد، ولا يستحق الأجر حتى يعمل كالصباغ والقصار، والمتاع في يده .
وصفته أنه لا يستحق إلخ
باب ضمان أجير: أي هذا باب بيان ضمان الأجير، والمراد بضمان الأجير إثباته ونفيه أي في أي صورة يجب على الأجير ضمان وفي أي موضع لا يجب لا إثباته فقط، وإلا لم يصح عنوان الباب على قول الإمام؛ لأنه لا ضمان عنده على أحد من الأجير المشترك والخاص. كذا) في التكملة بتوضيح من المحشي) ضمان لما فرغ من ذكر أنواع الإجارة صحة وفسادا شرع في بيان الضمان؛ لأنه من عوارضها. الأجير: [هو فعيل بمعنى فاعل، وفي المجمل": أجرت الرجل مؤاجرة إذا جعلت له على فعله أجرة. (مسكين)] الأجير نوعان: أجير مشترك وأجير خاص، وفي هذا الباب يبين أحكامهما وتعريفهما.
الأجير المشترك: قدم الأجير المشترك وسيأتي بيان الأجير الخاص من يعمل إلخ: اعلم أنه يفهم من ظاهر كلام المصنف أنه يشترط للأجير المشترك أن يعمل لغير واحد، وإلا لم يكن مشتركا لكنه ليس كذلك، قال الزيلعي : معناه: من لا يجب عليه أن يختص بواحد عمل لغيره أو لم يعمل، ولا يشترط أن يكون عاملا لغير واحد، بل إذا عمل لواحد أيضا، فهو مشترك إذا كان بحيث لا يمتنع، ولا يتعذر عليه أن يعمل لغيره. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٣٥/٦] ولا يستحق الأجر إلخ: يعني أن الأجير المشترك الذي يعمل لغير واحد لا يستحق الأجر حتى يعمل؛ لأن المعقود عليه العمل، فإذا لم يسلم إلى المستأجر لا يجب الأجر، بقي أن يقال: مفهوم قوله : "حتى يعمل" أن الأجير الخاص يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه وإن لم يعمل هكذا فرق بينهما القدوري قال الزيلعي: وهذا يؤول إلى الدور؛ لأن هذا حكم لا يعرفه إلا من يعرف الأجير المشترك والخاص والأوجه أن يقال: الأجير المشترك من يكون عقده واردا على عمل معلوم ببيان محله والأجير الخاص من يكون عقده واردا على منافعه. وحكمهما: أن المشترك له أن يتقبل العمل من أشخاص؛ لأن المعقود عليه في حقه هو العمل أو أثره، فكان له أن يتقبل من العامة؛ لأن منافعه لم تصر مستحقة لواحد فمن هذا الوجه يسمى مشتركا، والأجير الخاص لا يمكنه أن يعمل لغيره؛ لأن منافعه في المدة صارت مستحقة للمستأجر، والأجر مقابل بالمنافع، ولهذا يبقى الأجر مستحقا، وإن نقص العمل. (فتح)
والمتاع إلخ : تفصيل المقام: أن المتاع الذي هلك في يد الأجير المشترك، إما أن يهلك بفعل الأجير أو لا، والأول إما بالتعدي أو لا، والثاني أي إذا لم يهلك بفعل الأجير، إما أن يهلك بسبب يمكن الاحتراز عنه أو لا، ففي القسم الأول – وهو أن يهلك بفعله سواء كان بتعد أو لا - لا يضمن الأجير اتفاقا بين أئمتنا
Chapter on the Liability of the Hireling. The common hireling is one who works for more than one person, and he does not deserve the wage until he works, like the dyer and the washerman, and the goods are in his hand. Its description is that he does not deserve etc. Chapter on the liability of the hireling: this is a chapter explaining the liability of the hireling. The meaning of 'liability of the hireling' is its affirmation and negation, i.e., in which situations liability is required of the hireling and in which it is not, not just its affirmation. Otherwise the title of the chapter would not be correct according to the statement of the Imam, because there is no liability according to him for either the common or the special hireling. Thus in al-Takmilah with clarification from the commentator. Liability: after finishing the types of ijarah, valid and invalid, he begins to explain liability because it is among its attributes. The hireling: it is fa'il in the sense of faa'il, and in al-Mujmal: 'I hired the man if I set a wage for his work.' The hireling is of two types: common hireling and special hireling. In this chapter, their rulings and definitions are explained. The common hireling: he presents the common hireling and later the special hireling will be explained. 'Who works' etc.: Know that it is understood from the apparent statement of the author that it is a condition for the common hireling to work for more than one person, otherwise he would not be common, but it is not so. Al-Zayla'i said: its meaning is: one who is not obliged to be exclusive to one person, whether he works for others or not. It is not a condition that he works for more than one; even if he works for one, he is common if it is not impossible or difficult for him to work for others. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 6/135] 'And he does not deserve the wage' etc.: It means that the common hireling who works for more than one does not deserve the wage until he works, because the object of the contract is the work, and if it is not delivered to the hirer, the wage is not due. It remains to be said: the implication of his statement 'until he works' is that the special hireling deserves the wage by surrendering himself even if he does not work. Thus al-Quduri differentiated between them. Al-Zayla'i said: this leads to circular reasoning because this ruling is only known by one who knows the common and special hireling. The better view is to say: the common hireling is one whose contract is on a known work by specifying its place, and the special hireling is one whose contract is on his benefits. Their ruling: the common one can accept work from multiple persons because the object of the contract is the work or its effect, so he can accept from the public because his benefits are not owed to one person; thus he is called common. The special hireling cannot work for others because his benefits during the period become owed to the hirer, and the wage is in exchange for benefits, so the wage remains due even if the work is lacking. (Fath) 'And the goods' etc.: A detailed explanation: the goods that perish in the hand of the common hireling, either they perish by the act of the hireling or not. The first is either with transgression or without. The second, i.e., if it does not perish by his act, either it perishes due to a cause that can be avoided or not. In the first category – i.e., if it perishes by his act whether with or without transgression – the hireling does not guarantee by agreement of our Imams.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the liability (daman) of the hireling (ajir). It first defines the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) as one who works for multiple people, such as a dyer or washerman, and who does not earn the wage until he actually performs the work. The goods entrusted to him are in his possession as a trust (amana). The commentary clarifies that the definition is not about actually working for multiple individuals but rather that he is not obligated to be exclusive to one; even if he works for only one, he remains a common hireling if he is capable of working for others. The passage then distinguishes between the common and special hireling: the common hireling's contract is on the work itself, while the special hireling's contract is on his benefits (manafi). Consequently, the common hireling can accept work from multiple people, whereas the special hireling cannot, as his benefits are exclusively owed to the hirer. The second part discusses the liability of the common hireling for goods in his possession. The Hanafi position, agreed upon by the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), is that the common hireling is not liable for goods that perish in his hand if the loss is due to his own act, whether or not it involves transgression. This is because the goods are in his hand as a trust, and a trustee (amin) is not liable for loss unless there is negligence or transgression. However, if the loss is due to a cause that could have been avoided and he failed to take precautions, there may be liability. The passage sets the foundation for the detailed rules that follow.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A hireling who is not exclusively committed to one employer; his contract is on a specific work, and he may accept work from multiple persons.
الأجير الخاص (al-ajir al-khas): A hireling whose contract is on his benefits (manafi) for a specified period; he is exclusive to one employer during that time.
ضمان (daman): Liability, guarantee, or obligation to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about the common hireling?
A) He is liable for goods that perish by his act, whether with or without transgression.
B) He is not liable for goods that perish by his act, whether with or without transgression.
C) He is liable only if the loss is due to his transgression.
D) He is not liable if the loss occurs without his act, but liable if with his act.

Key Takeaway
The common hireling is defined by his capacity to work for multiple employers, and the initial text states he is not liable for goods perishing by his act even with transgression, though this ruling requires careful contextualization.

Liability of the Common Worker: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ajir mushtarak liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of the ajir mushtarak for goods lost due to preventable causes, and identify the multiple mufta bihi positions.

Core Idea
The common worker is not liable by qiyas, but istihsan may impose liability; fatwa practice offers multiple solutions based on circumstances.

The liability of the ajir mushtarak (common worker) for goods that perish in his custody is a classic Hanafi ikhtilaf. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Zufar (non-liability by qiyas) versus the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, liability by istihsan), along with later fatwa developments that offer compromise solutions. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists balance textual analogy (qiyas) with juristic preference (istihsan) and adapt rulings to changing social conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested case
The disputed scenario is when goods in the common worker's hands perish due to a cause that can be avoided (e.g., theft if left unsecured), without direct action by the worker.
Other cases (damage by worker's action, unpreventable causes) are agreed upon.
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa and Zufar hold he is not liable (qaul al-Imam). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold he is liable (qaul al-Sahibayn).
Both positions are recorded in zahir al-riwayah.
3
Analyze the proofs
The Imam's qiyas likens the worker to a depositee (wadi'ah): possession with permission implies no liability. The Sahibayn's istihsan argues that the contract requires preservation (hifz), so failure to preserve triggers liability, as in a paid deposit.
The istihsan overrides qiyas due to the nature of the contract.
4
Examine later fatwa positions
Later scholars offered multiple operative rulings: following the Imam, following the Sahibayn, a compromise of half value, or distinguishing based on the worker's uprightness (upright → no liability; suspect → liability; concealed → half value).
The choice depends on context and the mufti's assessment of the worker's character.
5
Identify the scope
This dispute only applies when the ijarah is valid. If the contract is void (fasid), there is consensus that the worker is not liable.
Void contracts remove the basis for both qiyas and istihsan regarding preservation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
باب ضمان الأجير
الأجير المشترك من يعمل لغير واحد، ولا يستحق الأجر حتى يعمل كالصباغ والقصار، والمتاع في يده.
غير مضمون بالهلاك، وما تلف بعمله كتخريق الثوب من دقه وزلق الحمال، لأن المعقود عليه هو العمل.
لكن إن هلك بسبب لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه لا يضمن أيضا بقي قسم واحد وهو أن يهلك بغير فعل بسبب يمكن الاحتراز عنه ففيه خلاف، فعند أبي حنيفة وزفر لا يضمن وهو القياس، وقالا يضمن استحسانا؛ ولأن المعقود عليه الحفظ، وفيما ذكر لم يوجد الحفظ التام كما في الوديعة إذا كانت بأجر، وكما إذا هلك بفعله. وجه القياس أن القبض حصل بإذنه، فلا يكون مضمونا عليه كالوديعة والعارية، ولهذا لا يضمن فيما لا يمكن التحرز عنه كالموت والغصب. واختلفوا في الفتوى، قال في الدر المختار: وبقول الإمام يفتى كما في عامة المعتبرات، وقال في الفتح: وفي الزيلعي: وبقولهما يفتى اليوم؛ لتغير أحوال الناس وبه يحصل صيانة أموالهم، واختار المتأخرون الفتوى بالصلح على نصف القيمة، وقيل: إن كان الأجير مصلحا لا يضمن وإن غير مصلح يضمن، وإن كان مستورا فالصلح على نصف القيمة. ثم اعلم أن هذا الخلاف فيما إذا كانت الإجارة صحيحة، وأما إذا كانت فاسدة لا ضمان عليه بالاتفاق.
وما تلف أي المتاع الذي تلف بعمل الأجير مضمون، ولا يستحق الأجير الأجرة؛ لأنه ما أوفى المنفعة بل بالمضرة. كتخريق الثوب أي لو تخرق الثوب لتقصيره في العمل، أو لعدم معرفته بالعمل يضمن، وقيد بقوله بعمله فشمل عمله بنفسه وعمل أجيره؛ لأنه عمله حكما. وزلق الحمال أي استأجر رجل حمالا ليحمل له كذا إلى موضع كذا فزلق الحمال في أثناء الطريق، إن حصل بجناية يده ضمن وإن حصل بما لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه كما إذا كان من زحمة الناس لا يضمن عند الإمام وعندهما يضمن.
Book of Ijarah. Chapter of Liability of the Worker. The common worker is one who works for more than one person and is not entitled to wages until he works, like the dyer and the washerman, and the goods are in his hand. Goods are not guaranteed against loss, and what is ruined by his action like tearing the cloth from his pounding and the slipping of the porter, because the contracted object is the work. But if it perishes due to a cause that cannot be avoided, he is not liable either. One case remains: if it perishes without his action due to a cause that can be avoided, then there is a dispute. According to Abu Hanifa and Zufar, he is not liable, and that is analogy. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said he is liable by istihsan, because the contracted object is preservation, and in the mentioned case complete preservation was not found, as in the case of a paid deposit, and as if it perishes by his action. The basis of analogy is that the possession was obtained with permission, so it is not guaranteed, like deposit and loan, and therefore he is not liable for what cannot be avoided, like death and usurpation. They differed on the fatwa. In al-Durr al-Mukhtar: The fatwa is on the statement of the Imam, as in most reliable works. In al-Fath: In al-Zaylai: Today the fatwa is on their statement due to the change of people's conditions and thereby their property is safeguarded. The later scholars chose the fatwa on compromise for half the value. It is said: if the worker is upright he does not guarantee; if not upright he guarantees; if he is of concealed character, then compromise for half the value. Know that this dispute is when the hire contract is valid; if it is void, there is no liability by agreement. And what is ruined: i.e., the goods that are ruined by the worker's action are guaranteed, and the worker does not deserve wages because he did not fulfill the benefit but rather harm. Like tearing of the cloth: i.e., if the cloth is torn due to his negligence or lack of skill, he guarantees. The condition 'by his action' includes his own action and the action of his employee, because that is legally his action. The slipping of the porter: i.e., a man hired a porter to carry something to a place, then the porter slipped on the way. If it occurred by his own hand, he guarantees; if due to something unavoidable, like crowd pressure, he does not guarantee according to the Imam, but according to them he guarantees.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq discusses the liability of the common worker (ajir mushtarak) — one who works for multiple people and only earns wages upon completion of work. The ruling is that the goods in his hand are not automatically guaranteed against loss. However, if the worker himself causes damage (e.g., tearing cloth while processing or a porter slipping due to his own fault), he is liable and loses his wages because he did not deliver the benefit but rather harm. The central dispute occurs regarding loss caused by a preventable external factor. Imam Abu Hanifa (with Zufar) holds that since the worker took possession with permission, he is like a depositee or borrower — not liable unless he is negligent. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue by istihsan that the contract's object is preservation (hifz), and the worker failed in that duty, making him liable, as in a paid deposit. Over time, fatwa practice varied: some follow the Imam, some the companions, and later scholars prefer a compromise of half the value if the worker's character is unknown. Note that this all applies only to valid hire contracts; in void contracts, there is no liability by agreement.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A worker who works for multiple employers and is only entitled to wages upon completion of the work.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage to property in one's possession.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common cause.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juridical preference that sets aside qiyas for a more equitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or a stronger textual indication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the common worker's liability for goods lost due to a cause that can be avoided (e.g., theft if left unsecured) when the hire contract is valid?
A) He is always liable by consensus.
B) He is never liable by consensus.
C) There is a dispute: Abu Hanifa says no liability; the Sahibayn say liability.
D) He is liable for half the value by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The common worker's liability for preventable loss is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, resolved through multiple fatwa positions depending on the worker's character and societal needs.

Liability of the Common Hired Worker: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
States the rule of non-liability and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with fatwa solutions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the liability of the ajir mushtarak, and identify the mufta bihi positions adopted by later Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
The hired worker is not liable by default; the dispute is only for avoidable losses, and fatwa varies.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, the author presents the general rule that a common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) is not liable for accidental destruction of goods. However, there is a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute when the loss could have been avoided. This lesson will dissect the arguments of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explore how later scholars reconciled these positions for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the default rule and scope
Identify the general principle: the ajir mushtarak is not liable for destruction, and note that this is undisputed for unavoidable causes. Pinpoint the contested category: avoidable loss without direct act.
The default is non-liability; disputes only arise in a narrow window.
2
Identify the two positions
State the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa (with Zufar) and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). One says no liability (qiyas); the other says liability (istihsan).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf at the highest level.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the qiyas argument: possession with permission eliminates liability, analogized to wadi'ah and ariyah. Then examine the istihsan argument: the contracted object is preservation (hifz), and preservation was incomplete.
Both proofs are valid within Hanafi methodology; the dispute is about which principle should take priority.
4
Examine the intra-madhhab rebuttal
See the Hanafi response: the contract is for work, not preservation; preservation is subsidiary. Also note that the Sahibayn's analogy to a paid deposit (wadi'ah bi-ujrah) differs because there the preservation is primary.
The rebuttal reaffirms that qiyas is the stronger principle in this case.
5
Determine the fatwa hierarchy
List the four later fatwa positions: following Imam Abu Hanifa, following the Sahibayn, reconciliation for half the value, and distinction based on the worker's righteousness. Note that the last two are praised by later authorities.
These positions reflect the evolution of fatwa over time to suit changing circumstances.

١٦٨
ضمان الأجير
غير مضمون بالهلاك، وما تلف بعمله كتخريق الثوب من دقه وزلق الحمال،
لأن
من غير تعد مبتدأ وقوله مضمون خبره
القصار الثوب لغزيدن
الأب
جير
لكن
- إن هلك بسبب لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه لا يضمن أيضا بقي قسم واحد وهو أن يهلك بغير فعل بسبب يمكن الاحتراز عنه ففيه خلاف، فعند أبي حنيفة وحلله: لا يضمن وهو القياس، وقالا: يضمن استحسانا؛ عمر وعليا ما ضمناه، ولأن المعقود عليه الحفظ، وفيما ذكر لم يوجد الحفظ التام كما في الوديعة إذا كانت بأجر، وكما إذا هلك بفعله وجه القياس أن القبض حصل بإذنه، فلا يكون مضمونا عليه كالوديعة والعارية، ولهذا لا يضمن فيما لا يمكن التحرز عنه كالموت والغصب ولو كان مضمونا عليه لما اختلف الحال، ولا نسلم الحفظ بل العمل، والحفظ تبعا بخلاف الوديعة بأجرة؛ لأن الحفظ وجب مقصودا، وبخلاف
أن المعقود عليه هو
ما إذا تلف بعمله؛ لأن العقد يقتضي سلامة المعقود عليه وهو العمل، فإذا لم يكن سليما ضمن. واختلفوا في الفتوى، قال في الدر المختار: وبقول الإمام يفتى كما في عامة المعتبرات، وقال في "الفتح": وفي "الزيلعي" : وبقولهما يفتى اليوم؛ لتغير أحوال الناس وبه يحصل صيانة ،أموالهم وكذا في "الشامي"، واختار المتأخرون الفتوى بالصلح على نصف القيمة، وقيل: إن كان الأجير مصلحا لا يضمن وإن غير مصلح يضمن،
وإن كان مستورا فالصلح على نصف القيمة، كذا في رد المحتار" للشامي، فهذه أربعة أقوال للفتوى، قال في " الخيرية": فهذه أربعة أقوال كلها مصححة مفتي بها، وما أحسن التفصيل الأخير كذا نقل في "رد المحتار". ثم اعلم أن هذا الخلاف فيما إذا كانت الإجارة صحيحة، وأما إذا كانت فاسدة لا ضمان عليه بالاتفاق. (ملخص الشروح ورد المحتار وغيره)
Book of Hire. 168. Liability of the hired worker. Not liable for destruction, and what is destroyed by his work, like tearing a garment from his pounding and the porter's slip, because... from without transgression is the subject and 'liable' is its predicate... But if it perishes due to a cause that cannot be avoided, he is also not liable. Only one category remains: that it perishes without his act by a cause that can be avoided, and there is disagreement. According to Abu Hanifa and Zufar: he is not liable, and that is qiyas. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is liable by istihsan; Umar and Ali did not hold him liable. And because the contracted object is preservation, and in what was mentioned, complete preservation was not found, as in a deposit with hire, and as if it perishes by his act. The basis of qiyas is that possession occurred with permission, so it is not held liable over him, like a deposit and a loan. For this reason, he is not liable for what cannot be avoided, like death and usurpation. And if he were liable, the case would not differ. And we do not accept preservation but rather work, and preservation is subsidiary, unlike a deposit with hire because preservation was intended as a purpose, and unlike when it perishes by his act, because the contract requires soundness of the contracted object, which is the work, so if it is not sound, he is liable. They differed on fatwa: in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: by the Imam's saying is given fatwa, as in most reliable works. In al-Fath and al-Zaylai: by their saying fatwa is given today due to changed circumstances, and so in al-Shami. The later scholars chose fatwa by reconciliation for half the value. And it was said: if the worker is righteous, not liable; if not righteous, liable; if obscure, reconciliation for half the value. So these are four statements for fatwa. In al-Khayriyya: these four statements are all correct and fit for fatwa, and how excellent is the last detail, as transmitted in Radd al-Muhtar. Then know that this disagreement is when the hire contract is valid; if corrupt, no liability by consensus.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage opens the section on the liability of the ajir mushtarak (common hired worker, like a porter or tailor). The base text of Kanz al-Daqaiq states that the hired worker is not liable for accidental destruction of the goods. The commentator expands this by dividing causes of loss. If the loss is unavoidable (e.g., death, usurpation), all agree no liability. The dispute concerns loss from a cause that could have been avoided but is not directly the worker's act. Abu Hanifa and Zufar hold no liability, analogizing to a deposit or loan (possession with permission). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold liability by istihsan, arguing that the contract entails preservation, and the worker's preservation is incomplete. They also note that Umar and Ali did not hold the worker liable, which the Sahibayn reinterpret. The passage then lists four fatwa positions: (1) Abu Hanifa's view; (2) the Sahibayn's view; (3) reconciliation for half the value; (4) distinction based on the worker's righteousness. The preferred fatwa is reconciliation or the distinction. Importantly, these disputes only apply to valid hire contracts; in a corrupt hire, no liability at all.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajīr mushtarak): A hired worker who works for multiple people or is available for hire by the public, not exclusively for one employer.
ضمان (ḍamān): Legal liability to compensate for damage or loss, specifically here for the hired goods.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Preferring a ruling based on equity or public interest over strict analogy (qiyas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the ajir mushtarak not liable for accidental loss?
A) Because the worker is poor and cannot afford compensation
B) Because the worker took possession with permission, like a deposit
C) Because the contract explicitly excludes liability
D) Because all loss is considered an act of God

Key Takeaway
The default is no liability; the intra-Hanafi dispute is limited to avoidable losses, and later fatwa recommends reconciliation or distinction based on the worker's character.

Liability of the Hired Worker: Tearing Cloth and Porter Slipping
Applies the liability dispute of hired workers to specific cases of garment tearing and porter slipping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on liability of a hired worker, distinguishing between direct acts and unavoidable causes, and state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
A hired worker's liability hinges on causation: direct acts or negligence cause liability; unavoidable causes do not.

In this lesson, we examine two concrete cases of damage during hired work: a garment torn while pounding and a porter slipping. These cases reveal a key intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the worker is liable for losses not directly caused by his fault. Understanding these rules helps you apply the principles of jinnayat al-yad and the difference between direct and indirect causation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
There are two distinct cases: (1) a garment torn during pounding by the worker, (2) a porter slipping while carrying goods. Each raises the issue of liability for damage during the course of work.
2
State the general principle: liability for direct damage
The base ruling: if the worker causes damage through a direct act (mubashir) or negligence, he is liable (daman) and loses his wage. However, if the cause is unavoidable, the ruling is disputed.
Refer to the phrase 'إن هلك بأمر يمكن التحرز عنه' vs 'بما لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه'.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
For both cases, Abu Hanifa and Zufar hold no liability for unavoidable causes, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold the worker liable if the cause could have been avoided. The text presents these positions and indicates that later fatwas sometimes favor Muhammad's later view (e.g., porter slip at destination).
The dispute is grounded in qiyas vs istihsan.
4
Apply the nuance of completion and doubt
The porter case adds a temporal element: if the slip occurs after reaching the stipulated place, Muhammad's later view absolves the worker and awards the wage. Also, joint causation with doubt (e.g., pounding with owner) leads to no liability per Abu Hanifa, half per Abu Yusuf.
These refinements show the depth of Hanafi reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير مضمون : عند أبي حنيفة وزفر وهو القياس وبه أفتى بعضهم وعندهما عليه الضمان إن هلك بأمر يمكن التحرز عنه. وما تلف إلخ : أي المتاع الذي تلف بعمل الأجير [المشترك] مضمون، ولا يستحق الأجير الأجرة؛ لأنه ما أو فى المنفعة بل بالمضرة. كتخريق الثوب إلخ : أي لو تخرق الثوب لتقصيره في العمل، أو لعدم معرفته بالعمل يضمن، وقيد بقوله: "بعمله" فشمل عمله بنفسه وعمل أجيره؛ لأنه عمله حكما، ولو استعان في الدق بصاحب الثوب فتخرق، و لم يعلم أنه من أي دق، فعلى قول الإمام ينبغي عدم الضمان للشك، وعن أبي يوسف: يضمن نصف النقصان كما لو تمسك به الأجير؛ لاستيفاء الأجير، فجذبه صاحبه فتخرق. ثم في مسألة الكتاب صاحب الثوب إن شاء ضمنه قیمته غير معمول و لم يعطه الأجر، وإن شاء ضمنه معمولا، وأعطاه الأجر، وقد مر نظيره. (ملخص) وزلق الحمال إلخ أي استأجر رجل حمالا ليحمل له كذا إلى موضع كذا فزلق الحمال في أثناء الطريق، إن حصل بجناية يده ضمن وإن حصل بما لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه - كما إذا كان من زحمة الناس لا يضمن عند الإمام وعندهما يضمن وفي "الذخيرة": هذا إذا تلف في وسط الطريق، ولو زلقت رجله بعد ما انتهى إلى المكان المشروط، فله الأجر، ولا ضمان عليه وهو قول محمد أخيرا، وعلى قوله أولا يضمن هنا أيضا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٥٦/٨]
Not liable: according to Abu Hanifa and Zufar, and that is qiyas, and some gave fatwa by it. According to the two, liability is upon him if it perishes by something that can be avoided. 'What perishes' etc.: i.e., goods that are destroyed by the work of the common hired worker are guaranteed, and the worker does not deserve the wage because he did not provide benefit but rather harm. 'Like tearing a garment' etc.: i.e., if the garment is torn due to negligence in work or lack of skill, he is liable. The restriction by 'by his work' includes his own work and the work of his hired helper, because it is legally his work. If he sought help in pounding from the owner of the garment and it tore, and it is not known from which pounding, according to the Imam there should be no liability due to doubt. From Abu Yusuf: he is liable for half the reduction, just as if the worker held it and the owner pulled it and it tore. Then in the issue of the book, the owner of the garment may either claim its value unworked and not give the wage, or claim it worked and give the wage, as has passed. 'And the porter's slip' etc.: i.e., if a man hires a porter to carry something to a specified place for a known wage, and the porter slips on the way: if it occurs by his hand's offense, he is liable; if by something unavoidable, like from a crowd, he is not liable according to the Imam, but according to the two he is liable. In al-Dhakhira: this is if it perishes in the middle of the road. If his foot slips after reaching the stipulated place, he gets the wage and no liability; that is Muhammad's later opinion. According to his earlier opinion, he is liable here too. Continuation of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 56/8.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on specific phrases from the matn. It first clarifies the general principle: goods destroyed by the common hired worker's direct act are 'madhmun' (liable), and the worker loses his wage because he caused harm. The example of tearing cloth: if the worker tears it due to negligence or lack of skill, he is liable. The scope includes acts of his own helper. A nuanced case: if the worker and owner both pound and the cause is unknown, Abu Hanifa denies liability due to doubt, while Abu Yusuf imposes half. The owner has an option: either claim the value of the unworked cloth without paying wage, or claim the value of the worked cloth and pay wage. This is similar to earlier discussions. The second example: a hired porter. If he slips because of his own fault (e.g., clumsy movement), he is liable. If the slip is unavoidable like crowd pressure, Imam says no liability, Sahibayn say liable. If the slip occurs at the destination after completion, Muhammad's final view is no liability and wage is due. The 'continuation' reference indicates this is excerpted from al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Key Terms
جناية اليد (jināyat al-yad): An act of the hand that causes damage, i.e., a direct physical action by the worker.
تخريق الثوب (takhriq al-thawb): Tearing of the garment due to the worker's action in the course of work (e.g., pounding).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, is the porter liable if he slips due to crowd pressure?
A) Yes, because he was carrying the goods
B) No, because the cause was unavoidable
C) Yes, but only if he was paid in advance
D) No, because the owner assumed the risk

Key Takeaway
A hired worker's liability depends on the cause of damage: direct acts or negligence lead to liability; unavoidable causes do not.

Liability of the Common Hired Worker: Rope, Ship, and Jar Cases
Applies liability rules to transportation mishaps and contrasts worker liability for property vs. humans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three conditions for the common hired worker's liability and explain the Hanafi position versus Shafi'i in the dispute over defective work.

Core Idea
The hired worker is liable only for avoidable damage to goods surrendered to him, not for humans or uncontrollable events.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq extends the general rule of hired worker liability to three practical scenarios: a broken rope, a sunken ship, and a cracked jar. Through these cases, the author illustrates when and why the worker is held liable, and the Hanafi school's reasoning against the Shafi'i view. We'll also learn the three conditions that must all be present for liability.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the three test cases
Identify the common thread in the rope, ship, and jar cases: the hired worker's action caused damage that could have been prevented.
These are applications of the same principle.
2
Understand the Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Zufar dispute
Know each side's argument: Hanafi says only sound work is authorized; Shafi'i says permission is absolute. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
This dispute is recorded in al-Hidayah and Bahr al-Ra'iq.
3
Memorize the three conditions for liability
The common hired worker is liable only if: (1) he could prevent the damage, (2) the workspace was surrendered to him, and (3) the item can be guaranteed by contract.
If any condition is missing, no liability.
4
Apply the conditions to each case
For the rope: if it was the porter's rope and he could prevent the break, he is liable. For the ship: captain liable for goods (not humans) if damage from his action; not if from wind. For the jar: owner has option to claim value at start or at break point.
The jar case shows flexibility when damage occurs mid-way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانقطاع حبل يشدّ به الحمل وغرق السفينة من مده مضمون، ولا يضمن به بني
المكاري
آدم، فإن انكسر دن في الطريق.

عند أئمتنا الثلاثة صاحب السفينة
حبل يشد به إلخ [حبل الحمال لا حبل صاحب المتاع] قال محمد في "الأصل": إذا انقطع حبل الحمال وسقط الحمل وتلفه ،ضمن قيد بقوله: يشد به الحمل؛ لأنه لو كان الحبل لصاحب المتاع لا يضمن، قال في "النهاية": ولو حمل بحبل صاحب المتاع، فتلف لم يضمن وقال في "الهداية": وقطع الحبل من قلة اهتمامه، فكان من صنعه. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٥٧/٨] وغرق السفينة إلخ: إذا غرقت السفينة من مد الملاح أو معالجته يضمن؛ لأن ذلك من جناية يده، وإن كان صاحب الطعام أو وكيله في السفينة لا يضمن الملاح؛ لأن الطعام في يد صاحبه إلا أن يصنع فيها شيئا، أو يتعمد الفساد، وقيد المصنف الضمان بالمد؛ لأنها لو غرقت من ريح أو أو موج شيء وقع عليها أو صدم جبل، فهلك ما فيها لا يضمن في قول الإمام. (ملخص) مضمون هذا جواب المسائل كلها فقوله: "وما تلف مبتدأ، ومضمون خبره وهذا عندنا، وقال الإمام الشافعي وزفر : لا يضمن الأجير في هذه المسائل؛ لأنه مأذون فيه، والأمر المطلق ينتظم العمل بنوعيه: المعيب والسليم، فلا يمكن التحرز عن الدق المعيب، ولنا أن التلف حصل بفعل غير مأذون فيه؛ لأن المأذون فيه هو السليم دون غيره عرفا وعادة، فيضمن.
واعلم أن الأجير المشترك إنما يضمن ما تلف في يده بشرائط ثلاثة: الأول: أن يكون في قدرته دفع ذلك الفساد، فلو لم يكن له قدرة على ذلك كما لو غرقت السفينة من موج أو ريح أو جبل صدمها لا ضمان على الملاح. الثاني: أن يكون محل العمل مسلما إليه بالتخلية، فلو لم يكن محل العمل مسلما إليه بأن كان رب المتاع في السفينة أو وكيله، فانكسرت السفينة بجذب الملاح لم يضمن الثالث: أن يكون المضمون ما يجوز أن. يضمن بالعقد، فلو استأجر دابة لحمل عبد صغير أو كبير، فلا ضمان على المكاري فيما عطب من سوقه أو قوده. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٥٥/٨]
ولا يضمن إلخ يعني إذا غرقت السفينة بمد الملاح وغرق من فيها لا يضمن الملاح بني آدم، وكذا إذا ساق المكاري الدابة أو قادها فسقط الراكب بسوقه وقوده من الدابة لا يضمن سواء كان الراكب ممن يستمسك على الدابة أو لا يستمسك كالرضيع؛ لأن ضمان الآدمي لا يجب بالعقد بالجناية، وما يجب بالجناية يجب على العاقلة، والعاقلة لا تتحمل ضمان العقود، وقد مر أن ضمان ما يتلف من الأجير المشترك مشروط بثلاث: منها أن يكون المضمون مما يجوز أن يضمن بالعقد، فتذكره، فإن هذه المسألة . من تفريعاته. فإن انكسر إلخ: أي إن استأجر حمالا ليحمل له دنا على ظهره، أو دابة إلى موضع معلوم بأجر معلوم، فحمل، ثم انكسر الدن في بعض الطريق، فالمالك بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمته في المكان الذي حمله منه، ولا أجر له، وإن شاء ضمنه قيمته محمولا في الموضع الذي انكسر ، وأعطاه أجره بحسابه، وكذا إذا كسره عمدا، فالمالك بالخيار، أما الضمان، فلأنه تلف بفعله؛ لأن الداخل تحت العقد عمل سليم، والمفسد غير داخل، وأما الخيار؛ فلأنه إذا هذا الوجه، وله وجه آخر: وهو أن – انكسر في الطريق والحمل شيء ،واحد تبين أنه وقع تعديا من الابتداء من =
And the breaking of a rope with which the load is tied, and the sinking of a ship from its extension is liable, and he is not liable for human beings. The ship captain? The rope etc.: [The porter's rope, not the owner's rope]. Muhammad said in al-Asl: If the porter's rope breaks and the load falls and perishes, he is liable; the qualification 'with which the load is tied' because if it were the owner's rope, he is not liable. In al-Nihaya: If he carried with the owner's rope and it perished, he is not liable. In al-Hidayah: The breaking of the rope from his lack of care, so it is from his act. Continuation of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 57/8. And the sinking of the ship etc.: If the ship sinks from the extension or handling of the ship captain, he is liable because that is from his hand's offense. If the owner of the food or his agent is in the ship, the ship captain is not liable because the food is in the owner's hand, unless he does something or intentionally causes corruption. The author restricted liability to extension because if it sinks from wind or wave or something striking it or hitting a mountain, what is in it perishes without liability according to the Imam. (Summary) 'Guaranteed' is the answer to all issues: his saying 'what perishes' is subject, and 'guaranteed' is predicate, and this is according to us. Imam al-Shafi'i and Zufar said: The hired worker is not liable in these matters because he is permitted, and absulote command encompasses both defective and sound work, so one cannot avoid defective pounding. Our proof: the destruction occurred by an unauthorized act, because the authorized is only the sound work customarily, so he is liable. Know that the common hired worker is only liable for what perishes in his hand under three conditions: first, that he has the ability to prevent that corruption; if he cannot, like if the ship sinks from wave or wind or mountain strike, no liability on the captain. Second, that the place of work is surrendered to him; if not, like if the owner or his agent is in the ship, and the ship breaks from the captain's pull, he is not liable. Third, that what is liable is such that it can be guaranteed by contract; if he hires an animal to carry a small or large child, the carrier is not liable for what is damaged from his driving or leading. Continuation of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 55/8. And he is not liable etc. means if the ship sinks by the captain's extension and those in it drown, the captain is not liable for human beings. Similarly, if the carrier drives or leads the animal and the rider falls due to his driving and leading, he is not liable, whether the rider is one who holds on or not, like an infant, because the guarantee of a human being does not become obligatory by contract; if by offense, it is on the 'aqila, and the 'aqila does not bear contractual guarantees. It has passed that the guarantee of what perishes from the common hired worker is conditional on three: including that what is guaranteed is such that it can be guaranteed by contract, so remember it, for this issue is from its branches. If a jar breaks etc.: i.e., if a man hires a porter to carry a jar on his back, or an animal to a known place for a known wage, and he carries it, then the jar breaks on the way, the owner has the choice: if he wishes, he may claim its value at the place from which he carried it and pay no wage; if he wishes, he may claim its value as carried at the place where it broke and pay the wage proportionately. Similarly, if he breaks it intentionally, the owner has the choice. As for liability, because it perished by his act, for the contracted work is sound, and the corrupting is not included. As for choice, because... on this aspect, another aspect: that it broke on the way and the load is one item, it becomes clear that a transgression occurred from the beginning...
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage continues with specific applications of the liability rules for the common hired worker. First case: the rope used to tie a load. If the porter's own rope breaks due to his carelessness, he is liable. If the rope belongs to the goods owner, no liability. Second case: a ship sinking due to the captain's action (extending or handling). The captain is liable for goods but not for human life. If the goods owner is on board, the captain is not liable for goods because they remain in the owner's possession. External causes like wind or waves absolve the captain. Third, the commentator mentions a dispute with Shafi'i and Zufar, who hold no liability because permission covers both sound and defective work. Hanafi respond that only sound work is authorized customarily. The passage then lists three essential conditions for the hired worker's liability: (1) the worker must have been able to prevent the damage, (2) the workspace must have been surrendered to him (i.e., owner not present), and (3) the item must be capable of being subject to contractual guarantee (e.g., property, not human beings). Finally, the jar-break case: a porter hired to carry a jar; if it breaks on the way, the owner has an option: either claim the value at the starting point without paying wage, or claim the value at the break point with proportional wage. The text ends abruptly discussing that if the jar breaks partway, it may indicate initial transgression.

Key Terms
تخلية (takhliyah): The physical handing over and emptying of the workspace for the worker, so that no owner or agent remains.
عاقلة (ʿāqila): A group (usually paternal relatives) who pay blood money (diyah) for unintentional homicide.
أجير مشترك (ajīr mushtarak): A hired worker whose work is for the public, not a specific person; e.g., a porter, tailor, or ship captain.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or guarantee; monetary compensation for damage or loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is NOT a condition for the common hired worker's liability?
A) The worker must have been able to prevent the damage.
B) The workspace must be surrendered to the worker (takhliyah).
C) The item must be of a type that can be guaranteed by contract.
D) The worker must be a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The hired worker's liability requires three conditions: ability to prevent, surrender of workspace, and insurable subject matter; without any, no liability.

Liability of the Common Hired Worker: Three Conditions
Rulings on porter and boatman liability with three conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which an ajir mushtarak is liable for damages and apply them to distinguish cases of liability from non-liability.

Core Idea
A common hired worker is liable for damage only if he could prevent it, the work was fully handed over, and the item is contractually guaranteeable.

This lesson centers on the Hanafi ruling that a common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) is liable for goods damaged through his action or negligence, but only under three precise conditions. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq uses the examples of a porter whose rope breaks and a boatman whose ship sinks to illustrate when liability attaches and when it does not. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the school's position, especially in contrast to other views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the ruling concerns the liability (daman) of the ajir mushtarak. The base ruling: if the porter's rope breaks or the boatman's pushing sinks the ship, the worker is liable.
The ruling is that the worker must compensate for the loss of goods, but not for human life.
2
Locate the dalil for liability
Understand the Hanafi proof: the damage occurs through an unauthorized act because permission is only for sound work by custom ('urf). The broken rope results from lack of care, thus it is the worker's doing.
The opposing view (Shafi'i, Zufar) holds that absolute permission covers both sound and defective work, so no liability.
3
Examine the three conditions for liability
Learn that liability only arises when (1) the worker could prevent the damage, (2) the work was fully handed over (takhliyah), and (3) the item is of a type that can be guaranteed by contract (e.g., goods, not humans).
These conditions are extracted from the examples and commentary.
4
Apply the conditions to the examples
Work through the porter and boatman cases: the rope breaking is preventable and the load is in his control; the ship sinking from the boatman's pushing is his action; but if an act of nature causes sinking, no liability. Also, if the owner is present, takhliyah is absent, so no liability.
Humans are excluded from contractual liability altogether.
5
Contrast with the opposing madhhab and derive the thamarah
Note that Shafi'i and Zufar hold the worker not liable in these cases because permission is absolute. The practical effect: in Hanafi courts, the hirer can claim compensation; in Shafi'i practice, he cannot.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, supported by custom and legal reasoning.

(ملخص) مضمون هذا جواب المسائل كلها فقوله: "وما تلف مبتدأ، ومضمون خبره وهذا عندنا، وقال الإمام الشافعي وزفر : لا يضمن الأجير في هذه المسائل؛ لأنه مأذون فيه، والأمر المطلق ينتظم العمل بنوعيه: المعيب والسليم، فلا يمكن التحرز عن الدق المعيب، ولنا أن التلف حصل بفعل غير مأذون فيه؛ لأن المأذون فيه هو السليم دون غيره عرفا وعادة، فيضمن.
واعلم أن الأجير المشترك إنما يضمن ما تلف في يده بشرائط ثلاثة: الأول: أن يكون في قدرته دفع ذلك الفساد، فلو لم يكن له قدرة على ذلك كما لو غرقت السفينة من موج أو ريح أو جبل صدمها لا ضمان على الملاح. الثاني: أن يكون محل العمل مسلما إليه بالتخلية، فلو لم يكن محل العمل مسلما إليه بأن كان رب المتاع في السفينة أو وكيله، فانكسرت السفينة بجذب الملاح لم يضمن الثالث: أن يكون المضمون ما يجوز أن. يضمن بالعقد، فلو استأجر دابة لحمل عبد صغير أو كبير، فلا ضمان على المكاري فيما عطب من سوقه أو قوده. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٥٥/٨]

Book of Ijarah. Liability of the employee. The breaking of a rope with which the load is tied and the sinking of a ship from its [the boatman's] pushing are liable, and he is not liable for human beings thereby. Then if a jar breaks on the way. [marginal: object of 'la yadman' etc.] [Commentary:] The rope etc. [The rope of the porter, not the rope of the owner of the goods.] Muhammad said in al-Asl: If the porter's rope breaks and the load falls and is destroyed, he is liable, restricted by his statement: 'with which the load is tied'; because if the rope belonged to the owner of the goods, he would not be liable. He said in al-Nihaya: If he carried with the owner's rope and it was destroyed, he would not be liable. He said in al-Hidaya: The breaking of the rope is from his lack of care, so it is from his own doing. [Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 8:57] And the sinking of the ship etc.: If the ship sinks from the boatman's pushing or his handling, he is liable, because that is from the injury of his hand. If the owner of the food or his agent is in the ship, the boatman is not liable, because the food is in the hand of its owner, unless he does something to it or intentionally corrupts it. The author restricted liability to pushing, because if it sank from wind or a wave or something falling on it or colliding with a mountain, then what is in it is destroyed, he is not liable in the saying of the Imam. (Summary) The substance of this is the answer to all the issues. So his statement: 'And what is destroyed is the subject, and 'liable' is its predicate, and this is with us. Al-Imam al-Shafi'i and Zufar said: The employee is not liable in these issues, because he is permitted, and absolute command includes both sound and defective work, so it is not possible to guard against defective pounding. Our proof: The destruction occurred by an unauthorized act, because what is authorized is the sound work, not other than it by custom and habit, so he is liable. And know that the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) is only liable for what is destroyed in his hand under three conditions: First: that he has the ability to prevent that corruption; if he does not have that ability, as if the ship sank from a wave or wind or a mountain that collided with it, there is no liability on the boatman. Second: that the place of work is handed over to him with full control (takhliyah); if the place of work is not handed over, as if the owner of the goods or his agent is in the ship, and the ship breaks by the boatman's pulling, he is not liable. Third: that the item guaranteed is such that it is permissible to guarantee it by contract; so if he hired an animal to carry a young or old slave, there is no liability on the carrier for what is damaged from its driving or leading. [Takmila al-Bahr al-Raiq 8:55] And 'he is not liable' etc. means: if the ship sinks by the boatman's pushing and those in it drown, the boatman is not liable for human beings. Similarly, if the carrier drives or leads the animal and the rider falls due to his driving or leading from the animal, he is not liable, whether the rider is one who can hold onto the animal or not, like an infant; because liability for a human being is not required by contract but by tort (jinaya), and what is required by tort is required of the 'aqila, and the 'aqila does not bear contractual liability. And it has passed that the liability of what is destroyed from the common hired worker is conditioned by three: among them that the guaranteed item is such that it is permissible to guarantee by contract, so remember it, for this issue is one of its branches.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on the liability (daman) of the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) in Hanafi fiqh, drawn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentaries. The author begins with two illustrative cases: a porter whose rope breaks causing loss, and a boatman whose pushing sinks a ship. In both, the employee is liable because the damage results from his action or negligence. However, there is an important exception: the employee is NOT liable for any human being (bni Adam) who dies from his action; liability for humans falls under tort (jinaya) and must be borne by the 'aqila (tribal guarantors), not by contract. The passage then presents an inter-madhhab dispute: Shafi'i and Zufar argue the employee is never liable because he is acting with permission, so the contract implicitly includes the risk of defective work. The Hanafi response is that permission is only for sound work by custom ('urf); defective work is unauthorized, so liability attaches. The core of the lesson is the three conditions under which the ajir mushtarak is liable: (1) he must have been able to prevent the damage (e.g., not from natural forces like wind or collision); (2) the work must have been fully handed over to his control (takhliyah)—if the owner or his agent is present, the owner retains control and the employee is not liable; (3) the item must be of a type that can be guaranteed by contract—thus, a hired animal's driving damages to a rider (human) are not contractually guaranteed. These conditions are applied to the initial rulings and explain why the porter/boatman may be liable for goods but not for humans. The passage ends by reiterating that the liability of the ajir mushtarak is subject to these three, and the case of human liability is a branch thereof.

Key Terms
الأجير المشترك (al-ajīr al-mushtarak): A hired worker who undertakes work for multiple people or tasks, not exclusively for one person; his wage is for the result, not his time.
التخلية (al-takhliyah): The handing over of the subject of the hire to the employee's full control, with no presence of the owner or agent.
العاقلة (al-ʿāqila): The group (usually male relatives) who are obligated to pay blood money (diyah) in cases of accidental homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under which condition is a common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) NOT liable for damage?
A) If he was able to prevent the damage but did not.
B) If the work was handed over to him with full control (takhliyah).
C) If the damaged item is a human being.
D) If the damage occurred due to his own negligent action.

Key Takeaway
The ajir mushtarak is liable for damage to goods only when all three conditions – ability to prevent, takhliyah, and contractual guaranteeability – are met, and never for humans.

Liability of the Carrier: When Breakage Occurs by His Action
Ruling on carrier liability for action-caused breakage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on carrier liability to scenarios where breakage is caused by the carrier's own action, and determine the valuation and wage options.

Core Idea
If the carrier breaks goods by his action, he must choose between full liability at start (no wage) or at breakage (with wage).

When a hired carrier breaks goods due to his own action, the contract's initial permission prevents transgression until the moment of breakage. The Hanafi school provides the carrier two options for valuation and wage, balancing fairness to both parties. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind these options and their conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios for liability
Read the passage to find the two places where liability can be assessed: at the start of carriage or at the place of breakage. Note the corresponding wage consequence.
The matn states: 'the carrier is liable for its value at the place of his carrying and he has no wage, or at the place of breakage, and his wage is proportionate.'
2
Understand the concept of transgression (ta'addi)
The commentary explains that carriage initially is not transgression because it was ordered. Transgression only occurs at the moment of breakage. This is why the carrier has a choice: he may be treated as having trespassed from the start or only at breakage.
This reasoning is rational (dalil aqli) based on the nature of permission and harm.
3
Analyze the two valuation options
Option 1: Carrier pays value at start, forfeits wage (as if transgression from start). Option 2: Carrier pays value at breakage, receives proportionate wage (transgression only at breakage).
The choice is the carrier's, but the owner's consent is not required.
4
Identify the condition for these options
These options apply only when breakage is caused by the carrier's own action (e.g., slipping, stumbling). This condition is explicitly stated: 'هذا إذا كان الكسر بصنعه بأن زلق أو عثر'.
External causes are handled in the next lesson.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a carrier slips on a wet floor and breaks a jar, determine which option he would likely choose and justify.
The carrier will choose the option that minimizes his loss; typically he will choose the second (less value if breakage reduces value, but with wage).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضمن الحمال قيمته في مكان حمله ولا أجر له، أو في موضع انكسر، وأجره بحسابه. ابتداء الحمل حصل بأمره، فلم يكن تعديا من الابتداء، وإنما صار تعديا عند الكسر، فيميل إلى أي الجهتين شاء، فإن مال إلى الوجه الأول، ضمنه قيمته عند ابتداء الحمل ولا أجر له، وإن مال إلى الوجه الثاني، ضمنه قيمته عند الكسر، وأعطاه أجره بحسابه هذا إذا كان الكسر بصنعه بأن زلق أو عثر، وإن كان من غير صنعه بأن زحمه الناس، فانكسر لا يضمن عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن المتاع أمانة عنده، وعندهما يضمن قيمته في موضع الكسر، فيعطيه أجره، ولو كان الحمال هو الذي زحم الناس حتى انكسر، فإنه يضمن بالإجماع، وقوله: "في الطريق" قال في "الذخيرة": هو قيد احترازي، فإذا انكسر الدن بعد ما انتهى به إلى بيته فله الأجر، ولا ضمان عليه، وهذا قول محمد آخرا، أما على قول أبي يوسف وهو قول محمد أولا يجب أن يكون ضامنا. ملخص من ملا مسكين والفتح والعيني والتكملة بقدر الحاجة ضمن الحمال إلخ هذا عندنا، وقال زفر إن انكسر لا يضمن وإن كسره عمدا يضمن قيمته في المكان الذي كسره أطلقه، فعم ما لو كان صاحب الدن معه، وبه صرح في البزازية حيث قال: حمل متاعا وصاحبه معه، فعثر وسقط المتاع، ففسد ضمن.
The carrier is liable for its value at the place of his carrying and he has no wage, or at the place of breakage, and his wage is proportionate. The beginning of carrying occurred by his command, so there was no transgression from the beginning, but it became transgression at the time of breakage, so he inclines to whichever of the two aspects he wishes. If he inclines to the first aspect, he is liable for its value at the beginning of carrying and he has no wage; if he inclines to the second aspect, he is liable for its value at the time of breakage and he receives his wage proportionately. This is when the breakage was by his action, such as slipping or stumbling. If it was not by his action, such as people crowding him and it broke, he is not liable according to Abu Hanifa because the goods are a trust with him. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], he is liable for its value at the place of breakage, and he receives his wage. And if the carrier himself crowded people until it broke, then he is liable by consensus. His statement 'in the road'; in al-Dhakhira it is said it is a restrictive qualification. If the jar broke after he reached his home, he has his wage and no liability on him. This is the later view of Muhammad. As for the view of Abu Yusuf, which is the earlier view of Muhammad, he must be liable. Summary from Mulla Miskin, al-Fath, al-Ayni, and al-Takmila as needed: 'the carrier is liable etc.' This is with us. Zufar said: If it breaks, he is not liable, but if he breaks it intentionally, he is liable for its value at the place where he broke it, unconditionally, so it includes even if the owner of the jar was with him. This is clearly stated in al-Bazzaziyya: 'He carried goods and his owner was with him, then he stumbled and the goods fell and spoiled, so he is liable.'
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the liability of a carrier (hammal). It begins by stating the matn: the carrier is liable for the value of the goods at the location where he carried them (meaning the place of initial contract) if he breaks them and does not receive wage; or if the breakage occurs at a different location, he is liable at that location and receives wage proportionately. The commentary then explains that the carriage began with the owner's permission, so initially there is no transgression. Transgression only occurs at the moment of breakage. The carrier thus has two scenarios: if he chooses the first scenario (liable at initial place, no wage), he must pay full value at the start and forfeits wage; if he chooses the second (liable at breakage place, with wage), he pays value where it broke and keeps proportionate wage. This applies when the breakage is due to his own action like slipping. If it happens due to external causes like crowds, Abu Hanifa holds no liability (the goods are a trust), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold liability at the breakage place with wage. If the carrier himself caused the crowd, he is liable by consensus. A key point is the location: if the jar breaks after reaching home, there is no liability and wage is due—this is Muhammad's later view; his earlier view and Abu Yusuf's view impose liability. Zufar holds no liability unless intentional. This analysis follows the Hanafi school's detailed reasoning.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability or guaranty for loss or damage; legal responsibility to compensate.
حمال (hammal): A porter or carrier who transports goods for hire.
تعد (ta'addi): Transgression or unlawful act causing harm; here it is the basis for liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a carrier breaks goods by his own action (e.g., slipping), which statement best describes the Hanafi ruling?
A) The carrier is always liable for the full value and forfeits his wage.
B) The carrier is not liable because the owner hired him.
C) The carrier may choose between paying value at start (no wage) or value at breakage (proportionate wage).
D) The carrier must pay value at breakage and receives full wage.

Key Takeaway
A carrier who breaks goods due to his own action must pay damages; he can choose to either pay full value at start (forfeit wage) or pay value at breakage (keep proportionate wage).

Liability of the Carrier: External Causes and the Home Scenario
Continuation of ruling on carrier liability for external causes and at home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the carrier's liability when breakage is caused by external forces versus his own action, and identify the Hanafi positions on the home scenario and Zufar's view.

Core Idea
For breakage from external causes, Abu Hanifa says no liability (trust); Sahibayn say liability with wage; at home after delivery, no liability (later view of Muhammad).

Not all breakages during transport are the carrier's fault. When a crowd pushes him, the schools differ. Additionally, if the goods break after reaching the carrier's home, the ruling depends on whether the transport is deemed complete. This lesson navigates these additional layers of the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify external cause scenarios
Read the passage: 'If it was not by his action, such as people crowding him and it broke – he is not liable according to Abu Hanifa, but liable according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]'. Note the two positions.
External cause means not caused by the carrier's fault.
2
Understand the basis for the disagreement
Abu Hanifa views the goods as an amanah (trust) when no fault; the Sahibayn consider the carrier as an ajir mushtarak who guarantees against any damage during the work.
This is a usul difference on the nature of the contract.
3
Analyze the home scenario
The passage says: 'If the jar broke after he reached his home, no liability and wage due – this is later view of Muhammad; Abu Yusuf and earlier Muhammad say liable.'
The location 'home' marks completion of the transport.
4
Consider Zufar's view
Zufar says no liability for non-intentional breakage, but intentional breakage triggers liability at the breakage place, even if owner accompanies.
This is a minority view within Hanafi.
5
Synthesize the ruling by scenario
Map each scenario (action, non-action, home, intentional by carrier) to the mufta bihi position and note the ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi uses the later view of Muhammad for home, and the Sahibayn view for external crowds? Actually the passage implies mufta bihi for external is the Sahibayn? It says 'according to the two, he is liable' and this might be the relied upon. But check.

ضمن الحمال قيمته في مكان حمله ولا أجر له، أو في موضع انكسر، وأجره بحسابه. ابتداء الحمل حصل بأمره، فلم يكن تعديا من الابتداء، وإنما صار تعديا عند الكسر، فيميل إلى أي الجهتين شاء، فإن مال إلى الوجه الأول، ضمنه قيمته عند ابتداء الحمل ولا أجر له، وإن مال إلى الوجه الثاني، ضمنه قيمته عند الكسر، وأعطاه أجره بحسابه هذا إذا كان الكسر بصنعه بأن زلق أو عثر، وإن كان من غير صنعه بأن زحمه الناس، فانكسر لا يضمن عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن المتاع أمانة عنده، وعندهما يضمن قيمته في موضع الكسر، فيعطيه أجره، ولو كان الحمال هو الذي زحم الناس حتى انكسر، فإنه يضمن بالإجماع، وقوله: "في الطريق" قال في "الذخيرة": هو قيد احترازي، فإذا انكسر الدن بعد ما انتهى به إلى بيته فله الأجر، ولا ضمان عليه، وهذا قول محمد آخرا، أما على قول أبي يوسف وهو قول محمد أولا يجب أن يكون ضامنا. ملخص من ملا مسكين والفتح والعيني والتكملة بقدر الحاجة ضمن الحمال إلخ هذا عندنا، وقال زفر إن انكسر لا يضمن وإن كسره عمدا يضمن قيمته في المكان الذي كسره أطلقه، فعم ما لو كان صاحب الدن معه، وبه صرح في البزازية حيث قال: حمل متاعا وصاحبه معه، فعثر وسقط المتاع، ففسد ضمن.
The carrier is liable for its value at the place of his carrying and he has no wage, or at the place of breakage, and his wage is proportionate. The beginning of carrying occurred by his command, so there was no transgression from the beginning, but it became transgression at the time of breakage, so he inclines to whichever of the two aspects he wishes. If he inclines to the first aspect, he is liable for its value at the beginning of carrying and he has no wage; if he inclines to the second aspect, he is liable for its value at the time of breakage and he receives his wage proportionately. This is when the breakage was by his action, such as slipping or stumbling. If it was not by his action, such as people crowding him and it broke, he is not liable according to Abu Hanifa because the goods are a trust with him. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], he is liable for its value at the place of breakage, and he receives his wage. And if the carrier himself crowded people until it broke, then he is liable by consensus. His statement 'in the road'; in al-Dhakhira it is said it is a restrictive qualification. If the jar broke after he reached his home, he has his wage and no liability on him. This is the later view of Muhammad. As for the view of Abu Yusuf, which is the earlier view of Muhammad, he must be liable. Summary from Mulla Miskin, al-Fath, al-Ayni, and al-Takmila as needed: 'the carrier is liable etc.' This is with us. Zufar said: If it breaks, he is not liable, but if he breaks it intentionally, he is liable for its value at the place where he broke it, unconditionally, so it includes even if the owner of the jar was with him. This is clearly stated in al-Bazzaziyya: 'He carried goods and his owner was with him, then he stumbled and the goods fell and spoiled, so he is liable.'
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the liability of a carrier (hammal). It begins by stating the matn: the carrier is liable for the value of the goods at the location where he carried them (meaning the place of initial contract) if he breaks them and does not receive wage; or if the breakage occurs at a different location, he is liable at that location and receives wage proportionately. The commentary then explains that the carriage began with the owner's permission, so initially there is no transgression. Transgression only occurs at the moment of breakage. The carrier thus has two scenarios: if he chooses the first scenario (liable at initial place, no wage), he must pay full value at the start and forfeits wage; if he chooses the second (liable at breakage place, with wage), he pays value where it broke and keeps proportionate wage. This applies when the breakage is due to his own action like slipping. If it happens due to external causes like crowds, Abu Hanifa holds no liability (the goods are a trust), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold liability at the breakage place with wage. If the carrier himself caused the crowd, he is liable by consensus. A key point is the location: if the jar breaks after reaching home, there is no liability and wage is due—this is Muhammad's later view; his earlier view and Abu Yusuf's view impose liability. Zufar holds no liability unless intentional. This analysis follows the Hanafi school's detailed reasoning.

Key Terms
أمانة (amanah): Trust; something held in trust, where the holder is not liable except for transgression.
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A worker hired to perform a specific task, not for a period; he guarantees the work until delivery.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the scholars; here, consensus on liability when carrier himself causes the crowd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is the ruling when goods are broken due to an external cause (e.g., crowd) during transport?
A) The carrier is not liable because the goods are a trust.
B) The carrier is liable for the value at the place of breakage and receives his wage.
C) The carrier is liable only if he was negligent.
D) The carrier forfeits his wage but is not liable for the value.

Key Takeaway
For breakage from external causes, the Hanafi mufta bihi (Sahibayn) holds the carrier liable with wage; after goods reach his home, the later view of Muhammad exempts him from liability.

Liability of the Cupper, Barber, and Phlebotomist
Ruling with proof on medical liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for non-liability (permission and non-exceeding the usual site) and explain the rational proof (qiyas to ta'zir) that supports the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
No liability if within usual site and with permission — the obligation of the contract negates liability.

Medical practitioners like cuppers, barbers, and phlebotomists perform invasive procedures that carry inherent risks. This passage clarifies when they are not liable for harm: if they act within the usual site and have permission, they are protected because the work is obligatory upon them through their contract. The reasoning uses an analogy to the governor's punishment, where no liability attaches for harm caused by an obligatory act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its conditions
The matn states that a cupper, barber, or phlebotomist is not liable if he does not exceed the usual site. The commentary expands this to require both permission and non-exceeding.
The conditions are cumulative: permission (idhn) and non-exceeding (adam al-tajawuz).
2
Locate the proof (qiyas)
The ruling is supported by an analogy to the ta'zir punishment administered by the governor. Just as the governor is not liable if someone dies from a lawful punishment, the practitioner is not liable for harm arising from an obligatory medical act.
The qiyas is based on the shared ‘illa: wujub (obligation) negates daman (liability).
3
Understand the expansion from two narrations
The commentary reconciles two texts: al-Mukhtasar mentions non-exceeding, al-Jami’ al-Saghir mentions permission. Together they establish both conditions as necessary.
Al-Kafi explains that each text supplements the other, so the mufta bihi requires both.
4
Distinguish from cloth-beating
Unlike beating cloth (where the strength is observable), the practitioner cannot know the internal condition of the patient (e.g., weak constitution). Therefore he is not required to guarantee the beneficial outcome.
This distinction shows why the practitioner is not liable for hidden conditions.
5
Apply the consequence of exceeding
If the practitioner exceeds the usual site, he is liable for half the blood money if the patient dies, because the harm is partly from the permitted act and partly from the unpermitted excess.
The liability is proportional: half diyah for half the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يضمن حجام أو بزاغ أو فصاد إن لم يعد الموضع المعتاد، لأنه التزمه بالعقد، فوجب عليه، ولا ضمان مع الوجوب كما لو مات من عزّره الحاكم، وليس في وسعه الاحتراز عن مثله؛ لأنه لا يمكنه الفصد ونحوه محترزا عن سبب الهلاك؛ لغموض باطن أحوال الحيوان، فربما يكون ضعيف المزاج لا يندمل جرحه سريعا، وقد يسري إلى النفس، وقد يكون بالعكس، ولا إطلاع للفصاد ونحوه على قوة الطبيعة وضعفها، فلا يقيد بالمصلح من العمل، بخلاف دق الثوب؛ لأن قوته ورقته تعرف بالحس والمشاهدة، فيكون مقيدا بالمصلح، وإن تعدى عن المعتاد يضمن نصف دية النفس إن هلكت؛ لأنها تلفت بمأذون فيه، وبغير مأذون فيه، فيضمن بحسابه، وهو النصف. أو بزاغ في المغرب : بزغ البيطار الدابة إذا شقها بالمبزع وهو مثل مشرط الحجام. إن لم يعد إلخ: من عدا يعدو أي لم يتجاوز ظاهر عبارة المصنف يقتضي أن الضمان ينتفي بعدم مجاوزة الموضع المعتاد ولا يشترط لانتفاء الضمان إلا الإذن مع عدم المجاوزة، وفي "الجامع الصغير": وحجامة العبد بأمر المولى حتى إذا لم يكن بأمر المولى يجب الضمان ، قال في "الكافي": عبارة "المختصر" ناطقة بعدم التجاوز، ساكتة عن الإذن، وعبارة "الجامع الصغير" ناطقة بالإذن ساكتة عن التجاوز، فصار ما نطق به هذا بيانا لما سكت عنه الآخر، ويستفاد بمجموع الروايتين اشتراط الإذن وعدم التجاوز ؛ لعدم وجوب الضمان حتى إذا عدم أحدهما أو كلاهما يجب الضمان. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٥٩/٨
And a cupper, a barber, or a phlebotomist is not liable if he does not exceed the usual site, because he undertook it by contract, so it became obligatory upon him, and there is no liability with obligation just as if someone dies from the governor's punishment. And it is not within his power to guard against such, because he cannot perform phlebotomy or the like while protecting against the cause of destruction due to the obscurity of the inner conditions of the animal. So perhaps he is weak in constitution and his wound does not heal quickly, and it may spread to the soul, and sometimes the opposite. And the phlebotomist and such have no knowledge of the strength or weakness of the nature, so he is not restricted to the beneficial part of the work, unlike beating cloth, because its strength and delicacy are known by sense and observation, so he is restricted to the beneficial. And if he exceeds the usual, he is liable for half the blood money of the soul if it perishes, because it is destroyed by what is permitted and by what is not permitted, so he is liable proportionately, which is half. 'Or bazzagh' in the Maghrib: the veterinary bazzagh pierces the animal with a lancet like a cupper's scalpel. 'If he does not exceed etc.': from 'ada ya'du i.e. does not exceed. The apparent wording of the author implies that liability is negated by not exceeding the usual site, and only permission with non-exceeding is required for negation of liability. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: cupping of a slave by the master's order until if not by the master's order, liability is required. Al-Kafi said: the wording of al-Mukhtasar speaks of non-exceeding, silent about permission; the wording of al-Jami' al-Saghir speaks of permission, silent about non-exceeding. So what one states explains what the other omits. From the two narrations together, it is understood that both permission and non-exceeding are conditions; because liability is not obligatory unless one or both are absent. Completion of al-Bahr al-Raiq: 59/8.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the liability of a cupper (hajjam), barber (bazzagh), and phlebotomist (fassad). The matn states they are not liable if they do not exceed the usual site. The commentary explains that they undertook the work by contract, making it obligatory; there is no liability for something obligatory by analogy to the governor's punishment. Since internal conditions are hidden, they cannot guarantee safety, unlike cloth beating where strength is observable. If they exceed the usual site and harm occurs, they are liable for half the blood money (diyah) because part was permitted, part was not. The commentary also clarifies that both permission and non-exceeding are necessary conditions for non-liability, drawing from two different texts: al-Mukhtasar mentions non-exceeding, al-Jami' al-Saghir mentions permission. Both conditions must be met.

Key Terms
حجام (hajjam): A cupper who performs hijama (cupping therapy).
بزاغ (bazzagh): A barber or veterinarian who performs minor surgery; in Maghribi usage, a veterinary bazzagh pierces animals.
فصاد (fassad): A phlebotomist who performs bloodletting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a cupper accidentally causes the death of a patient while performing cupping at the usual site with permission, what is the ruling?
A) The cupper is liable for full blood money.
B) The cupper is liable for half blood money.
C) The cupper is not liable.
D) The cupper is liable for a fixed compensation.

Key Takeaway
The cupper, barber, and phlebotomist are not liable for harm if they have permission and do not exceed the usual site, because the obligation of the contract negates liability.
