The Private Worker (Ajir Khas): Definition, Conditions, and Core Rulings
Definition and rulings of ajir khas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the ajir khas, identify the two conditions that make a worker private, and apply the rules of wage entitlement and non-liability.

Core Idea
A private worker earns wage by availability, not work, and is blameless for accidental loss.

The private worker (ajir khas) is one of the two main types of hired workers in the Hanafi school. His contract is on his benefits for a specified period or distance, and his rulings differ markedly from the common worker (ajir mushtarak). This lesson unpacks the definition, the two conditions for private status, the logic of wage entitlement, and the rule of non-liability — all based on the consensus cited in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of workers
Recognize that the private worker (ajir khas) is distinct from the common worker (ajir mushtarak). The private worker's contract is on his benefits for a period or distance.
2
Apply the conditions for private status
A hired worker becomes private only if the hirer mentions the period first or stipulates exclusivity. If both conditions are missing, the worker is common.
The passage gives detailed justifications for each condition.
3
Determine wage entitlement
The private worker is entitled to his wage by merely surrendering himself and being able to work, even if no actual work occurs. Exceptions exist for valid excuses (e.g., rain).
This is a key practical point: availability, not output, is the basis.
4
Apply the non-liability rule
The private worker is not liable for loss of the hirer's property in his hands unless he deliberately causes harm (e.g., hits an animal).
The analogy to a depositee (mudda') is used.
5
Recognize restrictions on working for others
A private worker cannot work for others during the contract period. If he does, his wage is reduced proportionally.
The example from al-Tatarkhaniyya illustrates this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخاص هذا بيان النوع الثاني من نوعي الأجير. واعلم أن الأجير الخاص هو الذي يكون عقده واردا على منافعه ولا تصير منافعه معلومة إلا بذكر المدة أو بذكر المسافة، يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه في المدة وإن لم يعمل كمن استوجر شهرا للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم، ولا يضمن ما تلف في يده أو عمله. ومنافعه في حكم العين، فإذا استحقت بعقد المعاوضة لا يتمكن من إيجارها لغيره، وقد يسمى الأجير الخاص أجير وحد؛ لأنه لا يمكن أن يعمل في تلك المدة لغيره. ويستحق الأجر الخ: يعني الأجير الخاص يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه إذا تمكن من العمل، وأما إذا سلّم نفسه ولم يتمكن منه لعذر المطر ونحوه لا أجر له. وإن لم يعمل: مع القدرة على العمل، وأما إذا لم يعمل بسبب عذر منعه عن العمل كالمطر وغيره لا يستحق الأجر. كمن استوجر إلخ هذا تفسير الأجير الخاص يعني إذا استوجر عبد شهرا للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم، فهو أجير خاص، وهذا المقام يقتضي بسطا وتفصيلا، فاعلم أن من استأجر عبدا للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم لا يكون أجيرا خاصا إلا بأحد الشرطين إما أن يقدم المستأجر ذكر المدة أولا ويقول: استأجرتك شهرا لترعى غنمي أو لتخدمني بدرهم مثلا، وإما أن يشترط عليه أن لا يرعي غنم غيره، ولا يخدم غيره، وإذا فات الشرطان، يكون أجيرا مشتركا لا أجيرا خاصا. وجه الأول: أنه لما ذكر المدة أولا أوقع الكلام على المدة، فتكون منافعه للمستأجر في تلك المدة، فيمتنع أن تكون لغيره فيها أيضا، وقوله بعد ذلك: "الرعي الغنم" يحتمل أن يكون لإيقاع العقد على العمل، فيصير أجيرا مشتركا؛ لأنه من يقع عقده على العمل، وأن يكون لبيان نوع العمل الواجب على الأجير الخاص في المدة، فإن الإجارة على المدة لا تصح في الأجير الخاص ما لم يبين نوع العمل بأن يقول: استأجرتك شهرا للخدمة أو للحصاد، فلا يتغير حكم الكلام الأول بالاحتمال، فيبقى أجيرا خاصا ما لم ينص على خلافه، بأن يقول: على أن ترعى غنم غيري مع غنمي، وهذا ظاهر. ووجه الثاني: أنه إذا أخر المدة بأن استأجره ليرعى غنما مسماة بأجر معلوم شهرا، فحينئذ يكون أجيرا مشتركا بأول الكلام؛ لإيقاع العقد على العمل في أوله، وقوله : "شهرا" في آخره يحتمل أن يكون لإيقاع العقد على المدة، فيصير أجيرا خاصا، ويحتمل أن يكون التقدير العمل الذي وقع العقد عليه، فلا يتغير أول كلامه بالاحتمال ما لم ينص على الخلاف، ويشترط عليه عدم رعي غنم غيره، وعدم خدمة غيره. ثم اعلم أنه ليس للأجير الخاص أن يعمل لغيره، ولو عمل لغيره نقص من أجرته بقدر ما عمل، قال في "التاتارخانية": نجار استوجر إلى الليل، فعمل لأخر دواة بدرهم وهو يعلم، فهو آثم، وإن لم يعلم فلا شيء عليه، وينقص من أجر النجار بقدر ما عمل في الدواة. للخدمة: أي لخدمة المستأجر وزوجته وأولاده. ولا يضمن إلخ يعني حكم الأجير الخاص أنه لا يضمن ما تلف في يده بأن ق منه أو غصب أو بعمله اتفاقا ولم يتعمد الفساد، فإن تعمد ذلك ضمن كالمودع إذا تعدى، ومن التعدي ما إذا ضرب الشاة ففقأ عينها أو كسر رجلها، فإنه يضمن وهذا الحكم أي عدم الضمان بالإجماع.
And 'al-khas' this is an explanation of the second type of the two types of worker. Know that the private worker (ajir khas) is the one whose contract is on his benefits, and his benefits become known only by mentioning the period or distance. He is entitled to wage by surrendering himself during the period even if he does not work, like one who hires out for a month for service or for sheep grazing, and he is not liable for what is lost in his hand or work. His benefits are considered like a commodity; when they become owed by a contract of exchange, he cannot lease them to another. Sometimes the private worker is called 'exclusive worker' because he cannot work for another during that period. The phrase 'and he is entitled to wage etc.' means: the private worker is entitled to wage by surrendering himself if he is able to work, but if he surrenders himself and cannot work due to an excuse like rain, he has no wage. 'Even if he does not work': with ability to work, but if he does not work due to an excuse preventing him from work like rain, he does not deserve wage. 'Like one who hires out etc.' this is an interpretation of the private worker: i.e., if someone hires a slave for a month for service or for sheep grazing, he is a private worker. This context requires expansion and detail. Know that if someone hires a slave for service or for sheep grazing, he does not become a private worker except with one of two conditions: either the hirer mentions the period first and says 'I hire you for a month to graze my sheep or to serve me for a dirham etc.', or he stipulates that he not graze sheep of others nor serve others. If both conditions are missing, he is a common worker (ajir mushtarak), not a private worker. The justification for the first: since he mentioned the period first, the speech is placed on the period, so his benefits belong to the hirer in that period, and they cannot be for others also. His later saying 'grazing sheep' could be for effecting the contract on the work, making him a common worker because his contract is on the work, or it could be for specifying the type of work obligatory on the private worker in the period. Indeed, hiring for a period is not valid for a private worker unless he specifies the type of work by saying 'I hire you for a month for service or for harvesting', so the ruling of the first speech does not change by possibility, so he remains a private worker unless he specifies otherwise, such as saying 'on condition that you also graze others' sheep with mine.' This is apparent. The justification for the second: if he delays the period by hiring him to graze specified sheep for a known wage for a month, then he becomes a common worker by the first part of the speech because the contract is on the work at its beginning. His saying 'a month' at the end could be for effecting the contract on the period, making him a private worker, or it could be considered as the work on which the contract was made. So his first speech does not change by possibility unless he specifies otherwise, and he stipulates that he not graze others' sheep or serve others. Then know that the private worker may not work for others; if he works for others, his wage is reduced by the amount of that work. Al-Tatarkhaniyya says: A carpenter is hired until night, and he works for another on a pen for a dirham while knowing, he is sinful; if he did not know, there is nothing on him. And the carpenter's wage is reduced by the amount of his work on the pen. 'For service': i.e., for service of the hirer, his wife, and his children. 'And does not guarantee etc.' means the ruling of the private worker is that he does not guarantee what is lost in his hand, whether by theft, usurpation, or by his work by agreement, unless he deliberately corrupts. If he deliberately does so, he guarantees like a depositee when he transgresses. Examples of transgression: if he hits a sheep and gouges its eye or breaks its leg, he guarantees. This ruling of non-liability is by consensus.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the private worker (ajir khas), the second type of hired worker. It opens by stating that the private worker's contract is on his benefits, and these benefits are known only by specifying a period or distance. He becomes entitled to his wage merely by offering himself for work during the period, even if no actual work occurs (provided he is able). He is not liable for loss of the employer's property in his hands unless he deliberately causes harm. The commentary then expands on the conditions that make a worker private rather than common: either the hirer mentions the period first, or he stipulates exclusivity. Examples clarify the difference. If both conditions are absent, the worker is a common worker (ajir mushtarak). The passage also discusses scenarios where the worker does not work due to an excuse—then he does not get wage. It further notes that a private worker cannot work for others; if he does, his wage is reduced accordingly, and he may be sinful if he knowingly does so. Finally, it reiterates non-liability for accidental loss, with deliberate harm triggering liability akin to a depositee's transgression. This ruling is by consensus within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A private worker whose contract is on his benefits for a specified period or distance; he is entitled to wage by making himself available.
مدة (mudda): The period or duration specified in the contract; a key element in defining the private worker.
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common worker whose contract is on a specific work, not on his time; he can work for multiple hirers simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for a hired worker to be considered an ajir khas (private worker)?
A) The hirer mentions the period first, or stipulates exclusivity.
B) The worker is paid daily.
C) The work is specified and measurable.
D) The contract is written.

Key Takeaway
An ajir khas is defined by period-based or exclusive contract; his wage is earned by availability, not output, and he is not liable for accidental loss.

Wage Entitlement and Non-Liability of the Special Employee
Ruling statement on wage entitlement and non-liability of the special employee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a special employee (ajir khas) becomes entitled to wages by making himself available, and distinguish when he is not liable for loss.

Core Idea
The special employee earns wages by availability, not work, and is not liable for accidental damage.

This lesson focuses on the core rulings for a special employee. You will learn that simply presenting yourself for work during the hire period entitles you to full wages, provided you are able. You will also see that the employee is not responsible for accidental damage unless he intentionally caused it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an ijarah contract with a special employee (ajir khas). The ruling is that the employee becomes entitled to wages by surrendering himself (taslim nafs) during the period.
This is a ruling statement: the entitlement is by availability, not actual work.
2
Determine the condition for entitlement
The entitlement requires ability to work (tamakkun min al-‘amal). If the employee is prevented by an excuse like rain, he does not deserve wages.
The condition is that the employee is able to work, even if he does nothing.
3
State the liability rule
The special employee is not liable for what is destroyed in his hand or by his work, provided he did not intentionally cause harm (ta‘addi). This is by consensus.
Non-liability covers loss, usurpation, or accidental damage.
4
Note the exception for intentional harm
If the employee intentionally causes damage, he becomes liable, similar to a depositary who transgresses.
Example: striking a sheep and blinding it makes the employee liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
ضمان الأجير
يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه في المدة وإن لم يعمل كمن استوجر شهرا للخدمة أو للعمل أي مدة الإجارة لرعي الغنم، ولا يضمن ما تلف في يده أو عمله. بدرهم مثلا ومنافعه في حكم العين، فإذا استحقت بعقد المعاوضة لا يتمكن من إيجارها لغيره، وقد يسمى الأجير الخاص أجير وحد؛ لأنه لا يمكن أن يعمل في تلك المدة لغيره. (فتح بتغيير) ويستحق الأجر الخ: يعني الأجير الخاص يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه إذا تمكن من العمل، وأما إذا سلّم نفسه ولم يتمكن منه لعذر المطر ونحوه لا أجر له تكملة البحر الرائق: ٥٩/٨] وإن لم يعمل: مع القدرة على العمل، وأما إذا لم يعمل بسبب عذر منعه عن العمل كالمطر وغيره لا يستحق الأجر. كمن استوجر إلخ هذا تفسير الأجير الخاص يعني إذا استوجر عبد شهرا للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم، فهو أجير خاص، وهذا المقام يقتضي بسطا وتفصيلا، فاعلم أن من استأجر عبدا للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم لا يكون أجيرا خاصا إلا بأحد الشرطين إما أن يقدم المستأجر ذكر المدة أولا ويقول: استأجرتك شهرا لترعى غنمي أو لتخدمني بدرهم مثلا، وإما أن يشترط عليه أن لا يرعي غنم غيره، ولا يخدم غيره، وإذا فات الشرطان، يكون أجيرا مشتركا لا أجيرا خاصا. وجه الأول: أنه لما ذكر المدة أولا أوقع الكلام على المدة، فتكون منافعه للمستأجر في تلك المدة، فيمتنع أن تكون لغيره فيها أيضا، وقوله بعد ذلك: "الرعي الغنم يحتمل أن يكون لإيقاع العقد على العمل، فيصير أجيرا مشتركا؛ لأنه من يقع عقده على العمل، وأن يكون لبيان نوع العمل الواجب على الأجير الخاص في المدة، فإن الإجارة على المدة لا تصح في الأجير الخاص ما لم يبين نوع العمل بأن يقول: استأجرتك شهرا للخدمة أو للحصاد، فلا يتغير حكم الكلام الأول بالاحتمال، فيبقى أجيرا خاصا ما لم ينص على خلافه، بأن يقول: على أن ترعى غنم غيري مع غنمي، وهذا ظاهر. ووجه الثاني: أنه إذا أخر المدة بأن استأجره ليرعى غنما مسماة بأجر معلوم شهرا، فحينئذ يكون أجيرا مشتركا بأول الكلام؛ لإيقاع العقد على العمل في أوله، وقوله : "شهرا" في آخره يحتمل أن يكون لإيقاع العقد على المدة، فيصير أجيرا خاصا، ويحتمل أن يكون التقدير العمل الذي وقع العقد عليه، فلا يتغير أول كلامه بالاحتمال ما لم ينص على الخلاف، ويشترط عليه عدم رعي غنم غيره، وعدم خدمة غيره. ثم اعلم أنه ليس للأجير الخاص أن يعمل لغيره، ولو عمل لغيره نقص من أجرته بقدر ما عمل، قال في "التاتارخانية": نجار استوجر إلى الليل، فعمل لأخر دواة بدرهم وهو يعلم، فهو آثم، وإن لم يعلم فلا شيء عليه، وينقص من أجر النجار بقدر ما عمل في الدواة. (رد المحتار بتوضيح وتغيير من المحشي) للخدمة: أي لخدمة المستأجر وزوجته وأولاده. (رد المحتار) ولا يضمن إلخ يعني حكم الأجير الخاص أنه لا يضمن ما تلف في يده بأن ق منه أو غصب أو بعمله اتفاقا ولم يتعمد الفساد، فإن تعمد ذلك ضمن كالمودع إذا تعدى، ومن التعدي ما إذا ضرب الشاة ففقأ عينها أو كسر رجلها، فإنه يضمن وهذا الحكم أي عدم الضمان بالإجماع؛
Book of Ijarah. Liability of the employee. He deserves the wage by surrendering himself during the period even if he does not work, like one who hires for a month for service or for work, i.e., the duration of the ijarah for grazing sheep, and he is not liable for what is destroyed in his hand or his work. For example, by a dirham. And his benefits are in the ruling of a thing (ayn), so if they are taken by a compensatory contract, he cannot rent them to others. And the special employee is sometimes called 'individual employee' because he cannot work for others during that period. (Fath, with modification) 'And he deserves the wage, etc.': meaning the special employee deserves the wage by surrendering himself if he is able to work. But if he surrenders himself and is not able due to an excuse like rain, etc., he has no wage. (Completion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 8/59) 'Even if he does not work': with ability to work. But if he does not work due to an excuse preventing work like rain, etc., he does not deserve the wage. 'Like one who hires, etc.': This is an interpretation of the special employee. Meaning if one hires a slave for a month for service or for grazing sheep, he is a special employee. This context requires elaboration and detail. Know that whoever hires a slave for service or grazing sheep is not a special employee except with one of two conditions: either the lessor mentions the period first and says, 'I hired you for a month to graze my sheep or to serve me, for example with a dirham,' or he stipulates that he should not graze others' sheep nor serve others. If both conditions are missing, he is a common employee, not a special employee. The reasoning for the first: when he mentioned the period first, he placed the speech on the period, so his benefits belong to the lessor during that period, and they are prevented from being for others in that period. His subsequent statement 'grazing sheep' may be for concluding the contract on work, making him a common employee because the contract is on work, or it may be to specify the type of work obligatory on the special employee during the period. Indeed, ijarah for a period is not valid for the special employee unless the type of work is specified, e.g., he says 'I hired you for a month for service or for harvesting.' So the ruling of the first speech does not change due to probability, so he remains a special employee unless he stipulates otherwise, like saying 'on condition that you graze others' sheep along with mine.' This is apparent. The reasoning for the second: if he postpones the period, e.g., hires him to graze named sheep for a known wage for a month, then he is a common employee from the beginning of the speech due to concluding the contract on work at its start. His word 'month' at the end may be for concluding the contract on period, making him a special employee, or it may be the work on which the contract was concluded. So the beginning of his speech does not change due to probability unless he stipulates otherwise and requires that he does not graze others' sheep nor serve others. Then know that it is not permissible for the special employee to work for others. If he works for others, his wage is reduced by the amount of his work. It is stated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: a carpenter hired until night, if he worked for another making an inkwell for a dirham knowingly, he is sinful; if he did not know, there is no sin on him, and the carpenter's wage is reduced by the amount he worked on the inkwell. (Radd al-Muhtar, with clarification and modification from the annotator) 'For service': i.e., for the service of the lessor, his wife and children. (Radd al-Muhtar) 'And he is not liable, etc.': meaning the ruling of the special employee is that he is not liable for what is destroyed in his hand, whether by loss, usurpation, or by his work, by agreement if he did not intentionally cause corruption. If he intentionally does that, he is liable, like a depositary (mudi') if he transgresses. And from transgression is if he struck the sheep and blinded its eye or broke its leg, then he is liable. This ruling, i.e., no liability, is by consensus (ijma).
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Ijarah explains the rulings concerning the 'special employee' (ajir khas). A special employee is hired for a specific period (e.g., a month) for a particular type of work or service, such that his benefit (manfa'ah) is exclusively for the lessor during that period. The key ruling is that the special employee becomes entitled to his wage merely by making himself available for work (taslim nafs) for the entire period, even if he does not actually perform the work, provided he is able to do so. However, if he is prevented by an excuse like rain, he does not earn the wage. Conversely, the employee is not liable for accidental damage to property in his custody unless he intentionally caused harm (ta'addi). This non-liability is established by consensus (ijma) among the Hanafi scholars. The passage also distinguishes a special employee from a common employee (ajir mushtarak). The distinguishing factor is whether the contract focuses on the period (making the employee special) or on the specific work (making him common). The text clarifies that to be a special employee, either the period must be mentioned first in the contract, or a condition prohibiting work for others must be stipulated. If both are absent, the employee is common. Additionally, if a special employee works for others during the contract period, his wage is reduced proportionally, and he may be sinful if done knowingly. The example of a carpenter hired until night who makes an inkwell for another illustrates this reduction.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): An employee hired for a specific period (e.g., a month) such that his benefit (manfa'ah) is exclusively for the lessor during that period; he cannot work for others unless stipulated otherwise.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or guarantee; here specifically, the responsibility of the employee for damage or loss of the hired property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for a special employee (ajir khas) to become entitled to wages?
A) He must complete the assigned work.
B) He must present himself and be able to work.
C) He must work for at least half the period.
D) He must not have any other employment.

Key Takeaway
A special employee earns his wage by being available and able; he is not liable for accidental loss unless he intentionally causes harm.

Conditions for Being a Special Employee and Consequences of Working for Others
Expansion of the definition of special employee: conditions and consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions that make an employee special (ajir khas) and apply the rule that if a special employee works for others, his wage is reduced proportionally.

Core Idea
An employee is special only if the period is mentioned first or exclusivity is stipulated; working for others reduces his wage.

This lesson clarifies how to distinguish between a special employee (ajir khas) and a common employee (ajir mushtarak) based on contract wording. You will learn the two conditions for being special, and what happens if a special employee works for others during the contract period.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two conditions for being a special employee
A hired person is a special employee only if one of two conditions is met: (1) the lessor mentions the period first in the contract, or (2) the lessor stipulates that the employee cannot work for others.
If neither condition is present, the employee is common (ajir mushtarak).
2
Analyze the effect of mentioning period first vs. work first
When the period is mentioned first, the contract focuses on the period, making the employee special. When the work is mentioned first, the contract focuses on the work, making the employee common, unless a later stipulation changes it.
The passage provides reasoning: probability does not change the initial focus.
3
Apply the ruling on working for others
If a special employee works for another person during the contract period, his wage is reduced by the proportion of time or work he spent on that other work. He may also be sinful if he knew it was prohibited.
Example from al-Tatarkhaniyyah: a carpenter hired until night who makes an inkwell for another gets his wage reduced.

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Ijarah explains the rulings concerning the 'special employee' (ajir khas). A special employee is hired for a specific period (e.g., a month) for a particular type of work or service, such that his benefit (manfa'ah) is exclusively for the lessor during that period. The key ruling is that the special employee becomes entitled to his wage merely by making himself available for work (taslim nafs) for the entire period, even if he does not actually perform the work, provided he is able to do so. However, if he is prevented by an excuse like rain, he does not earn the wage. Conversely, the employee is not liable for accidental damage to property in his custody unless he intentionally caused harm (ta'addi). This non-liability is established by consensus (ijma) among the Hanafi scholars. The passage also distinguishes a special employee from a common employee (ajir mushtarak). The distinguishing factor is whether the contract focuses on the period (making the employee special) or on the specific work (making him common). The text clarifies that to be a special employee, either the period must be mentioned first in the contract, or a condition prohibiting work for others must be stipulated. If both are absent, the employee is common. Additionally, if a special employee works for others during the contract period, his wage is reduced proportionally, and he may be sinful if done knowingly. The example of a carpenter hired until night who makes an inkwell for another illustrates this reduction.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): An employee hired for a specific period (e.g., a month) such that his benefit (manfa'ah) is exclusively for the lessor during that period; he cannot work for others unless stipulated otherwise.
أجير مشترك (ajīr mushtarak): An employee hired for a specific work (e.g., grazing a named flock) whose benefit is not exclusive; he may work for others simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what happens if a special employee (ajir khas) works for another person during the contract period?

Key Takeaway
A special employee is defined by period-first or exclusivity stipulation; violating exclusivity reduces his wage and may incur sin.

Permissibility of Conditional Wages in Ijarah (Tardid al-Ajr)
Explains the ruling on making wages conditional on different types or times of work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits conditional wages (tardid al-ajr) in ijarah without requiring khiyar, and distinguish this from the ruling in sale.

Core Idea
Conditional wages in ijarah are valid without option because the wage is due only upon work, resolving ambiguity.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on making wages conditional on different types or times of work (tardid al-ajr). The passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq contrasts the ijarah ruling with sale, where an option (khiyar) is required. You will explore the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and the intra-school disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: tardid al-ajr is valid (sahih) for up to three options without requiring khiyar.
The ruling applies to both type and time-based work alternatives.
2
Identify the opposing view
Zufar and some others hold that such contracts are invalid due to ambiguity (jahalah) at the time of contract.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab dispute.
3
Follow the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof: analogy to sale (where tardid is allowed for up to three with khiyar), but with a key difference – in ijarah, the wage is due only upon work, so khiyar is unnecessary. Need (hajah) is fulfilled by three types (good, medium, poor).
The text explicitly compares to sale to show similarity and difference.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response to Zufar: the two works are known and specified; the ambiguity is resolved by performance. The contract is valid because the work is among known alternatives.
Each alternative is individually known, so the contract does not have fundamental jahalah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis permit such contracts and enforce the agreed wage upon performance; Zufar would consider them void.
The mufta bihi is the position of the three masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

باب الأجرة على أحد الشرطين الأجرة على أحد الشرطين وصح ترديد الأجر بترديد العمل في الثوب نوعا وزمانا في الأول.. أي بسبب من حيث النوع من حيث الزمان لأن المستأجر لما ملك منافعه وأمره بالتصرف في ملكه كان كفعله بنفسه وهذا عند أبي حنيفة حاله ظاهر، وكذا عندهما؛ لأن تضمينهما الأجير المشترك كان استحسانا؛ لصيانة أموال الناس والأجير الخاص يعمل في بيت المستأجر، ولا يتقبل الأعمال، فتكون السلامة أغلب فأخذا فيه بالقياس. (فتح، بتوضيح وتغيير) باب الأجرة: أقول: لم يقع هذا اللفظ في أكثر نسخ "الكنز" ولا أخذه العيني في شرحه، ولا ملا مسكين ولا صاحب "التكملة"، وإنما هو في النسخة الأحمدية، وقد وقع في "الهداية"، لكنه فيه مكان الأجرة لفظ الإجارة ومحصلهما واحد هذا باب يبين فيه أحكام الأجرة على أحد الشرطين. على أحد الشرطين لما فرغ عن ذكر الإجارة على شرط واحد ذكر في هذا الباب الإجارة على أحد الشرطين؛ لأن الواحد قبل الاثنين. صح ترديد الأجر : أي صح للمستأجر أن يردد الأجرة للأجير بين عملين بأن يقول له: إن عملت كذا فلك كذا، وإن عملت كذا فلك كذا، وسيأتي تشريحه. يعني بترديد العمل إلخ يعني يجوز للمستأجر أن يجعل الأجر مترددا بين أجرين، ويجعل العمل مترددا بين عملين كأن يقول: إن خطت الثوب فارسيا فبدرهم أو روميا فبدر همين، أو صبغته بعصفر فبدرهم أو بزعفران فبدرهمين. واعلم أن الترديد في الإجارة بين عملين أو ثلاثة جائز كالبيع يعني كما أن في البيع يجوز أن يقول: بعتك أحد الثوبين أو أحد الأثواب الثلاثة على أن تأخذ أيهما شئت، ولا يجوز في الزائد على الثلاثة، كذلك في الإجارة يجوز الترديد بين الاثنين والثلاثة لا في الزائد إلا أنه لابد في البيع من اشتراط الخيار، وفي الإجارة لا يشترط ذلك، والفرق: أن تحقق الجهالة في البيع لا يرتفع إلا بإثبات الخيار؛ لأنه يجب فيه الثمن بنفس العقد، فلابد من الخيار ليرتفع الجهالة، ولا كذلك الإجارة؛ لأن الأجر إنما يجب فيها بالعمل، وعند ذلك يصير المعقود عليه معلوما، فلا حاجة إلى إثبات الخيار، ووجه جواز الترديد في كلا العقدين هو دفع الحاجة وهي إنما تندفع بالثلاثة؛ لاشتمالها على الجيد والوسط والردي، فلا حاجة إلى الأربعة ملتقط مع توضيح من المحشي) نوعا وزمانا إلخ: اعلم أن ترديد العمل في الثوب إما أن يكون من حيث النوع بأن يقول: إن خطته فارسيا فبدرهم أو روميا فبدرهمين، وكذا إن صبغته بعصفر فبدرهم أو بزعفران فبدرهمين، أو يكون من حيث الزمان بأن يقول: إن خطته اليوم فبدرهم، وإن خطته غدا فبنصف درهم، فحكم الترديد من حيث النوع أنه يجوز بلا خلاف بين علمائنا الثلاثة حتى إذا عمل أي العملين في الخياطة الفارسية أو الرومية استحق ما سماه أجرا؛ لأنه سمي نوعين معلومين من العمل، وسمي لكل واحد منهما بدلا معلوما، فيجوز كما إذا خيره في البيع بين العبدين، وقال زفر والثلاثة لا يجوز؛ لجهالة المعقود عليه في الحال ولنا أنهما عملان مختلفان ببدلين مختلفين وكل واحد معلوم
Chapter on hire with one of two conditions. [Commentary:] The hire (ujrah) on one of two conditions. [Matn:] It is valid to make the wage conditional (tardid al-ajr) by making the work on the cloth conditional in type and time in the first... (i.e., because, from the perspective of type, from the perspective of time) because when the lessor owns his benefits and orders him to dispose in his property, it is like his own act. This is apparent in Abu Hanifa's view, and also according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); because they made the common employee liable by istihsan, to safeguard people's property, while the special employee works in the lessor's house and does not accept other work, so safety predominates, so they applied qiyas in his case. (Fath, with clarification and modification) Chapter on hire: I say: This wording is not found in most copies of al-Kanz, nor did al-Ayni take it in his commentary, nor Mulla Miskin, nor the author of al-Takmila. It is only in the Ahmadiyya edition. It occurs in al-Hidayah, but there instead of 'ujrah' it has 'ijarah', and their sum is the same. This chapter explains the rulings of hire on one of two conditions. 'On one of two conditions': When the author finished mentioning ijarah on a single condition, he mentioned in this chapter ijarah on one of two conditions, because the one precedes the two. (Matn:) 'It is valid to make the wage conditional': that is, it is valid for the lessor to make the wage for the employee conditional between two works, by saying to him: If you do this, you have such-and-such, and if you do that, you have such-and-such. Its explanation will come. (Commentary:) That is, by making the work conditional, etc. Means it is permissible for the lessor to make the wage conditional between two wages, and make the work conditional between two works, such as saying: If you sew the cloth in Persian style, one dirham, or Roman style, two dirhams, or if you dye it with safflower, one dirham, or with saffron, two dirhams. And know that making conditional (tardid) in ijarah between two or three works is permissible, like in sale; that is, just as in sale it is permissible to say: I sell you one of the two garments or one of the three garments, on condition that you take whichever you wish, and it is not permissible for more than three, similarly in ijarah, tardid between two or three is permissible, not for more, except that in sale it is necessary to stipulate option (khiyar), while in ijarah it is not required. The difference is that the removal of ambiguity (jahalah) in sale is only achieved by establishing khiyar, because the price (thaman) becomes due by the contract itself, so khiyar is needed to remove ambiguity. Not so in ijarah, because the wage is only due by work, and at that point the subject matter becomes known, so there is no need to establish khiyar. The justification for permissibility of tardid in both contracts is the fulfillment of need, and need is only fulfilled by three (options) because they include good, medium, and bad, so there is no need for four. (Multaqat with clarification from the annotator) 'In type and time, etc.': Know that tardid of work on cloth is either from the perspective of type, e.g., if you sew it in Persian style, one dirham, or Roman style, two dirhams; similarly if you dye it with safflower, one dirham, or with saffron, two dirhams; or from the perspective of time, e.g., if you sew it today, one dirham, and if you sew it tomorrow, half a dirham. The ruling of tardid from the perspective of type is that it is permissible without disagreement among our three scholars, so that if he does either of the two works (Persian or Roman tailoring), he deserves the wage he named, because he named two known types of work and named for each a known substitute, so it is permissible, just as if he gave him a choice in sale between two slaves. But Zufar and the three said it is not permissible, because of ambiguity in the subject matter at the time. Our response: they are two different works with two different substitutes, each known.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq introduces a chapter on 'hire with one of two conditions' (al-ujrah 'ala ahad al-shartayn). It discusses the permissibility of making the wage contingent on the type or timing of work, a practice called 'tardid al-ajr'. The ruling is that such conditional hiring is valid without any option (khiyar) requirement, unlike in sale. The reason is that in sale, the price becomes due immediately, so ambiguity (jahalah) must be removed by a stipulated option. In ijarah, the wage is due only upon performance, so by the time the wage is due, the work is known and ambiguity is resolved. The text further notes that tardid is permissible for up to three options (types of work or timeframes) because need is fulfilled by three (good, medium, poor). It distinguishes between tardid by type (e.g., Persian vs. Roman tailoring) and by time (e.g., today vs. tomorrow). The first is unanimously permissible among the three Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). However, Zufar and others object, arguing that the contract is ambiguous at its inception. The Hanafi response is that the alternative works are each known and specified, so the ambiguity is only apparent. The passage also clarifies that the same ruling applies to hiring a special employee (ajir khas) by noting that the lessor owns his benefits, and the employee is akin to the lessor himself in disposal.

Key Terms
ترديد الأجر (tardīd al-ajr): Making the wage conditional on different types or times of work; e.g., 'if you sew Persian, you get one dirham; if Roman, two dirhams'.
جهالة (jahālah): Ambiguity or uncertainty in the subject matter or price of a contract, which can render it invalid if excessive.
خيار (khiyār): Option; a contractual right to cancel the contract within a period, used to remove ambiguity in sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is khiyar (option) not required in ijarah with tardid (conditional wages), according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the wage is known from the start
B) Because the wage becomes due only upon work, so ambiguity is resolved by then
C) Because ijarah is not a binding contract
D) Because the employee must accept any wage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits conditional wages in ijarah for up to three options without khiyar, because the wage is due only upon work, resolving any initial ambiguity.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Variable Wage by Time in Garment Hire: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tardid al-ajr by time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on tardid al-ajr by time in garment hire, explain the reasoning (talil) of each, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
When the wage depends on which day the work is done, Abu Hanifa rules the second day's wage is only ajr al-mithl; the Sahibayn enforce the named wage.

In Hanafi fiqh, it is generally permissible to make the wage variable by specifying different wages for different types of work. However, when the variability is based on time (e.g., today vs. tomorrow), the ruling becomes contested. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and explains the practical consequence (thamarah) of each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute concerns a hire contract where the hirer says: 'If you tailor this garment today, you get 1 dirham; if tomorrow, you get 0.5 dirham.' The question is whether the contract is valid for both days, only the first, or neither.
This is called tardid al-ajr bi al-zaman (variable wage by time).
2
List the three positions
Abu Hanifa: valid for first day (named wage), invalid for second (ajr al-mithl capped at named wage). Sahibayn: valid for both days, each named wage due. Zufar: invalid for both days.
Muttafaq 'alayh: type-based tardid is valid; only time-based is disputed.
3
Trace the reasoning of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa argues that mentioning 'today' is for haste (ta'jil), not for limiting (ta'qit); mentioning 'tomorrow' is for easing (tarfih). Thus, two wages gather for tomorrow, causing ignorance, so the second session is invalid.
If 'today' were for limiting, combining time and work (khiyata) would invalidate the contract, which is not the case.
4
Trace the reasoning of the Sahibayn
They argue that 'today' is literal (haqiqa) and means limiting (ta'qit); the contract ends with the day. 'Tomorrow' is for addition (idafa), so no two namings in one day. Hence both days are valid.
They avoid the problem of two namings by separating the times.
5
Identify the thamarah and mufta bihi
Practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, if work is done tomorrow, the worker gets ajr al-mithl (capped at 0.5 dirham); under Sahibayn, he gets the named 0.5 dirham. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, as implied by the text 'fi al-awwal'.
Zufar's view is not adopted; the dispute is internal to the school.

صَحَّ تَرْدِيدُ الْأَجْرِ بِتَرْدِيدِ الْعَمَلِ فِي الثَّوْبِ نَوْعًا وَزَمَانًا فِي الْأَوَّلِ.. أَيْ بِسَبَبِ مِنْ حَيْثُ النَّوْعِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الزَّمَانِ لِأَنَّ الْمُسْتَأْجِرَ لَمَّا مَلَكَ مَنَافِعَهُ وَأَمَرَهُ بِالتَّصَرُّفِ فِي مِلْكِهِ كَانَ كَفِعْلِهِ بِنَفْسِهِ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ حَالُهُ ظَاهِرٌ، وَكَذَا عِنْدَهُمَا؛ لِأَنَّ تَضْمِينَهُمَا الْأَجِيرَ الْمُشْتَرَكَ كَانَ اسْتِحْسَانًا؛ لِصِيَانَةِ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ وَالْأَجِيرُ الْخَاصُّ يَعْمَلُ فِي بَيْتِ الْمُسْتَأْجِرِ، وَلَا يَتَقَبَّلُ الْأَعْمَالَ، فَتَكُونُ السَّلَامَةُ أَغْلَبَ فَأَخَذَا فِيهِ بِالْقِيَاسِ. (فَتْحٌ، بِتَوْضِيحٍ وَتَغْيِيرٍ) بَابُ الْأَجْرَةِ: أَقُولُ: لَمْ يَقَعْ هَذَا اللَّفْظُ فِي أَكْثَرِ نُسَخِ "الْكَنْزِ" وَلَا أَخَذَهُ الْعَيْنِيُّ فِي شَرْحِهِ، وَلَا مَلَّا مِسْكِينٍ وَلَا صَاحِبُ "التَّكْمِلَةِ"، وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ فِي النُّسْخَةِ الْأَحْمَدِيَّةِ، وَقَدْ وَقَعَ فِي "الْهِدَايَةِ"، لَكِنَّهُ فِيهِ مَكَانَ الْأَجْرَةِ لَفْظُ الْإِجَارَةِ وَمُحَصَّلُهُمَا وَاحِدٌ هَذَا بَابٌ يُبَيَّنُ فِيهِ أَحْكَامُ الْأَجْرَةِ عَلَى أَحَدِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ. عَلَى أَحَدِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ لَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ ذِكْرِ الْإِجَارَةِ عَلَى شَرْطٍ وَاحِدٍ ذَكَرَ فِي هَذَا الْبَابِ الْإِجَارَةَ عَلَى أَحَدِ الشَّرْطَيْنِ؛ لِأَنَّ الْوَاحِدَ قَبْلَ الِاثْنَيْنِ. صَحَّ تَرْدِيدُ الْأَجْرِ: أَيْ صَحَّ لِلْمُسْتَأْجِرِ أَنْ يُرَدِّدَ الْأَجْرَةَ لِلْأَجِيرِ بَيْنَ عَمَلَيْنِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ لَهُ: إِنْ عَمِلْتَ كَذَا فَلَكَ كَذَا، وَإِنْ عَمِلْتَ كَذَا فَلَكَ كَذَا، وَسَيَأْتِي تَشْرِيحُهُ. يَعْنِي بِتَرْدِيدِ الْعَمَلِ إِلَخْ يَعْنِي يَجُوزُ لِلْمُسْتَأْجِرِ أَنْ يَجْعَلَ الْأَجْرَ مُتَرَدِّدًا بَيْنَ أَجْرَيْنِ، وَيَجْعَلَ الْعَمَلَ مُتَرَدِّدًا بَيْنَ عَمَلَيْنِ كَأَنْ يَقُولَ: إِنْ خِطْتَ الثَّوْبَ فَارِسِيًّا فَبِدِرْهَمٍ أَوْ رُومِيًّا فَبِدِرْهَمَيْنِ، أَوْ صَبَغْتَهُ بِعُصْفُرٍ فَبِدِرْهَمٍ أَوْ بِزَعْفَرَانٍ فَبِدِرْهَمَيْنِ. وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ التَّرْدِيدَ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ بَيْنَ عَمَلَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثَةٍ جَائِزٌ كَالْبَيْعِ يَعْنِي كَمَا أَنَّ فِي الْبَيْعِ يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَقُولَ: بِعْتُكَ أَحَدَ الثَّوْبَيْنِ أَوْ أَحَدَ الْأَثْوَابِ الثَّلَاثَةِ عَلَى أَنْ تَأْخُذَ أَيَّهَا شِئْتَ، وَلَا يَجُوزُ فِي الزَّائِدِ عَلَى الثَّلَاثَةِ، كَذَلِكَ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ يَجُوزُ التَّرْدِيدُ بَيْنَ الِاثْنَيْنِ وَالثَّلَاثَةِ لَا فِي الزَّائِدِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ فِي الْبَيْعِ مِنَ اشْتِرَاطِ الْخِيَارِ، وَفِي الْإِجَارَةِ لَا يُشْتَرَطُ ذَلِكَ، وَالْفَرْقُ: أَنَّ تَحَقُّقَ الْجَهَالَةِ فِي الْبَيْعِ لَا يَرْتَفِعُ إِلَّا بِإِثْبَاتِ الْخِيَارِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ يَجِبُ فِيهِ الثَّمَنُ بِنَفْسِ الْعَقْدِ، فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْخِيَارِ لِيَرْتَفِعَ الْجَهَالَةُ، وَلَا كَذَلِكَ الْإِجَارَةُ؛ لِأَنَّ الْأَجْرَ إِنَّمَا يَجِبُ فِيهَا بِالْعَمَلِ، وَعِنْدَ ذَلِكَ يَصِيرُ الْمَعْقُودُ عَلَيْهِ مَعْلُومًا، فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى إِثْبَاتِ الْخِيَارِ، وَوَجْهُ جَوَازِ التَّرْدِيدِ فِي كِلَا الْعَقْدَيْنِ هُوَ دَفْعُ الْحَاجَةِ وَهِيَ إِنَّمَا تَنْدَفِعُ بِالثَّلَاثَةِ؛ لِاشْتِمَالِهَا عَلَى الْجَيِّدِ وَالْوَسَطِ وَالرَّدِيءِ، فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى الْأَرْبَعَةِ (مُلْتَقَطٌ مَعَ تَوْضِيحٍ مِنَ الْمُحَشِّي) نَوْعًا وَزَمَانًا إِلَخْ: اعْلَمْ أَنَّ تَرْدِيدَ الْعَمَلِ فِي الثَّوْبِ إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مِنْ حَيْثُ النَّوْعِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: إِنْ خِطْتَهُ فَارِسِيًّا فَبِدِرْهَمٍ أَوْ رُومِيًّا فَبِدِرْهَمَيْنِ، وَكَذَا إِنْ صَبَغْتَهُ بِعُصْفُرٍ فَبِدِرْهَمٍ أَوْ بِزَعْفَرَانٍ فَبِدِرْهَمَيْنِ، أَوْ يَكُونَ مِنْ حَيْثُ الزَّمَانِ بِأَنْ يَقُولَ: إِنْ خِطْتَهُ الْيَوْمَ فَبِدِرْهَمٍ، وَإِنْ خِطْتَهُ غَدًا فَبِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ، فَحُكْمُ التَّرْدِيدِ مِنْ حَيْثُ النَّوْعِ أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ بِلَا خِلَافٍ بَيْنَ عُلَمَائِنَا الثَّلَاثَةِ حَتَّى إِذَا عَمِلَ أَيَّ الْعَمَلَيْنِ فِي الْخِيَاطَةِ الْفَارِسِيَّةِ أَوِ الرُّومِيَّةِ اسْتَحَقَّ مَا سَمَّاهُ أَجْرًا؛ لِأَنَّهُ سَمَّى نَوْعَيْنِ مَعْلُومَيْنِ مِنَ الْعَمَلِ، وَسَمَّى لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَدَلًا مَعْلُومًا، فَيَجُوزُ كَمَا إِذَا خَيَّرَهُ فِي الْبَيْعِ بَيْنَ الْعَبْدَيْنِ، وَقَالَ زُفَرُ وَالثَّلَاثَةُ لَا يَجُوزُ؛ لِجَهَالَةِ الْمَعْقُودِ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْحَالِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُمَا عَمَلَانِ مُخْتَلِفَانِ بِبَدَلَيْنِ مُخْتَلِفَيْنِ وَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مَعْلُومٌ فَيَتَعَيَّنُ أَحَدُهُمَا بِاخْتِيَارِهِ، وَتَرْتَفِعُ الْجَهَالَةُ الْمُفْضِيَةُ لِلْمُنَازَعَةِ، وَحُكْمُ التَّرْدِيدِ فِي الثَّوْبِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الزَّمَانِ أَنَّهُ فِي الْأَوَّلِ أَيْ يَجِبُ مَا سُمِّيَ إِذَا وُجِدَ الْعَمَلُ فِي الْيَوْمِ الْأَوَّلِ مِنَ الْيَوْمَيْنِ الْمُتَرَدَّدِ فِيهِمَا دُونَ الثَّانِي، وَهَذَا مَعْنَى قَوْلِ الْمُصَنِّفِ: "وَزَمَانًا فِي الْأَوَّلِ" حَتَّى إِذَا خَاطَهُ الْيَوْمَ فَلَهُ دِرْهَمٌ فَإِنْ خَاطَهُ غَدًا فَلَهُ أَجْرُ مِثْلِهِ لَا يُجَاوَزُ بِهِ الْمُسَمَّى، وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِلَّهِ، وَقَالَا : يَصِحُّ فِي الْأَوَّلِ وَالثَّانِي حَتَّى إِذَا خَاطَهُ الْيَوْمَ فَلَهُ دِرْهَمٌ فَإِذَا خَاطَهُ غَدًا فَلَهُ نِصْفُ دِرْهَمٍ، وَقَالَ زُفَرُ وَالثَّلَاثَةُ لَا يَصِحُّ فِي الْأَوَّلِ وَلَا فِي الثَّانِي؛ لِأَنَّ الْخِيَاطَةَ شَيْءٌ وَاحِدٌ وَقَدْ ذُكِرَ بِمُقَابَلَتِهِ بَدَلَانِ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْبَدَلِيَّةِ، فَيَكُونُ مَجْهُولًا، وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ ذِكْرَ الْيَوْمِ فِي قَوْلِهِ: "إِنْ خِطْتَهُ الْيَوْمَ فَبِدِرْهَمٍ" لِلتَّعْجِيلِ لَا لِلتَّأْقِيتِ وَإِنْ كَانَ حَقِيقَةً فِيهِ، وَإِلَّا يَلْزَمُ اجْتِمَاعُ الْوَقْتِ وَالْعَمَلِ فِي الْإِجَارَةِ، وَهُوَ مُفْسِدٌ كَمَا مَرَّ . وَذِكْرُ الْغَدِ فِي قَوْلِهِ : "إِنْ خِطْتَهُ غَدًا فَبِنِصْفِ دِرْهَمٍ لِلتَّرْفِيهِ لَا لِلتَّعْلِيقِ وَلَا لِلْإِضَافَةِ فَإِذَا كَانَ ذِكْرُ الْيَوْمِ لِلتَّعْجِيلِ كَانَ الْأَجْرُ مُقَابِلًا بِنَفْسِ الْخِيَاطَةِ فِي الْيَوْمِ، وَكَذَا فِي الْغَدِ؛ لِأَنَّ ذِكْرَهُ لِلتَّرْفِيهِ، فَيَجْتَمِعُ فِي كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ أَجْرَانِ عَلَى الْبَدَلِ، وَهُوَ يُوجِبُ الْجَهَالَةَ وَلَهُمَا: أَنَّ ذِكْرَ الْيَوْمِ لِلتَّأْقِيتِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ حَقِيقَةٌ فَكَانَ قَوْلُهُ إِنْ خِطْتَهُ الْيَوْمَ فَبِدِرْهَمٍ يَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى الْيَوْمِ، فَبَانْقِضَاءِ الْيَوْمِ لَا يَبْقَى الْعَقْدُ إِلَى الْغَدِ، بَلْ يَنْقَضِي بِانْقِضَاءِ الْوَقْتِ وَذِكْرُ الْغَدِ لِلْإِضَافَةِ، وَإِذَا كَانَ لِلْإِضَافَةِ لَمْ يَكُنِ الْعَقْدُ ثَابِتًا فِي الْحَالِ، فَلَا يَجْتَمِعُ فِي كُلِّ يَوْمٍ تَسْمِيَتَانِ وَلَهُ أَنَّ ذِكْرَ الْغَدِ لِلْإِضَافَةِ، وَذِكْرَ الْيَوْمِ لِلتَّعْجِيلِ لَا يُمْكِنُ حَمْلُهُ عَلَى التَّأْقِيتِ الَّذِي هُوَ حَقِيقَةٌ، وَإِلَّا فَسَدَ الْعَقْدُ؛ لِاجْتِمَاعِ الْوَقْتِ وَالْعَمَلِ، وَإِذَا كَانَ كَذَلِكَ يَجْتَمِعُ فِي الْغَدِ تَسْمِيَتَانِ دُونَ الْيَوْمِ، فَيَصِحُّ فِي الْأَوَّلِ، وَيَجِبُ الْمُسَمَّى، وَيَفْسُدُ الثَّانِي، وَيَجِبُ أَجْرُ الْمِثْلِ لَا يُجَاوَزُ بِهِ نِصْفُ دِرْهَمٍ؛ لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْمُسَمَّى فِي الْيَوْمِ الثَّانِي.
It is valid to make the wage variable by making the work variable in the garment, in terms of type and time, regarding the first. That is, because of the reason, from the perspective of type, from the perspective of time. Because when the hirer owns the benefits and commands him to act in his property, it is as if he did it himself. This is apparent in the view of Abu Hanifa, and similarly in their view, because their holding the common hired worker liable was istihsan, to protect people's wealth. The private hired worker works in the hirer's house and does not accept multiple jobs, so safety is more prevalent, so they used qiyas in that. (Fath, with clarification and modification) Chapter of hire: I say: This wording does not occur in most copies of al-Kanz, nor did al-Ayni take it in his commentary, nor Mulla Miskin, nor the author of al-Takmila. Rather it is in the Ahmadi copy, and it occurs in al-Hidayah, but there the word al-ijarah is used instead of al-ajrah, and their meaning is the same. This is a chapter explaining the rulings of hire with one of two conditions. With one of two conditions: When he finished mentioning hire with one condition, he mentioned in this chapter hire with one of two conditions, because the one is before two. It is valid to make the wage variable: i.e., it is valid for the hirer to make the wage variable for the hired worker between two works, by saying to him: if you do this, you have such-and-such, and if you do that, you have such-and-such. Its dissection will come. He means: by making the work variable etc.: He means it is permissible for the hirer to make the wage variable between two wages, and make the work variable between two works, like if he says: if you tailor the garment Persian-style, then for one dirham, or Roman-style then for two dirhams, or if you dye it with safflower then for one dirham, or with saffron then for two dirhams. Know that making variable in hire between two works or three is permissible, like in sale. That is, just as it is permissible in sale to say: I sell you one of the two garments or one of the three garments, on condition that you take whichever you wish, and it is not permissible beyond three, similarly in hire it is permissible to make variable between two and three, not beyond. However, in sale it is necessary to stipulate the option, and in hire that is not stipulated. The difference is that the realization of ignorance in sale is not removed except by establishing the option, because the price becomes obligatory by the contract itself, so the option is needed to remove ignorance. Not so in hire, because the wage only becomes obligatory by the work, and at that point the object of contract becomes known, so there is no need to establish the option. The reason for permissibility of making variable in both contracts is to meet the need, and the need is only satisfied by three, because they include good, medium, and poor, so there is no need for four. (Compiled with clarification from the commentator) Type and time etc.: Know that making the work variable in the garment is either from the perspective of type, by saying: if you tailor it Persian-style then for one dirham, or Roman-style then for two dirhams; similarly if you dye it with safflower then for one dirham, or with saffron then for two dirhams; or from the perspective of time, by saying: if you tailor it today then for one dirham, and if you tailor it tomorrow then for half a dirham. The ruling of making variable from the perspective of type is that it is permissible without disagreement among our three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), so if he does either of the two works in Persian tailoring or Roman tailoring, he deserves what he named as wage, because he named two known types of work, and named for each of them a known compensation, so it is permissible, like when he gave him a choice in sale between two slaves. Zufar and the three (Zufar and the three later scholars?) said: it is not permissible due to ignorance of the object of contract at present. Our argument: they are two different works with two different compensations, each one known, so one becomes specified by his choice, and the ignorance leading to dispute is removed. The ruling of making variable in the garment from the perspective of time is that it is valid in the first, i.e., what is named becomes due if the work occurs in the first of the two days in which the variable occurs, not the second. This is the meaning of the author's statement: 'and time in the first'. So if he tailors it today, he gets one dirham; if he tailors it tomorrow, he gets its equivalent wage, not exceeding the named. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is valid in the first and second, so if he tailors it today he gets one dirham, and if he tailors it tomorrow he gets half a dirham. Zufar and the three said: it is not valid in the first nor the second, because tailoring is one thing, and two compensations have been mentioned corresponding to it as alternatives, so it becomes unknown. This is because mentioning today in his statement 'if you tailor it today, then for one dirham' is for haste, not for limit, although it is the literal meaning; otherwise, the combination of time and work in hire would be necessary, which is invalidating as previously. Mentioning tomorrow in his statement 'if you tailor it tomorrow then for half a dirham' is for easing, not for suspension nor for addition. So if mentioning today is for haste, the wage corresponds to the tailoring itself today, similarly tomorrow because its mention is for easing, so in each day two wages gather as alternatives, which necessitates ignorance. Their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) argument: mentioning today is for limiting because it is literal, so his statement 'if you tailor it today then for one dirham' is confined to today; so with the passing of today the contract does not remain until tomorrow, but it ends with the passing of the time. Mentioning tomorrow is for addition, and if it is for addition, the contract is not established at present, so no two namings gather in each day. Abu Hanifa's argument: mentioning tomorrow is for addition, and mentioning today cannot be interpreted as limiting, which is the literal meaning, because otherwise the contract would be invalidated due to combination of time and work. Since that is the case, two namings gather for tomorrow but not for today, so it is valid in the first, and the named is due, and the second is invalid, and the equivalent wage is due, not exceeding half a dirham, because that is the named for the second day.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the validity of making the wage variable by making the work variable in a garment contract. It begins by clarifying that the ruling applies to both type and time, but the author's reference 'in the first' indicates a qualification. The commentary explains that the hirer may stipulate different wages for different types of work (e.g., Persian vs. Roman tailoring) or different times (today vs. tomorrow). The text first establishes that making the wage variable in hire between two or three works is valid, analogous to sale, but with the difference that hire does not require an option to remove ignorance because the wage becomes determined only upon performance of work. For type-based variability, there is consensus among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad that it is valid; Zufar and later scholars object on grounds of initial ignorance, but the Hanafi response is that the two works are known and specified by choice. For time-based variability, there is a three-way dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the first day's work earns the named wage, while the second day's work earns the equivalent wage not exceeding the named amount; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold both days' work earn their respective named wages; Zufar holds neither is valid. The reasoning hinges on whether mentioning 'today' is for haste or limiting, and 'tomorrow' for easing or addition. Abu Hanifa's view is that the contract is valid for the first day (with named wage) but invalid for the second (so ajr al-mithl is due, capped at half dirham). This is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
تَرْدِيدُ الْأَجْرِ (tardīd al-ajr): Making the wage variable between two or more alternatives, determined by the worker's choice of work or time.
الْأَجِيرُ الْخَاصُّ (al-ajīr al-khāṣṣ): A private hired worker who works exclusively for one employer, usually at the employer's premises.
الْأَجِيرُ الْمُشْتَرَكُ (al-ajīr al-mushtarak): A common hired worker who works for multiple people, like a tailor in a shop.
التَّعْجِيلُ (al-ta'jil): Interpretation of a time reference as indicating haste rather than limiting the contract.
التَّأْقِيتُ (al-ta'qit): Interpretation of a time reference as limiting the contract to that specific time.
التَّرْفِيهُ (al-tarfih): Interpretation of a future time reference as easing the worker's burden, not suspending the contract.
أَجْرُ الْمِثْلِ (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent wage for similar work in the market, used when a contract is invalid but work has been done.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi view on tardid al-ajr by time, if a hirer says 'If you work today, $100; if tomorrow, $80' and the worker works tomorrow, what is the wage?
A) $80, as named for tomorrow.
B) $100, because the contract is valid for today's rate.
C) The equivalent market wage (ajr al-mithl), not exceeding $80.
D) Nothing, because the contract is void.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that tardid al-ajr by time is valid only for the first day; the second day's wage is ajr al-mithl, not exceeding the named amount.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Variable Wages in Hiring: The Hanafi Dispute on Tardid al-Ajr
Ruling and dispute on variable wages in hiring shops, houses, and beasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Hanifa's position on hiring with variable wages contingent on occupant or destination, and evaluate the Sahibayn's objection based on uncertainty.

Core Idea
A hiring contract with variable wage is valid if the minimum is certain and the extra depends on actual work.

This passage extends the ruling on variable wages from garment tailoring to hiring premises and beasts. The key issue is whether uncertainty (gharar) in the wage invalidates the contract. Abu Hanifa permits it by reasoning that the minimum wage is due immediately, while the increment is suspended on the work. The Sahibayn and Zufar consider the contract void due to unknown wages. Let us unpack the argument.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Identify the ruling: the contract is valid (sahih) and the lesser wage is due upon delivery; the extra depends on actual use (occupant type, destination, or load).
This applies to shops, houses, and beasts with conditions on distance or load.
2
Identify the Opposing View
State the Sahibayn's (and Zufar's) position: the contract is invalid because the object is one and the wages differ, creating uncertainty (jahl) about the due wage.
Their dalil is the general principle against gharar in contracts.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Abu Hanifa counter-argues that the contract is not for one fixed object; the work is variable by the lessee's choice. The minimum wage is certain, and the increase is contingent on the actual work, analogous to the tailoring case where wage is suspended on the type of stitching.
The commentator notes 'هذا أولى' (this is even more appropriate), strengthening the Hanafi view.
4
Apply to the Beast Cases
The same reasoning applies to hiring a beast with variable wage based on distance (Baghdad vs Kufa) or load (oil vs iron). Abu Hanifa holds validity; others disagree.
The analogy is direct: the minimum wage is due, the extra depends on actual distance or load.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, if the tenant uses the shop as a blacksmith, the higher wage is due; under Sahibayn, the contract would be invalid from the start, so no wage is due at all (or the contract must be reformed).
The mufta bihi (operative view) is Abu Hanifa's, as indicated by the commentator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الدكان والبيت والدابة مسافة وحملا. يصح. = عطف على " في الثوب" أي صح ترديد الأجر بترديد العمل في الدكان والبيت بأن قال: إن أسكنت هذا الدكان أو هذا البيت عطارا فبدرهم في الشهر ، وإن أسكنتها حدادا فبدرهمين، فالعقد جائز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يصح العقد؛ لأن المعقود عليه واحد والأجران مختلفان، ولا ندري أيهما يجب فلا يصح، وبه قال زفر والثلاثة، وله أن أقل الأجرتين يجب بتسليم المحل، والزيادة موقوفة على ظهور العمل، ولو كان الأجر موقوفا على ذلك أي ظهور العمل كما في مسألة الخياطة الرومية والفارسية جاز، فهذا أولى. رمز الحقائق: ٢٨٤/٢] والدابة مسافة وحملا إلخ [عطف على الدكان أي صح ترديد الأجر بترديد العمل في الدابة أيضا من حيث المسافة بأن قال: آجرتك هذه الدابة إلى بغداد بعشرين درهما، وإلى الكوفة بعشرة دراهم، ومن حيث الحمل بأن قال: آجرتكها على أنك إن حملت عليها قنطارا من زيت فبعشرة، وإن حملت عليها قنطارا من حديد فبمائة، فالعقد جائز فيهما عند أبي حنيفة، خلافا لهما ولزفر والثلاثة، والوجه ما مر. [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٨٤/٢] مسافة وحملا: متعلقان بقوله: "والدابة" أي صح ترديد الأجر بترديد العمل في الدابة من حيث المسافة والحمل.
And in the shop and house and beast, by distance and load. It is valid. It is a conjunction to 'in the garment', i.e., it is valid to make the wage variable by making the work variable in the shop and house, like if he said: If you house in this shop or this house a perfume seller, then one dirham per month, and if you house a blacksmith, then two dirhams. Then the contract is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the contract is not valid, because the object of contract is one and the two wages are different, and we do not know which one is due, so it is not valid. Zufar and the three said the same. Abu Hanifa's argument: the lesser of the two wages is due upon delivery of the premises, and the increase is suspended upon the appearance of the work. Had the wage been suspended upon that, i.e., the appearance of the work, as in the case of Roman and Persian tailoring, it would be permissible; this is even more appropriate. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/284] And the beast by distance and load etc. [It is a conjunction to the shop, i.e., it is valid to make the wage variable by making the work variable in the beast as well, from the perspective of distance, like if he said: I hire this beast to you to Baghdad for twenty dirhams, and to Kufa for ten dirhams; and from the perspective of load, like if he said: I hire it to you on condition that if you load on it a qintar of oil then for ten, and if you load on it a qintar of iron then for a hundred. Then the contract is permissible in both according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Zufar and the three. The reasoning is as before. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/284] Distance and load: they are related to his statement 'and the beast', i.e., it is valid to make the wage variable by making the work variable in the beast from the perspective of distance and load.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage extends the ruling on variable wages to hiring shops, houses, and beasts. It presents a case where the hirer stipulates different rents depending on the type of occupant (e.g., perfume seller vs. blacksmith) or the destination (Baghdad vs. Kufa) or the load (oil vs. iron). Abu Hanifa permits such contracts, reasoning that the minimum wage is due immediately upon delivery of the property, and the additional amount is only due once the work (occupancy or destination) becomes known. The Sahibayn and Zufar disallow it because the object of contract appears to be one (the premises or beast) while the wages are uncertain. Abu Hanifa's position is preferred, analogizing to the garment tailoring case where wage is suspended on the work. The phrase 'هذا أولى' (this is even more appropriate) suggests Abu Hanifa's view is stronger here.

Key Terms
تَرْدِيدُ الْأَجْرِ (tardīd al-ajr): Variable wage dependent on the type of work, distance, or load.
الخياطة الرومية والفارسية (al-khiyāṭa al-rūmiyya wa-l-fārisiyya): Roman and Persian tailoring – two different styles of stitching, used as an analogy for variable wages in hiring.
جَهَالَة (jahāla): Uncertainty or ignorance in a contract term that can lead to invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if a landlord says, 'I rent you this house: if you live in it, rent is 10 dirhams; if you use it as a warehouse, 15 dirhams'?
A) The contract is invalid because the rent is uncertain.
B) The contract is valid, and 10 dirhams is due immediately; if used as warehouse, extra 5 dirhams are due.
C) The contract is valid only if the tenant selects one option at the start.
D) The contract is valid only if both rents are paid upfront.

Key Takeaway
A hiring contract with variable wages linked to actual work is valid in the Hanafi school, as the minimum wage eliminates uncertainty and the extra is contingent on performance.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Wage Conditional on Time of Work
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional wage by day in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a conditional wage varying by day, and apply Abu Hanifa's interpretation of ta'jil and tarfi to determine the correct wage.

Core Idea
A wage conditional on time is valid only if the time reference serves to hasten payment, not to fix a deadline that merges time and work.

In ijarah, ambiguity (jahalah) about the wage voids the contract. But what if the ambiguity is resolved by the worker's choice of when to perform? This passage examines a case where a tailor is promised one dirham if he sews today, half a dirham if he sews tomorrow. The Hanafi masters disagree on whether this is valid, and the outcome hinges on the legal interpretation of the words 'today' and 'tomorrow'. We will unpack the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and see how a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) preserves the contract for the first day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Conditional Structure
The act is hiring a tailor (ijarah). The wage is not fixed absolutely: 'if you sew today, one dirham; if tomorrow, half a dirham.' This creates a range of possibilities. First, recognize that the work (sewing) is a single task, but two wages are offered alternatively based on time.
This structure is called tardid – alternation between conditions.
2
Distinguish Abu Hanifa's Interpretation (ta'jil & tarfi)
Abu Hanifa interprets 'today' as ta'jil (hastening) – it prompts immediate payment, not a fixed time limit. 'Tomorrow' is tarfi (broadening/giving respite) – it simply widens the time frame, not a suspension or a new contract. Thus, on the first day, there is only one wage (one dirham) for the work, so no ambiguity. For the second day, two wages are present (dirham and half dirham) on an alternative basis, creating jahalah, so that part is invalid.
This avoids ijtima' (concurrence) of time and work, which would invalidate the entire ijarah.
3
Contrast the Sahibayn's Interpretation (ta'qit & idafah)
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) interpret 'today' literally as a time limit (ta'qit). The contract covers only today; after today it expires. 'Tomorrow' is idafah (addition) – a new contract for the next day with its own named wage. Thus, each day has a single wage, so both days are valid.
Under this view, if the tailor sews tomorrow, he gets exactly half a dirham, not ujrat al-mithl.
4
Note Zufar's Position – Total Invalidity
Zufar and the 'three' hold the entire contract void because one sewing job is paired with two alternative wages, causing uncertainty (jahalah) from the outset. This view rejects any validity.
This is the strictest position, avoiding any conditional pricing.
5
Apply Abu Hanifa's Ruling to Determine the Tailor's Wage
Under the mufta bihi position of Abu Hanifa: if the tailor sews today, he receives the named one dirham. If he sews tomorrow, the contract for that day is invalid, so he gets the customary wage (ujrat al-mithl) for the work, but capped at the named half dirham (the maximum agreed for that day).
The thamarah al-khilaf: the Sahibayn would give exactly half a dirham for tomorrow; Abu Hanifa would give ujrat al-mithl ≤ half dirham.

Source Text

يصح

وذكر الغد في قوله : "إن خطته غدا فبنصف درهم للترفيه لا للتعليق ولا للإضافة فإذا كان ذكر اليوم للتعجيل كان الأجر مقابلا بنفس الخياطة في اليوم، وكذا في الغد؛ لأن ذكره للترفيه، فيجتمع في كل واحد أجران على البدل، وهو يوجب الجهالة ولهما: أن ذكر اليوم للتأقيت؛ لأنه حقيقة فكان قوله إن خطته اليوم فبدرهم يقتصر على اليوم، فبانقضاء اليوم لا يبقى العقد إلى الغد، بل ينقضي بانقضاء الوقت وذكر الغد للإضافة، وإذا كان للإضافة لم يكن العقد ثابتا في الحال، فلا يجتمع في كل يوم تسميتان وله أن ذكر الغد للإضافة، وذكر اليوم للتعجيل لا يمكن حمله على التأقيت الذي هو حقيقة، وإلا فسد العقد؛ لاجتماع الوقت والعمل، وإذا كان كذلك يجتمع في الغد تسميتان دون اليوم، فيصح في الأول، ويجب المسمى، ويفسد الثاني، ويجب أجر المثل لا يجاوز به نصف درهم؛ لأنه هو المسمى في اليوم الثاني. (هذا ما لخصته من الشروح والحواشي)
The wage on one of two conditions. And regarding the shop, house, and animal, distance and load. = It is valid. So one of them becomes determined by his choice, and the ambiguity leading to dispute is removed. The ruling of the alternation regarding the garment in terms of time is that in the first [day] meaning what is named is obligatory if the work occurs on the first of the two days between which alternation occurs, not the second. This is the meaning of the author's statement: 'And time-wise in the first.' So if he sews it today, he gets a dirham; if he sews it tomorrow, he gets its equivalent wage not exceeding the named amount. This according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is valid in the first and the second, so if he sews it today, he gets a dirham; if he sews it tomorrow, he gets half a dirham. And Zufar and the three said: It is not valid in the first nor the second, because sewing is one thing and two compensations are mentioned in exchange for it on an alternative basis, so it becomes ambiguous. And this is because the mention of 'today' in his statement 'If you sew it today, then for a dirham' is for hastening not for specifying a time, even though it is literal in it; otherwise, concurrence of time and work would occur in ijarah, which is invalidating as previously mentioned. And the mention of 'tomorrow' in his statement 'If you sew it tomorrow, then for half a dirham' is for broadening (giving respite), not for suspension nor for addition. So when the mention of today is for hastening, the wage is in exchange for the sewing itself on that day, and similarly for tomorrow; because its mention is for broadening; thus two wages combine in each one on an alternative basis, which causes ambiguity. And for them (the two): The mention of today is for specifying a time, because it is literal; so his statement 'If you sew it today, then for a dirham' is confined to today; when today ends, the contract does not remain until tomorrow but expires with the time. And the mention of tomorrow is for addition; when it is for addition, the contract is not established at the present, so two namings do not combine in each day. And for him (Abu Hanifa): The mention of tomorrow is for addition, and the mention of today for hastening cannot be interpreted as specification of time which is its literal meaning; otherwise the contract would be invalid due to concurrence of time and work. When it is so, two namings combine in tomorrow but not in today; so it is valid in the first, and the named sum is obligatory, and the second is invalid, and the equivalent wage is obligatory not exceeding half a dirham, because that is the named sum in the second day. (This is what I summarized from the commentaries and glosses).
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of an ijarah contract where the wage is conditioned on the time of performance. The author presents the case: a tailor is hired with the condition that if he sews today, he gets one dirham, but if he sews tomorrow, he gets half a dirham. The dispute centers on whether such conditional pricing creates fatal ambiguity (jahalah) or can be resolved. 

Abu Hanifa holds that the contract is valid only for the first day (today). If the tailor sews today, he gets the named dirham. If he sews tomorrow, the contract is invalid for the second day and he gets the customary wage (ujrat al-mithl) not exceeding the second named sum (half dirham). His reasoning: The mention of 'today' is for 'ta'jil' (hastening of payment) not for specifying a time limit, because if it were a time limit, there would be concurrence (ijtima') of time and work, which invalidates ijarah. The mention of 'tomorrow' is for 'tarfi' (broadening/giving respite). Thus, the contract is valid for today with a definite wage. For tomorrow, since two wages are mentioned (the original dirham and the half dirham) on an alternative basis, ambiguity arises, so that part is invalid.

Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue the contract is valid for both days. They interpret 'today' as a time limit (ta'qit), so the contract only covers today. Tomorrow, a new contract must be formed, and the half dirham is the named wage for that new contract. Thus no ambiguity.

Zufar and the later three scholars (probably from other schools or a later generation) hold the entire contract invalid because the single work (sewing) is paired with two wages alternatively, resulting in uncertain obligation.

The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) seems to be Abu Hanifa's view, as the author elaborates its reasoning and concludes with the summary. The text annotates that this ruling applies similarly to hiring a shop, house, or animal with conditional wages based on use or destination (as will be discussed next).

Key Terms
الترديد (al-tardid): Alternation or conditional offering of wages; stating two different wages conditionally on different times.
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Hastening; implying prompt payment or performance, not setting a time limit.
الترفيه (al-tarfi): Broadening; giving respite or widening the time frame, akin to granting an extension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what wage does the tailor receive if he sews tomorrow?
A) Full dirham
B) Half dirham
C) Equivalent wage not exceeding half dirham
D) Nothing, contract void

Key Takeaway
The validity of a time-conditioned wage in ijarah depends on whether the time reference is interpreted as hastening payment (ta'jil) or fixing a deadline (ta'qit); Abu Hanifa's interpretation ensures the contract is valid for the first day.

Conditional Rent Varying by Profession: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Extension of wage variation principle to shop/house rental

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional wages in ijarah where rent varies by the tenant's profession, explain the Sahibayn's objection, and apply Abu Hanifa's reasoning to similar cases.

Core Idea
A conditional wage in ijarah is valid if the lesser wage is due immediately and the extra is suspended on the condition.

This lesson extends the earlier dispute about wages in tailoring to a new scenario: renting a shop or house where the rent depends on the tenant's profession. Abu Hanifa validates such a contract by making the lesser wage immediately due and the increase contingent on the actual work, while the Sahibayn and others reject it due to uncertainty. The passage uses analogy to show why this approach is sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the dispute
The case: rent of a shop/house varies based on whether the tenant is a perfume seller (1 dirham) or a blacksmith (2 dirhams). Abu Hanifa says the contract is valid; the Sahibayn say it is invalid because the object of contract (usufruct) is one but wages differ, creating uncertainty (jahalah).
Note: The Sahibayn include Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani; Zufar and the 'three' later scholars agree with them.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that upon delivery of the premises, the lesser wage (1 dirham) becomes wajib (obligatory). The extra dirham is suspended (mawquf) on the occurrence of the condition (the actual profession performed). This removes the uncertainty because at any point, the due amount is known: either 1 or 2 dirhams, determined by the actual work.
The lesser wage is like a base rent; the increase is a conditional premium.
3
Compare to the analogous case (qiyas)
The author states that if wage suspension is valid in the tailoring case (Roman vs. Persian stitching), it is even more appropriate here (awla). This is an a fortiori analogy: the principle of suspending wage on work appearance is already accepted, so it applies here.
The tailoring case had the wage vary by type of work (Roman vs. Persian), which was deemed valid despite initial uncertainty.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text says 'hadha awla' (this is more appropriate), indicating preference for Abu Hanifa's view. Thus the mufta bihi in this matn is the validity of the contract with the lesser wage due immediately and the extra suspended.
Later Hanafi jurists (e.g., in al-Hidayah) also adopt this as the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الدكان والبيت إلخ عطف على " في الثوب" أي صح ترديد الأجر بترديد العمل في الدكان والبيت بأن قال: إن أسكنت هذا الدكان أو هذا البيت عطارا فبدرهم في الشهر ، وإن أسكنتها حدادا فبدرهمين، فالعقد جائز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يصح العقد؛ لأن المعقود عليه ،واحد والأجران مختلفان، ولا ندري أيهما يجب فلا يصح، وبه قال زفر والثلاثة، وله أن أقل الأجرتين يجب بتسليم المحل، والزيادة موقوفة على ظهور العمل، ولو كان الأجر موقوفا على ذلك أي ظهور العمل كما في مسألة الخياطة الرومية والفارسية جاز، فهذا أولى. رمز الحقائق: ٢٨٤/٢]
And regarding the shop and house etc., it is connected by conjunction to 'in the garment', i.e., the alternation of the wage by the alternation of the work in the shop and house is valid, such that he says: 'If I lodge in this shop or house a perfume seller, then one dirham per month; and if I lodge in it a blacksmith, then two dirhams.' The contract is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The contract is not valid because the object of the contract is one and the wages are different, and we do not know which one is obligatory, so it is not valid. And Zufar and the three said the same. And for him (Abu Hanifa): The lesser of the two wages is obligatory upon delivery of the premises, and the increase is suspended upon the appearance of the work. And if the wage were suspended on that (i.e., appearance of work) as in the case of Roman and Persian tailoring, it would be valid; so this is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage extends the previous dispute to a case where a shop or house is rented with rent varying based on the profession of the tenant. The example: if a perfume seller lodges, rent is 1 dirham/month; if a blacksmith, 2 dirhams/month. 

Abu Hanifa validates the contract. His reasoning: Upon delivery of the premises, the lesser wage (1 dirham) becomes due immediately. The extra dirham is contingent on the actual work/profession being performed. This is analogous to the previous case of tailoring with different styles (Roman vs. Persian), where the wage varied by the type of work done. Since that was valid, this is even more fitting (awla).

The Sahibayn and others reject validity because the contracted object (the benefit of the premises) is one, but the wages are two and uncertain (which will be paid?). 

The relied-upon position in the matn is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is introduced with 'And for him' supporting reasoning and the phrase 'this is more appropriate'.

Key Terms
المعقود عليه (al-ma'qud 'alayhi): The object of the contract; in ijarah, it is the usufruct (manfa'ah) of the premises.
ترديد الأجر (tardid al-ajr): Alternation or variation of the wage depending on a condition.
موقوفة (mawqufah): Suspended; the extra wage is not immediately due but contingent on the occurrence of the condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's ruling validates conditional wage contracts in ijarah by making the lesser wage immediately due and the extra suspended on the condition, an approach upheld by the school as mufta bihi.
