Disputes over Garment Type, Color, and Wage: Owner vs. Craftsman
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wage claims with split rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disputes between cloth owner and craftsman regarding specifications and wage, and identify the mufta bihi position within the school.

Core Idea
The owner's word prevails on specifications; but a professional craftsman's wage claim is accepted.

When a cloth owner and a craftsman disagree about what was ordered or whether a wage was agreed, how does Hanafi law resolve it? This passage presents the key rulings and an important intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. You will learn the default qiyas position, the istihsan-based exceptions, and which view is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputes covered
The passage addresses two main types: (1) dispute over the type of garment (shirt vs. cloak) or color (red vs. yellow), and (2) dispute over whether a wage was agreed.
2
Analyze the rule for specification disputes
In both garment and color disputes, the owner's statement is given weight with an oath. Trace the reasoning: the owner is the source of permission, so he knows best what he ordered. The owner then has the option to sue for damages or accept the garment and pay a fair wage.
Condition: dispute must be after work is done and no evidence exists.
3
Analyze the wage dispute and intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa (qiyas): owner's word prevails as denier. Abu Yusuf: if regular dealing, craftsman gets wage. Muhammad: if craftsman is known for working for wages, his word is given weight (istihsan). Follow the reasoning for each.
Muhammad's view is the mufta bihi.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, owner never pays without proof. Under Muhammad, a professional tailor is paid the customary wage. Note how this protects the livelihood of artisans.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling to a modern scenario
Imagine you hire a professional tailor to stitch a shirt; you later dispute the agreed wage. According to mufta bihi, the tailor's statement is accepted if he is known for working for wages. You would pay the customary wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقول لرب الثوب في القميص والقباء والحمرة والصفرة والأجر وعدمه. يعني لو استأجر عبدا شهرا مثلا، ثم قال المستأجر في آخر الشهر أبق العبد أو مرض في المدة، وأنكر المولى ذلك، أو أنكر استناده إلى أول المدة، فقال: أصابه المرض قبل أن تأتيني بساعة، يحكم الحال، فيكون القول - قول من شهد له الحال مع يمينه؛ لأن القول في الدعاوي قول من يشهد له الظاهر، ووجوده في الحال يدل على وجوده في الماضي، فيصلح الظاهر مرجحا وإن لم يصلح حجة كما إذا اختلفا في جريان ماء الطاحون وانقطاعه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٦٧/٨ والقول: أي إن اختلف رب الثوب والخياط في المخيط، فقال رب الثوب: أمرتك أن تعمله قباء، وقال الخياط: بل أمرتني أن أعمل قميصا فالقول لرب الثوب والحمرة والصفرة إلخ : يعني إذا اختلف رب الثوب والصباغ رب الثوب: أمرتك أن تصبغه أحمر فصبغت أصفر، وقال الصباغ بل أمرتني بصبغه أصفر، فالقول لرب الثوب كما في اختلاف القميص والقباء. ووجهما: أن الإذن يستفاد من جهة رب الثوب فكان أعلم بكيفيته، ولأنه لو أنكر الإذن بالكلية كان القول قوله، فكذا إذا أنكر وصفه؛ إذ الوصف تابع للأصل لكنه يحلف؛ لأنه ادعى عليه شيئا لو أقر به يلزمه، فإذا أنكره يحلف، فإذا حلف فالخياط ضامن وصاحب الثوب مخير إن شاء ضمنه قيمة الثوب غير معمول ولا أجر له، أو قيمته معمولا وله أجر مثله لا يجاوز به المسمى تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٤/٦ وتبعه العيني والحموي، قال في "الفتح": قال شيخنا نقلا عن "عربي زاده وهذا سهو مخالف لكلام القوم، والذي في عامة الكتب: وإن شاء أخذه وأعطاه أجر مثله، فتنبه له ثم ههنا قيدان الأول أن يكون اختلافهما بعد العمل، أما لو كان قبله فيتحالفان، والثاني: أن لا يكون لهما بينة، فإن أقاما البينة فالبينة بينة الخياط. (فتح وغيره مع توضيح) والأجر إلخ أي إذا اختلف رب الثوب والصانع بأن قال رب الثوب: عملته لي بغير أجر، وقال الصانع: بل بأجر، فالقول لرب الثوب أيضا مطلقا عند الإمام كما في المسألتين الأوليين؛ لأن رب الثوب ينكر تقوم عمله، الأجر عليه، والصانع يدعيه فكان القول للمنكر، وهذا هو القياس، وقال أبو يوسف: إن كان الصانع معاملا له بأن كان بينهما أخذ وإعطاء، فله الأجر، وإلا فلا، وقال محمد: إن كان الصانع معروفا بهذه الصنعة بالأجرة كان القول قوله وإلا فلا؛ لأنه لما فتح الدكان لذلك جرى ذلك مجرى التنصيص على الأجر اعتبارا للظاهر، وقولهما الاستحسان والجواب عنه : أن الظاهر الدفع والحاجة ههنا إلى الاستحقاق، فلا يكفي، كذا في "الفتح" و"التكملة" وغيرهما وفي "الدر المختار" وكذا في "التكملة" وبقول محمد يفتى.
And the saying is with the owner of the cloth regarding the shirt and the cloak and the red and the yellow and the wage and its absence. That is, if someone hires a slave for a month, etc. (the repeated ibaq/marad passage) And the saying: that is, if the owner of the cloth and the tailor dispute about the stitched garment, and the owner of the cloth says: I ordered you to make it a cloak, and the tailor says: rather you ordered me to make a shirt, then the saying is with the owner of the cloth. And the red and the yellow etc.: that is, if the owner of the cloth and the dyer dispute, the owner of the cloth says: I ordered you to dye it red but you dyed it yellow, and the dyer says: rather you ordered me to dye it yellow, then the saying is with the owner of the cloth as in the dispute of the shirt and cloak. And the explanation for both: that permission is derived from the owner of the cloth, so he is more knowledgeable about its nature, and because if he denied the permission entirely, the saying would be his; so likewise if he denies its description, for the description follows the original. But he takes an oath because he claims something against him that if he admitted would necessitate liability, so if he denies it, he takes an oath. Once he takes the oath, the tailor is liable, and the owner of the cloth has the option: if he wishes, he can hold him liable for the value of the cloth unworked, with no wage for the tailor, or its value worked, and the tailor gets the like of his wage not exceeding the named amount. Clarification of Truths: 6/154, and al-Ayni and al-Hamawi followed him. He said in al-Fath: Our shaykh said quoting from Arabizada: 'This is a mistake contrary to the statements of the people. What is in most books is: if he wishes, he takes it and gives him the like of his wage.' So be aware of this. Then there are two conditions: first, that their dispute occurs after the work; if before, they take mutual oaths (tahaluf); second, that they have no evidence, for if they produce evidence, the evidence of the tailor is preferred. (Fath and others with clarification) And the wage etc.: that is, if the owner of the cloth and the artisan dispute: the owner says: you worked it for me without wage, and the artisan says: rather for a wage, then the saying is with the owner of the cloth absolutely according to Imam Abu Hanifa, as in the first two issues; because the owner denies that his work is a countervalue, that the wage is due, while the artisan claims it, so the saying is with the denier, and this is the analogy (qiyas). Abu Yusuf said: if the artisan was a trader dealing with him, i.e., there was taking and giving between them, then he gets the wage; otherwise not. Muhammad said: if the artisan is known for this craft with wages, then his saying is given weight; otherwise not; because when he opened the shop for that, it is like explicit stipulation of wages, considering the apparent. Their statement is istihsan. The response to it: that the apparent is payment and the need here is for entitlement, so it is not sufficient. This is in al-Fath, al-Takmilah, etc., and in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and similarly in al-Takmilah, and the fatwa is given according to Muhammad's opinion.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage deals with disputes between the owner of a cloth (or garment) and a craftsman (tailor or dyer). It covers two scenarios: (1) dispute about the type of garment ordered (shirt vs. cloak) or the color (red vs. yellow), and (2) dispute about whether a wage was agreed. In the first scenario, the Hanafi rule is that the owner's statement is given weight, with an oath, because he is the source of permission and knows best what he ordered. The owner has the option after the oath: he can claim the value of the unworked cloth (by suing for damages) and not pay the craftsman, or take the worked cloth and pay the craftsman the market wage for the work, not exceeding the agreed amount. This is with two conditions: the dispute must be after the work is done (if before, the parties take mutual oaths and the contract is rescinded), and they have no evidence (if they have evidence, the tailor's evidence is preferred because it supports his claim). In the second scenario (wage dispute), Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the owner's statement is given weight absolutely, as he is the denier. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad offer modifications: Abu Yusuf says if the craftsman is a regular business partner (mut'amal), he gets the wage; Muhammad says if the craftsman is known for working for wages (e.g., a professional tailor), his statement is given weight. The fatwa (mufta bihi) is according to Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
رب الثوب (rabb al-thawb): The owner of the cloth or garment who hires a craftsman to work on it.
الخياط (al-khayyat): The tailor who stitches the garment.
الصباغ (al-sabbagh): The dyer who colors the cloth.
المسمى (al-musamma): The wage explicitly named in the contract (ajr musamma).
أجر مثله (ajr mithlihi): The customary or fair wage for similar work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, if a cloth owner and a tailor dispute about whether a wage was agreed, and the tailor is a professional known for working for wages, whose statement is accepted?
A) The owner's, because he denies the claim.
B) The tailor's, because he is known for working for wages.
C) Both must take oaths and the contract is rescinded.
D) The tailor's, only if he can produce evidence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the owner's word decides garment specifications, but for wages the mufta bihi protects professional artisans by accepting their word.

Disputes Between Owner and Craftsman in Ijarah: The Three Questions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah disputes: qiyas vs istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of disputes in ijarah and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on wage disputes, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In ijarah disputes, the owner's word is taken by qiyas, but istihsan prefers the craftsman if custom supports him.

When an owner gives cloth to a tailor or dyer, disputes may arise over what was ordered or whether a wage was agreed. The Hanafi school addresses these with a general rule: the owner's word is accepted if the circumstances suggest he is right. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) introduced exceptions based on custom and common practice. This lesson walks through the three key disputes and the ikhtilaf that led to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three disputes
The passage deals with three scenarios: 1) dispute over garment type (shirt vs cloak), 2) dispute over dye color (red vs yellow), 3) dispute over wage (whether wage was agreed). List them.
The first two are parallel; the third has more nuance.
2
Understand the default qiyas rule
Abu Hanifa applies qiyas: the owner is the denier (munkir) of the wage claim, so his word is taken with oath. Similarly for type and color, since permission comes from him.
This is consistent with the principle 'al-bayyinah 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara'.
3
Examine the istihsan of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad depart from qiyas using istihsan. They argue that custom (urf) and apparent circumstance (zahir al-hal) should be considered. Abu Yusuf looks at regular dealing; Muhammad looks at the craftsman's known trade.
Istihsan is applied to avoid hardship and give weight to common practice.
4
Note the conditions for the ruling
The dispute must be after the work is done; if before, they take mutual oaths (tahaluf). Also, neither party may have evidence; if they do, the tailor's evidence is preferred.
These conditions modify the application.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The passage states that fatwa is given by Muhammad's position: if the craftsman is known for wage work (e.g., has a shop), his word is accepted; otherwise the owner's word prevails.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة
والقول لرب الثوب في القميص والقباء والحمرة والصفرة والأجر وعدمه.
إجارة العبد
- قول من شهد له الحال مع يمينه؛ لأن القول في الدعاوي قول من يشهد له الظاهر، ووجوده في الحال يدل على وجوده في الماضي، فيصلح الظاهر مرجحا وإن لم يصلح حجة كما إذا اختلفا في جريان ماء الطاحون وانقطاعه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٦٧/٨] والقول: أي إن اختلف رب الثوب والخياط في المخيط، فقال رب الثوب: أمرتك أن تعمله قباء، وقال الخياط: بل أمرتني أن أعمل قميصا فالقول لرب الثوب والحمرة والصفرة إلخ : يعني إذا اختلف رب الثوب والصباغ رب الثوب: أمرتك أن تصبغه أحمر فصبغت أصفر، وقال الصباغ بل أمرتني بصبغه أصفر، فالقول لرب الثوب كما في اختلاف القميص والقباء.
فقال
ووجهما: أن الإذن يستفاد من جهة رب الثوب فكان أعلم بكيفيته، ولأنه لو أنكر الإذن بالكلية كان القول قوله، فكذا إذا أنكر وصفه؛ إذ الوصف تابع للأصل لكنه يحلف؛ لأنه ادعى عليه شيئا لو أقر به يلزمه، فإذا أنكره يحلف، فإذا حلف فالخياط ضامن وصاحب الثوب مخير إن شاء ضمنه قيمة الثوب غير معمول ولا أجر له، أو قيمته معمولا وله أجر مثله لا يجاوز به المسمى تبيين الحقائق: ١٥٤/٦] وتبعه العيني والحموي، قال في "الفتح": قال شيخنا نقلا عن "عربي زاده وهذا سهو مخالف لكلام القوم، والذي في عامة الكتب: وإن شاء أخذه وأعطاه أجر مثله، فتنبه له ثم ههنا قيدان الأول أن يكون اختلافهما بعد العمل، أما لو كان قبله فيتحالفان، والثاني: أن لا يكون لهما بينة، فإن أقاما البينة فالبينة بينة الخياط. (فتح وغيره مع توضيح) والأجر إلخ أي إذا اختلف رب الثوب والصانع بأن قال رب الثوب: عملته لي بغير أجر، وقال الصانع: بل بأجر، فالقول لرب الثوب أيضا مطلقا عند الإمام كما في المسألتين الأوليين؛ لأن رب الثوب ينكر تقوم عمله، الأجر عليه، والصانع يدعيه فكان القول للمنكر، وهذا هو القياس، وقال أبو يوسف: إن كان الصانع معاملا له بأن كان بينهما أخذ وإعطاء، فله الأجر، وإلا فلا، وقال محمد: إن كان الصانع معروفا بهذه الصنعة بالأجرة كان القول قوله وإلا فلا؛ لأنه لما فتح الدكان لذلك جرى ذلك مجرى التنصيص على الأجر اعتبارا للظاهر، وقولهما الاستحسان والجواب عنه : أن الظاهر الدفع والحاجة ههنا إلى الاستحقاق، فلا يكفي، كذا في "الفتح" و"التكملة" وغيرهما وفي "الدر المختار" وكذا في "التكملة" وبقول محمد يفتى.
The Book of Ijarah. And the word is that of the owner of the cloth regarding the shirt and the cloak, and the red and yellow, and the wage and its absence. It is the word of one whom the present state supports with his oath; because in claims, the word is that of one whom the apparent circumstance supports, and its existence in the present indicates its existence in the past, so the apparent circumstance is suitable as a weight (for preference) even if it is not suitable as a proof, just as when they differ regarding the running of the mill water and its cessation. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:67) And the word: meaning when the owner of the cloth and the tailor differ about the sewing, and the owner of the cloth says: I ordered you to make it a cloak, and the tailor says: Rather you ordered me to make a shirt, then the word is that of the owner of the cloth. And the red and the yellow etc.: meaning when the owner of the cloth and the dyer differ, the owner of the cloth says: I ordered you to dye it red and you dyed it yellow, and the dyer says: Rather you ordered me to dye it yellow, then the word is that of the owner of the cloth, as in the difference of the shirt and the cloak. So he said: And their justification: that the permission is obtained from the side of the owner of the cloth, so he is more knowledgeable of its manner; and because if he had denied the permission entirely, his word would be accepted, so likewise when he denies its description, since the description is subsidiary to the principal; but he takes an oath, because something is claimed against him that if he admitted it, it would be binding on him; when he denies it, he takes an oath. So when he takes the oath, the tailor is liable, and the owner of the cloth has the option: if he wishes, he may make him liable for the value of the cloth unworked, with no wage for him; or its value worked, and he gets its like wage not exceeding the named amount. (Tabayin al-Haqa'iq 6:154) And al-Ayni and al-Himawi followed him. He said in al-Fath: Our teacher said, quoting from Arabizada: 'And this is an error contrary to the statement of the people; and what is in most books is: And if he wishes, he may take it and give him its like wage. So pay attention to this.' Then here there are two restrictions: first, that their dispute is after the work; if it is before, then they take mutual oaths (tahaluf); second, that neither has evidence; if they produce evidence, then the evidence is that of the tailor. (al-Fath and others with clarification) And the wage etc.: meaning when the owner of the cloth and the craftsman differ, the owner of the cloth saying: You worked it for me without wage, and the craftsman saying: Rather with wage, then the word is that of the owner of the cloth also, absolutely according to al-Imam (Abu Hanifa), as in the first two issues, because the owner of the cloth denies the occurrence of his work, and the wage is claimed against him, and the craftsman claims it, so the word is that of the denier; this is qiyas. And Abu Yusuf said: If the craftsman was a dealer with him, meaning there was taking and giving between them, then he gets the wage, otherwise not. And Muhammad said: If the craftsman was known for this trade for a wage, then his word is accepted, otherwise not; because when he opened the shop for that, this takes the place of specification of the wage, considering the apparent circumstance. And their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) statement is istihsan. The answer to it: that the apparent circumstance is for payment, but here there is need for entitlement, so it is not sufficient. (Thus in al-Fath and al-Takmilah and others) And in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: and likewise in al-Takmilah: And by Muhammad's statement fatwa is given.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ijarah deals with disputes between the owner of a cloth and a craftsman (tailor or dyer) regarding the specifications of the work and the wage. The author first states the general principle: in disputes, the word is given to the one whom the present circumstances support, and he takes an oath. This principle is applied to three specific disputes. First, if the owner says he ordered a cloak and the tailor says he ordered a shirt, the owner's word is taken. Second, similarly for dyeing color disputes. The reasoning is that the permission comes from the owner, so he knows best what he ordered. Third, regarding the wage: if the owner claims the work was without wage and the craftsman claims it was for a wage, the owner's word is taken at face value according to Abu Hanifa (qiyas). However, Abu Yusuf qualifies this: if the craftsman was a regular business associate, his claim is accepted. Muhammad goes further: if the craftsman is known to work for wages (like having a shop), his word is preferred because the custom indicates a wage. The passage concludes that fatwa is given by Muhammad's statement (which prefers the craftsman's claim if he is known for wage work). The text also mentions that if the work was before the dispute, the owner can choose either to take the cloth unworked and get its value, or take it worked and pay the market wage (not exceeding the agreed amount). If there is evidence, the tailor's evidence is preferred. The two conditions noted: the dispute must be after the work, and neither party must have evidence.

Key Terms
القميص (al-qamīṣ): A shirt-like garment
القباء (al-qabā'): A cloak or outer garment
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a departure from qiyas for a stronger reason such as custom or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Always, because the craftsman did the work.
B) Never, because the owner is the denier.
C) Only if the craftsman is known to work for wages, e.g., has a shop.
D) Only if there is a written contract.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that if the craftsman is known to work for wages, his word is taken; otherwise the owner's word prevails.

Termination of Ijarah Due to Defect or Destruction
Rulings on termination by defect and destruction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a lessee may terminate an ijarah contract due to a defect and apply the ruling to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A lessee may terminate ijarah only for defects that impair the intended benefit; minor defects give no option.

In this passage, the author explains the rules for terminating a lease when the property is defective or destroyed. The key is whether the defect actually harms the benefit the lessee intended. Let's work through the conditions and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defect's impact
Determine whether the defect is harmful to the intended benefit (e.g., a collapsed wall that disrupts dwelling) or minor (e.g., a fallen wall that does not affect dwelling). Only harmful defects give a termination option.
The text gives examples: loss of an eye or hair of a hired slave is minor; illness of the slave is harmful.
2
Check lessee's knowledge at contract
If the lessee saw the defect at the time of contract, he has no option to terminate because he consented. If he was unaware, the option exists.
The contract implies soundness; if soundness is missing, consent is vitiated.
3
Consider lessee's use after defect
If the lessee uses the property despite knowing the defect, he is deemed to have consented, and the option is lost. Full rent is due.
Use after knowledge implies acceptance.
4
Check if lessor removes the defect
If the lessor removes the defect, the lessee loses the option to terminate. The contract continues.
Removal restores the intended benefit.
5
Apply special rules for total destruction
If the entire house collapses (or water source is cut off, etc.), the lessee can terminate without the lessor's presence, and no rent is due for the remaining period.
Total destruction makes benefit impossible; termination is immediate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب فسخ الإجارة
وتفسخ بالعيب وخراب الدار .
وانفساخها
باب فسخ الإجارة: هذا باب في بيان أحكام فسخ الإجارة، أخر هذا الباب؛ لأن فسخ العقد بعد وجوده لا محالة. تفسخ بالعيب: لما كانت الإجارة تفسخ بخيار شرط ورؤية وعيب وبعذر شرع المصنف في بيانها، وشرع أولا في بيان العيب، فقال: "وتفسخ "بالعيب" يعني إذا استأجر أحد دارا، فوجد بها عيبا يضر بالسكني، فللمستأجر الفسخ وتفصيله: أن العيب سواء كان قديما أو حدث بعد العقد أو بعد القبض، إما أن يكون مضرا بالمستأجر ومؤثرا بالانتفاع أو لا، فإن لم يكن مضرا ولا مؤثرا بالانتفاع كأن سقط حائط من الدار، ولم يخل بالسكنى، أو فقأت إحدى عيني العبد المستأجر أو سقط شعره بقي العقد لازما، ولا خيار للمستأجر، وإن كان مضرا بالانتفاع كأن سقط من الدار حائط يضر بالسكنى، أو مرض العبد أو وبرت الدابة. فإما أن يكون المستأجر رآه وقت العقد أو لا، فإن رآه فلا خيار له؛ لرضائه به وإن لم يره فله فسخ الإجارة؛ لاقتضاء العقد السلامة، فإذا لم يسلم فات رضاه، فله أن يفسخ كما في البيع والمعقود عليه ههنا المنافع، وهي تحدث ساعة فساعة فما وجد من العيب يكون حادثا قبل القبض في حق ما بقي من المنافع، فيوجب خيار الفسخ، ولو استوفى مع العيب، فقد رضي به فيلزمه كل البدل، ولو أزال المؤجر العيب، فلا خيار له، ولابد للفسخ من حضرة المؤجر؛ لأن الرد بعيب شرطه ذلك اتفاقا، فلو فسخ بلا حضوره لزمه الأجر؛ لأن الرد لم يصح، ولو انهدم كل الدار كان له الفسخ عند غيبته، ويسقط الأجر عند الكل، ولا تنفسخ ما لم يفسخ؛ لأن الانتفاع بالوصية ممكن.
فسقط
واعلم أنه يشترط للفسخ من الرضاء أو القضاء، قال في "التكملة": وفي "الزيادات": يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي ليفسخ، قال شمس الأئمة: رواية الزيادات أصح كذا في "الخلاصة" وفي الجامع الصغير: يشترط لصحة الفسخ الرضاء أو القضاء انتهى تكملة البحر الرائق: ۷۰/۸] وفيه تفصيل سيأتي، وفيه أيضا: أو استأجر دارين من أحدهما حائط أو يمنع مانع من أحدهما أو وجد في أحدهما عيب ينقص السكنى فله أن يتركهما جميعا إذا كان عقد عليهما عقدا واحدا. [ملخص الشروح ورد المحتار وغيره] وخراب الدار إلخ يعني إذا خربت الدار المستأجرة للسكنى أو انقطع الماء عن الضيعة، أو انقطع الماء عن الرحى، تفسخ الإجارة؛ لأن كلا منها يفوت النفع به فيثبت خيار الفسخ، ولا أجر على مستأجر؛ لعدم التمكن من الانتفاع على الوجه الذي قصده بالاستئجار.
اعلم أن العيوب بعضها ما يفوت به النفع رأسا كخراب الدار وانقطاع الماء وغيرهما، وبعضها ما يخل بالنفع كمرض العبد ووبر الدابة وسقوط الحائط، ولما كان القسم الثاني لابد فيه من الفسخ اتفاقا تركه المصنف، وبين =
Chapter of Termination of Ijarah. And it is terminated by defect and ruin of the house. And its termination. Chapter of termination of ijarah: This is a chapter explaining the rulings of termination of ijarah. He placed this chapter later because termination of a contract after its existence is inevitable. "It is terminated by defect": Since ijarah is terminated by option of condition, option of seeing, defect, and excuse, the author began explaining them, and first began with explanation of defect. He said: "And it is terminated by defect" meaning if one rents a house and finds in it a defect harmful to dwelling, then the lessee has the right to terminate. Its detail: the defect, whether it was old or occurred after the contract or after taking possession, either is harmful to the lessee and affects the benefit, or not. If it is not harmful and does not affect the benefit, such as a wall of the house falling without disrupting dwelling, or one eye of the hired slave being gouged, or his hair falling out, the contract remains binding and there is no option for the lessee. And if it is harmful to the benefit, such as a wall of the house falling that harms dwelling, or the slave falling ill, or the animal losing its fur. Then if the lessee saw it at the time of the contract, he has no option because of his consent. And if he did not see it, he has the right to terminate the ijarah because the contract implies safety (salama); when safety is not present, his consent is absent, so he may terminate as in sale. And the subject matter here is the benefits, which come into being moment by moment. So the defect found occurs before taking possession with respect to the remaining benefits, thus it creates the option of termination. And if he used the property despite the defect, he has consented, so the entire rent is binding. And if the lessor removes the defect, the lessee has no option. And termination requires the presence of the lessor, because the return due to defect has that condition by agreement. So if he terminates without his presence, the rent becomes due because the return is not valid. And if the entire house collapses, he has the right to terminate in the lessor's absence, and the rent falls away according to all. And the ijarah does not terminate unless he actually terminates, because the benefit may be possible through endowment (?) [possibly 'وصية' but unclear]. So it falls. And know that termination requires either mutual consent or court order. Al-Takmilah said: In al-Ziyadat: He raises the matter to the judge to terminate. Shams al-A'immah said: The narration of al-Ziyadat is more correct. Thus in al-Khulasa. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: The validity of termination requires consent or court order. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 8:70). And in it details will come. And in it also: If he rented two houses, and a wall from one falls, or an impediment prevents from one, or finds in one a defect that reduces dwelling, he may leave both if the contract was one contract for both. (Summary from commentaries and Radd al-Muhtar etc.) And "ruin of the house" etc.: meaning if the rented house for dwelling is ruined, or water is cut off from the estate (day'a), or water is cut off from the mill, the ijarah is terminated; because each causes the benefit to be lost, so the option of termination is established, and there is no rent on the lessee because of inability to benefit in the manner he intended by hiring. Know that some defects completely prevent benefit, like ruin of the house and water cut-off and others; and some impair benefit, like illness of the slave, loss of fur of the animal, and wall falling. And since the second category necessarily requires termination by agreement, the author left it, and explained =
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on termination (faskh) of ijarah. The author states that ijarah is terminated by defect ('ayb) and by destruction of the property (kharab al-dar). The commentary explains that defects must be harmful to the benefit: minor defects that do not affect use (e.g., a fallen wall that does not impair dwelling) do not give the right to terminate. If the defect is harmful (e.g., a wall collapse that impairs dwelling, illness of a hired slave), and the lessee was unaware at the time of contract, he may terminate the lease by analogy to sale. The reasoning is that the contract implies the property is sound (salama), and since benefits arise moment by moment, a defect occurring after contract but before possession of the remaining benefits creates an option. If the lessee uses the property despite the defect, he consents and the full rent is due. If the lessor removes the defect, the option is lost. Termination generally requires the presence of the lessor (to return the property), but if the entire house collapses, the lessee can terminate in his absence and the rent is dropped entirely. Furthermore, termination requires either mutual consent or a court order; according to al-Ziyadat, the matter should be raised to the judge. A detail is given: if one rents two houses in one contract and a defect occurs in one, he may terminate both. Finally, defects are categorized into those that fully prevent benefit (like destruction) and those that impair benefit (like illness). The author leaves the second category, noting that it necessarily requires termination by agreement.

Key Terms
العيب (al-'ayb): A defect in the leased property that impairs the intended benefit.
خراب الدار (kharāb al-dār): Total destruction of the rented house, rendering it unlivable.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Rescission or termination of a contract, here of ijarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A lessee rents a house. After one month, a wall in the garden collapses but the house remains fully habitable. The lessee wants to terminate. Which is correct?
A) He may terminate because any defect creates an option.
B) He may not terminate because the defect does not impair dwelling.
C) He may terminate only if the lessor agrees.
D) He may terminate after a court order.

Key Takeaway
A lessee may terminate an ijarah contract for a defect only if it harms the intended benefit and he was unaware at contract; total destruction allows immediate termination without lessor presence.

Actionable Defects in Lease Contracts
Detailed ruling on when a defect gives option to terminate lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between harmful and non-harmful defects in a leased property and state when the lessee has the option to terminate.

Core Idea
A defect triggers termination only if it materially impairs the intended benefit; minor defects do not.

In Hanafi law, not every defect in a leased property gives the lessee the right to cancel. The defect must be harmful to the intended benefit. This lesson unpacks the criteria used to determine when a defect is actionable, drawing on examples from the classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defect and its impact
Analyze the defect found in the leased property. Is it a crack in the wall, sickness of an animal, or loss of an eye of a slave? Determine how it affects the primary benefit (sukna, work, transport).
The defect may be pre-existing or occur after contract.
2
Classify as harmful or non-harmful
Assess whether the defect 'yadurru bil-intifa'' (harms the benefit). The text gives examples: a collapsed wall that still allows habitation is non-harmful; a wall that makes habitation difficult or impossible is harmful.
Non-harmful defects leave the contract binding with no option.
3
Check lessee's knowledge at contract time
If the lessee saw the defect at the time of contract, consent is presumed and no option exists. If unseen, the option arises because the contract implies safety.
Knowledge after contract but before exercising option may affect consent.
4
Apply the ruling
If the defect is harmful and the lessee was unaware, the lessee has the right to terminate (khiyar al-‘ayb). If the lessee used the property after discovering the defect, consent is implied and the option lapses.
Removal of the defect by the lessor also ends the option.
5
Note special scenarios
Consider cases like a joint contract for two houses where one becomes defective: the lessee may cancel the entire contract because the benefits are indivisible.
This mirrors the rule of indivisibility in sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب فسخ الإجارة: هذا باب في بيان أحكام فسخ الإجارة، أخر هذا الباب؛ لأن فسخ العقد بعد وجوده لا محالة. تفسخ بالعيب: لما كانت الإجارة تفسخ بخيار شرط ورؤية وعيب وبعذر شرع المصنف في بيانها، وشرع أولا في بيان العيب، فقال: "وتفسخ "بالعيب" يعني إذا استأجر أحد دارا، فوجد بها عيبا يضر بالسكني، فللمستأجر الفسخ وتفصيله: أن العيب سواء كان قديما أو حدث بعد العقد أو بعد القبض، إما أن يكون مضرا بالمستأجر ومؤثرا بالانتفاع أو لا، فإن لم يكن مضرا ولا مؤثرا بالانتفاع كأن سقط حائط من الدار، ولم يخل بالسكنى، أو فقأت إحدى عيني العبد المستأجر أو سقط شعره بقي العقد لازما، ولا خيار للمستأجر، وإن كان مضرا بالانتفاع كأن سقط من الدار حائط يضر بالسكنى، أو مرض العبد أو وبرت الدابة. فإما أن يكون المستأجر رآه وقت العقد أو لا، فإن رآه فلا خيار له؛ لرضائه به وإن لم يره فله فسخ الإجارة؛ لاقتضاء العقد السلامة، فإذا لم يسلم فات رضاه، فله أن يفسخ كما في البيع والمعقود عليه ههنا المنافع، وهي تحدث ساعة فساعة فما وجد من العيب يكون حادثا قبل القبض في حق ما بقي من المنافع، فيوجب خيار الفسخ، ولو استوفى مع العيب، فقد رضي به فيلزمه كل البدل، ولو أزال المؤجر العيب، فلا خيار له، ولابد للفسخ من حضرة المؤجر؛ لأن الرد بعيب شرطه ذلك اتفاقا، فلو فسخ بلا حضوره لزمه الأجر؛ لأن الرد لم يصح، ولو انهدم كل الدار كان له الفسخ عند غيبته، ويسقط الأجر عند الكل، ولا تنفسخ ما لم يفسخ؛ لأن الانتفاع بالوصية ممكن. فسقط واعلم أنه يشترط للفسخ من الرضاء أو القضاء، قال في "التكملة": وفي "الزيادات": يرفع الأمر إلى القاضي ليفسخ، قال شمس الأئمة: رواية الزيادات أصح كذا في "الخلاصة" وفي الجامع الصغير: يشترط لصحة الفسخ الرضاء أو القضاء انتهى تكملة البحر الرائق: 70/8] وفيه تفصيل سيأتي، وفيه أيضا: أو استأجر دارين من أحدهما حائط أو يمنع مانع من أحدهما أو وجد في أحدهما عيب ينقص السكنى فله أن يتركهما جميعا إذا كان عقد عليهما عقدا واحدا. [ملخص الشروح ورد المحتار وغيره]
Chapter of termination of lease: This chapter is about explaining the rulings of termination of lease, and he (the author) delayed this chapter because termination of a contract after its existence is inevitable. It terminates due to defect: because the lease may terminate by option of condition, inspection, defect, and excuse, so the author began explaining them. He started first with explaining defect, and said: 'It terminates due to defect' meaning if one rents a house and finds in it a defect harmful to residence, the lessee has the right to terminate. Its detail: the defect, whether it is old or occurred after the contract or after possession, is either harmful to the lessee and affecting the benefit or not. If it is not harmful and does not affect the benefit, like a wall of the house collapsed but it does not affect habitation, or one eye of the hired slave is knocked out or his hair falls out, the contract remains binding, and there is no option for the lessee. If it is harmful to the benefit, like a wall of the house collapsed that harms habitation, or the slave became sick, or the animal became scabbed, then if the lessee saw it at the time of the contract, he has no option due to his consent. If he did not see it, he has the right to terminate the lease because the contract implies safety. When safety is not present, his consent is nullified, so he may terminate just as in sale. Here the object of contract is the benefits, and they occur moment by moment, so whatever defect occurs is new before possession with respect to the remaining benefits, thus it gives an option to terminate. If he used (the hired item) despite the defect, he has consented, and thus the entire rental is incumbent. If the lessor removes the defect, there is no option for the lessee. Termination requires the presence of the lessor because return due to defect requires that unanimously. If he terminates without his presence, the rental becomes due because the return is invalid. If the entire house collapses, he may terminate in the lessor's absence, and the rental is waived according to all. It does not terminate unless he terminates because benefit through the will is possible. It has fallen. And know that for termination, either consent or judicial order is required. It is said in at-Takmila: In az-Ziyadat, the matter is raised to the judge to annul. Shams al-A'imma said: the narration of az-Ziyadat is more authentic, as in al-Khulasa. And in al-Jami' as-Saghir: For the validity of termination, consent or judicial order is required. End of Takmilat al-Bahr ar-Ra'iq 70/8. There is a detail that will come. And also: if he rents two houses and a wall of one or an obstacle prevents from one or he finds a defect in one that reduces habitation, he may leave both if they were contracted as one contract. (Summarized from commentaries and Radd al-Muhtar etc.)
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the ruling on terminating a lease due to a defect (al-‘ayb). The author begins by stating the general principle: a lease can be terminated due to a condition option, inspection, defect, or excuse. He then focuses on the defect. The ruling distinguishes between defects that impair benefit and those that do not. If a defect does not significantly impair the intended benefit (e.g., a minor crack or loss of one eye of a hired slave), the contract remains binding and the lessee has no right of cancellation. However, if the defect is harmful (e.g., a collapsed wall affecting habitation or the hired animal falling sick), the lessee has the right to rescind (khiyar al-‘ayb) provided he was unaware of the defect at the time of the contract. If he continued to use the property despite the defect, his consent is implied and he must pay the full rental. The lessor may also cure the defect, which extinguishes the lessee's option. Importantly, termination must be effected in the presence of the lessor or with judicial order (qada’) or mutual consent (rida’), according to the relied-upon position from az-Ziyadat. The passage also notes a special case: if someone rents two houses in a single contract and one becomes defective, he can cancel the entire contract. This is analogous to the rule of indivisibility in sale. The text draws an analogy to the law of sale, confirming that the option for defect in lease mirrors that in sale, but with attention to the unique nature of benefits as the subject matter (ma‘qud ‘alayh).

Key Terms
فسخ الإجارة (faskh al-ijarah): Termination of the lease contract before its expiry due to a recognized cause such as defect, destruction, or death.
العيب (al-‘ayb): A defect in the leased property that diminishes the benefit intended by the lessee. It gives rise to khiyar al-‘ayb (option of defect).
الرضاء أو القضاء (ar-rida' aw al-qada'): Consent (rida') of both parties or a judicial decree (qada') are the two methods to effect a valid termination of the lease in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person rents a house and finds that a wall has collapsed but the house remains habitable, does the lessee have the right to terminate the lease?
A) Yes, because any defect gives the right to terminate.
B) No, because the defect is not harmful to the intended benefit.
C) Yes, but only with the lessor's permission.
D) No, because the lessee saw the house before contracting.

Key Takeaway
A defect in a leased property gives the lessee an option to cancel only if it is harmful to the benefit and the lessee was unaware at contract time.

Procedure for Terminating a Lease Due to Defect
Detailed ruling on when a defect gives option to terminate lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi requirement that termination of a lease due to defect requires mutual consent or a judicial decree, and apply the rule to cases of joint contracts.

Core Idea
Termination of lease due to defect is not automatic; it requires either mutual consent or a judge's ruling.

Once a lessee discovers a harmful defect, the process of termination is not immediate. Hanafi law stipulates that the lease can only be ended by mutual agreement of both parties or by a judicial decree. This lesson explains the procedure, the effect of continued use, removal of the defect, and the special case of a single contract covering multiple properties.

Guided Path
1
State the requirement for termination
The text explicitly says 'يشترط للفسخ من الرضاء أو القضاء' (termination requires either consent or judicial decree). This is the foundational rule.
This applies to faskh due to defect, not to other causes.
2
Understand the basis from the sources
The passage cites two narrations: one from az-Ziyadat that requires raising the matter to a judge, and one from al-Jami' as-Saghir that requires consent or judicial decree. Shams al-A'imma prefers the Ziyadat narration as more authentic.
The mufta bihi is that a judicial decree is necessary if the lessor does not consent.
3
Apply to scenarios of usage and removal
If the lessee uses the property after discovering the defect, consent is implied and termination is lost. If the lessor removes the defect, the option also ends.
These are extensions of the consent principle.
4
Handle the joint contract case
If two properties are leased in one contract and one becomes defective, the lessee may cancel the entire contract because the benefits are indivisible (tafrīq al-ṣafqah is not allowed).
This mirrors the rule of indivisibility in sale.
5
Consider the special case of total destruction
If the entire leased property is destroyed (e.g., house collapses), the lessee may terminate without the lessor's presence and rent is automatically waived.
This is an exception: no need for consent or qada because the subject matter is gone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Does a Lease Terminate Automatically When the Property Becomes Unusable?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lease termination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on termination of a lease due to loss of benefit, identify the analogy used by each, and evaluate which is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The lease does not automatically dissolve when benefit is lost if the loss may be temporary; the lessee must exercise an option to cancel.

This lesson deals with a scenario in lease (ijara) where the property is destroyed or its essential utility (like water for a mill) is cut off. The central question is: does the contract automatically terminate because the subject matter is lost, or does it remain valid until the lessee chooses to cancel? The Hanafi school has an internal difference on this point. We will examine the two views, the qiyas behind them, and the preferred position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The text lists three specific cases: collapse of a rented house (for residence), cutting off water from an agricultural estate, and cutting off water from a mill. In each, the intended benefit is lost. Recognize that these are the triggers for the dispute.
These are the only cases mentioned, but the principle may extend to similar situations.
2
State the first view: automatic termination
Some Hanafi mashayikh hold that the lease terminates automatically (by itself) because the subject matter (the benefits) has perished, analogous to the destruction of a sold item before delivery, which voids the sale.
This view does not require any action from the lessee; the contract ceases immediately.
3
State the second view: option to terminate
The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Ayni hold that the lease does not automatically dissolve. Instead, the lessee has an option to cancel. They analogize to the case of a sold slave who absconds (ibaq) before delivery: the sale remains valid because the slave may return, and similarly the benefit may be restored.
The key distinction is that the loss may be temporary, so the contract is not void per se.
4
Identify the differentiating factor
The critical factor is whether the loss of benefit is such that return is conceivable. For temporary losses (like water cut that may resume), the contract continues; for permanent destruction (like the house collapsing entirely), automatic termination may be argued, but the preferred view still requires explicit cancellation because even reconstruction is possible.
This is the basis of the qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
5
Note the tarjih
The text states that the first position (automatic termination) is 'asahh' (more correct), but then al-Ayni supports the option view. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that the lessee must exercise the option to terminate.
The 'weaker but safer' view is that explicit cancellation is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخراب الدار إلخ يعني إذا خربت الدار المستأجرة للسكنى أو انقطع الماء عن الضيعة، أو انقطع الماء عن الرحى، تفسخ الإجارة؛ لأن كلا منها يفوت النفع به فيثبت خيار الفسخ، ولا أجر على مستأجر؛ لعدم التمكن من الانتفاع على الوجه الذي قصده بالاستئجار. اعلم أن العيوب بعضها ما يفوت به النفع رأسا كخراب الدار وانقطاع الماء وغيرهما، وبعضها ما يخل بالنفع كمرض العبد ووبر الدابة وسقوط الحائط، ولما كان القسم الثاني لابد فيه من الفسخ اتفاقا تركه المصنف، وبين القسم الأول الذي اختلف المشايخ فيه، قال في "ملا" مسكين": وقد اختلف المشايخ في هذه المسائل الثلاث، فقيل: تنفسخ بنفسها ولا يحتاج إلى الفسخ، قال في "الفتح": لأن المعقود عليه وهي المنافع قد فاتت، فصار كهلاك المبيع قبل القبض، والأول أي ما قال المصنف أصح؛ لأن المنافع قد فاتت على وجه يتصور عودها، فأشبه إباق المبيع قبل القبض، قال العيني: وهذا يشير إلى أن الإجارة لا تنفسخ بهذه الأشياء، وقال بعضهم: تنفسخ لفوات المقصود، والأول أصح؛ لأن المنافع فاتت على وجه يتصور عودها.
And destruction of the house etc.: meaning if the rented house for habitation becomes ruined, or water is cut off from the estate (agricultural land), or water is cut off from the mill, the lease terminates because each of these causes the benefit to be lost, thus the option of termination is established, and no rent is due from the lessee due to inability to benefit in the manner intended by the lease. Know that defects, some of them cause total loss of benefit like destruction of the house, cutting off of water, and others; and some of them impair benefit like sickness of the slave, scab of the animal, and collapse of a wall. Since for the second category, termination is necessary by agreement, the author left it and explained the first category concerning which the mashayikh differed. It is said in '[?]': The mashayikh differed concerning these three issues. Some said: It terminates by itself and does not need termination. It is said in al-Fath: because the subject matter, which is the benefits, has perished, so it becomes like destruction of the sold item before possession. The first (which the author said) is more correct because the benefits have perished in a manner that their return is conceivable, so it resembles the absconding (ibaq) of the sold item before possession. Al-'Ayni said: This indicates that the lease does not terminate due to these things. Some said: It terminates due to loss of purpose. The first is more correct because the benefits have perished in a manner that their return is conceivable.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when the leased property is destroyed or its essential utility is lost (e.g., a house collapses, water supply to farmland or mill is cut). The author of the matn initially states that such events cause termination, implying that the lessee has an option to cancel. However, the commentator then reveals a dispute among Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) about whether the lease terminates automatically (by itself) without the need for an act of termination, or whether it requires an exercise of the option. The text lists three scenarios: destruction of the house, cutting off water from the estate, and cutting off water from the mill. One group analogizes to the destruction of a sold item before possession, arguing that the contract becomes void because the subject matter is gone. This view holds that no formal termination is needed. The preferred view (as stated by the author and supported by al-Ayni) is that the lease does not terminate automatically; rather, the lessee must exercise the option, because the loss of benefit might be temporary (e.g., water may return). This is analogous to the case of a slave absconding (ibaq) before delivery, where the buyer has an option but the sale does not automatically dissolve. The decisive factor is that the benefit may potentially return; therefore, the contract remains valid until cancellation. This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement, with the more cautious view being that the contract remains unless formally terminated.

Key Terms
فوات النفع (fawat an-naf‘): Loss of the benefit intended from the lease, either completely (like house destruction) or partially (like a wall falling)
إباق المبيع (ibāq al-mabī‘): The absconding of a sold slave before delivery to the buyer, a classic Hanafi example for conditional contract continuation.
كهلاك المبيع (halak al-mabī‘): Destruction of the sold item before possession, causing the contract to become void automatically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi tradition, if a rented mill's water supply is cut off temporarily, the lease:
A) Terminates automatically because the benefit is lost.
B) Does not terminate automatically; the lessee must exercise an option.
C) Remains binding and the rent is still due.
D) Terminates only if the lessor agrees.

Key Takeaway
The lease does not automatically dissolve when the property becomes unusable if the loss may be temporary; the lessee must explicitly cancel to be free of obligations.

Does Death Dissolve a Lease? Hanafi vs. Other Schools
Inter-madhhab dispute on death effect on lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on termination of lease upon death, distinguish between personal and agency contracts, and evaluate the inter-madhhab argument with the practical difference.

Core Idea
Lease dissolves on death of a party who contracted for themselves; other schools analogize to sale, but Hanafi distinguishes benefit stream from ownership transfer.

The death of a lessor or lessee can bring the lease contract to an abrupt end — but only under the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, its proof, and how it differs from the Shafi‘i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools. We will also explore exceptions for agents and emergencies, and the minority view of Imam Zafar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Hanafi Rule
Find the statement in the text: 'The lease terminates by the death of one of the contracting parties if he contracted for himself.' Understand that this is the default ruling.
The condition 'if he contracted for himself' is crucial – it excludes agents and trustees.
2
Examine the Exceptions
Note two exceptions: (1) If the party contracted for another (e.g., as agent), the lease does not dissolve upon the agent's death. (2) If necessity arises (e.g., death during Hajj journey with no judge), the lease may continue temporarily until a judge decides.
The continuation under necessity is a temporary measure, not a permanent rule.
3
Analyze the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Contrast with the Shafi‘i/Maliki/Hanbali position that lease does not dissolve by death, analogous to sale. Identify the Hanafi response: the analogy fails because lease involves periodic benefits, not complete transfer like sale.
This is a classic usul dispute over the scope of qiyas.
4
Understand the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Imam Zafar argued that if one co-owner dies, the entire lease dissolves due to indivisibility (shuyu‘). The majority holds it dissolves only in the deceased's share and continues for the living owner.
The majority's reasoning: conditions are considered at inception, not during the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتنفسخ بموت أحد المتعاقدين إن عقدها لنفسه، وإن عقدها لغيره لا كالوكيل تنفسخ بموته الإجارة [؟] قال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد لا تبطل بموت أحدهما ولا بموتهما كالبيع، ولنا: أن المنافع والأجرة صارت ملكا للورثة والعقد السابق لم يوجد منهم، فتنقض، وإنما قيد بالموت احترازا عن الجنون؛ لأنه لا تنفسخ الإجارة به، ولو مطبقا، وهذا الحكم أي انفساخ العقد بلا فسخ مقيد بما إذا لم يكن ثمه ضرورة، وأما إذا دعت ضرورة، فتبقى الإجارة بالأجر المسمى فيرفع إلى القاضي ليفعل ما هو الأصلح كما إذا مات المؤجر في طريق مكة، ولا حاكم في الطريق، فإنها تبقى إلى مكة فيرفع الأمر إلى القاضي ليفعل الأصلح، فيؤجرها له لو أمينا أو يبيعها بالقيمة، ويدفع له أجرة الإياب إن برهن على دفعها. قال في "الولوالجية": قال: هذا إذا كان في موضع يخاف أن ينقطع به وليس ثمه قاض ولا سلطان يرفع الأمر إليه، فكان المؤثر في بقاء الإجارة كلا المعنيين انتهى ووجه بقاء الإجارة: أن الإجارة كما تنتقض بالأعذار تبقى بالأعذار ولو رضي الوارث وهو كبير ببقاء الإجارة، ورضي المستأجر جاز، فيجعل الرضاء بالبقاء إنشاء للعقد، فجوازها بالتعاطي. أحد المتعاقدين وهذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي: لا تبطل بالموت كالبيع. وإن عقدها لغيره: أي إذا عقد الإجارة لغيره بأن كان وكيلا أو وصيا له أو كان متولي الوقف ومات المباشر للعقد، لا تنفسخ؛ لبقاء المستحق حتى لو مات المعقود له بطلت؛ لما ذكرنا، وتنفسخ بموت أحد المؤجرين أو المستأجرين في حصته فقط، وبقيت في حصة الحي، وقال زفر: تبطل فيهما؛ لأن الشيوع مانع، قلنا: الشروط يراعي وجودها في الابتداء لا البقاء كالشهادة في النكاح كذا في "الفتح" مع زيادة. كالوكيل إلخ قال في "التكملة": أطلق في الوكيل، فشمل الوكيل بالإيجار والوكيل بالاستئجار، قال في "الذخيرة" : وأما الوكيل بالاستئجار إذا مات تبطل الإجارة؛ لأن التوكيل بالاستئجار توكيل شراء المنافع، فيصير مشتريا لنفسه، ثم يصير مؤجرا من الموكل انتهى أقول لعل هذا إذا لم يسلم إلى الموكل، أما لو سلم لا تبطل، فتدبره. انتهى تكملة البحر الرائق: 72/8]
It terminates by the death of one of the contracting parties if he contracted for himself; and if he contracted for another, like the agent, the lease terminates by his death [?] Ash-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad said: it does not become void by the death of one of them nor by the death of both, like sale. Our evidence: that the benefits and the rent have become property of the heirs, and the earlier contract did not exist from them, so it is annulled. It is restricted to death to exclude insanity; because the lease does not terminate by it even if continuous. This ruling (i.e., the dissolution of the contract without termination) is conditioned on there being no necessity. But if necessity arises, the lease remains with the named rent, and it is raised to the judge to do what is most appropriate, as when the lessor dies on the way to Mecca and there is no judge on the road; then it remains until Mecca, and the matter is raised to the judge to do the most appropriate: he may rent it out for him if he be trustworthy, or sell it for its value, and pay him the return fare if he proves his payment. It is said in al-Walwaljiyya: 'This is when it is in a place where he fears being cut off, and there is no judge or sultan to whom to refer the matter.' So the effective cause of the lease remaining is both meanings. The aspect of the lease remaining: that just as the lease is annulled by excuses, it remains due to excuses. If the heir, being of age, agrees to the continuation of the lease, and the lessee agrees, it is permissible; then the consent to remain is considered a new contract, so its permissibility is by mutual dealing. (Quoted from al-Fath, al-'Ayni, ad-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Radd al-Muhtar) One of the two contracting parties: this is according to us (Hanafis). Ash-Shafi'i said: it does not become void by death like sale. And if he contracted for another: i.e., if he contracted the lease for someone else, such as being an agent or executor (wasi) or administrator of a waqf, and the direct contractor dies, it does not terminate because the beneficiary remains. However, if the beneficiary (ma'qud lahu) dies, it terminates for the reason we mentioned. It terminates by the death of one of the lessors or lessees only in his share, and remains in the share of the living. Zafar said: it becomes void in both because indivisibility (shuyu') is an impediment. We said: conditions are considered at the beginning, not at the end, like testimony in marriage, as in al-Fath with additions. 'Like the agent' etc. It is said in at-Takmila: 'He generalizes regarding the agent, so it includes the agent for leasing out and the agent for hiring. It is said in adh-Dhakhira: As for the agent for hiring, if he dies, the lease is void because appointment for hiring is an appointment to purchase benefits; he becomes a buyer for himself and then acts as lessor for the principal.' I say: maybe this is if he has not handed over to the principal; but if he has, it does not become void. So consider it. End of Takmilat al-Bahr ar-Ra'iq 72/8.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rule on the effect of death of one of the parties in a lease contract, along with the opposing views of other schools (Shafi‘i, Maliki, Hanbali) and an intra-Hanafi opinion of Zafar. According to Abu Hanifa and his disciples, if a person leases for his own benefit (i.e., as a principal), the contract dissolves automatically upon the death of either the lessor or the lessee. This is because the subject matter (benefits) and the rent become part of the deceased's estate, and the contract was personal to the deceased. The other schools analogize to sale, which does not terminate upon death, but the Hanafis distinguish on the basis that the contract of lease is like a series of periodic exchanges; the relationship is personal and not transferable to heirs automatically. However, there is an exception: if necessity demands (e.g., the lessor dies en route to Hajj with the hired animal), the lease can remain until the judge can decide what is in the best interest. Additionally, if the lease was contracted by an agent (wakil), guardian, or trustee for the benefit of another, the death of the agent does not terminate the lease because the true beneficiary remains. The text also notes a minority Hanafi view from Zafar that in joint ownership, if one co-owner dies, the entire lease should dissolve because the undivided share is an impediment to continuation. But the majority holds that the lease continues in the share of the living co-owner, considering conditions only at inception. Finally, there is a refinement concerning the agent for hire: if an agent hires something on behalf of a principal and dies before transferring possession, the lease becomes void because the agent effectively bought the benefits for himself before transferring. However, if he had already handed over the property, the lease stands.

Key Terms
عقدها لنفسه (‘aqadahā li-nafsihi): The lease contract was entered into by a party for his own personal benefit, not as an agent or representative.
وكيل (wakīl): An agent authorized to contract on behalf of another. The death of a wakil does not dissolve the lease because the principal remains.
الشيوع (ash-shuyū‘): Indivisibility or common ownership. Zafar argued that if a co-owner dies, the lease cannot continue due to the indivisible nature of the rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person rents a house and then dies, what happens to the lease contract?
A) The lease continues and the heirs may use the house.
B) The lease terminates automatically because the contract was for the deceased's own benefit.
C) The lease continues if the lessor agrees.
D) The lease must be renewed by a judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a lease contract terminates by death of a party who contracted for themselves, with exceptions for agents and necessity, distinguishing lease from sale based on the periodic nature of benefit transfer.

Rescission of Ijarah by Death: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on death and rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rescission of ijarah by death of a party, distinguish between contracting for oneself and for another, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, ijarah rescinds automatically upon death of a party, unlike sale, because usufructs cannot be inherited and consent is lost.

This lesson examines the crucial difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings on the effect of death on an ijarah contract. While a sale contract survives the death of either party, the Hanafi school argues that ijarah is inherently different: usufructs (manafi') are consumed over time and cannot be returned like a physical object. Moreover, the consent of the parties is essential for the contract's continuity, and death terminates that consent. We will explore the proofs and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
Death of either the lessor or lessee rescinds the contract automatically if it was contracted for oneself.
If contracted for another (e.g., agent, executor), the contract does not rescind.
2
Understand the condition of 'for oneself'
The ruling applies only when the party contracted for their own benefit; if they acted as a representative, the contract continues after their death.
Similarly, if one of multiple lessors dies, only his share rescinds.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Upon death, the usufruct and rent become property of the heirs; the original contract did not come from them, so it is annulled. Also, the usufructs are consumed over time and cannot be returned like a sold object.
Hanafis analogize this to the case where the subject matter perishes before delivery.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that ijarah is not voided by death, because it is like a sale contract which continues.
Their proof: sale is not voided by death, and ijarah is a type of sale of usufructs.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Sale transfers ownership of a specific object, which can be inherited; ijarah transfers usufructs that are consumed over time and cannot be returned. Also, the contract's continuity requires ongoing consent, which is absent after death.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence): under Hanafi law, heirs must vacate; under Shafi'i, they may continue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة فسخ الإجارة وانقطاع ماء الضيعة ،والرحى، وتنفسخ بموت أحد المتعاقدين إن عقدها لنفسه، وإن عقدها لغيره لا كالوكيل تنفسخ بموته الإجارة القسم الأول الذي اختلف المشايخ فيه، قال في "ملا" مسكين": وقد اختلف المشايخ في هذه المسائل الثلاث، فقيل: تنفسخ بنفسها ولا يحتاج إلى الفسخ، قال في "الفتح": لأن المعقود عليه وهي المنافع قد فاتت، فصار كهلاك المبيع قبل القبض، والأول أي ما قال المصنف أصح؛ لأن المنافع قد فاتت على وجه يتصور عودها، فأشبه إباق المبيع قبل القبض، قال العيني: وهذا يشير إلى أن الإجارة لا تنفسخ بهذه الأشياء، وقال بعضهم: تنفسخ لفوات المقصود، والأول أصح؛ لأن المنافع فاتت على وجه يتصور عودها. (ملتقط من الشروح) وتنفسخ الخ: أي إذا عقد المتعاقدين الإجارة لنفسها، فمات أحدهما أي المؤجر أو المستأجر، تنفسخ الإجارة، ولا يحتاج إلى الفسخ، وقال الشافعي ومالك وأحمد لا تبطل بموت أحدهما ولا بموتهما كالبيع، ولنا: أن المنافع والأجرة صارت ملكا للورثة والعقد السابق لم يوجد منهم، فتنقض، وإنما قيد بالموت احترازا عن الجنون؛ لأنه لا تنفسخ الإجارة به، ولو مطبقا، وهذا الحكم أي انفساخ العقد بلا فسخ مقيد بما إذا لم يكن ثمه ضرورة، وأما إذا دعت ضرورة، فتبقى الإجارة بالأجر المسمى فيرفع إلى القاضي ليفعل ما هو الأصلح كما إذا مات المؤجر في طريق مكة، ولا حاكم في الطريق، فإنها تبقى إلى مكة فيرفع الأمر إلى القاضي ليفعل الأصلح، فيؤجرها له لو أمينا أو يبيعها بالقيمة، ويدفع له أجرة الإياب إن برهن على دفعها. قال في "الولوالجية": قال: هذا إذا كان في موضع يخاف أن ينقطع به وليس ثمه قاض ولا سلطان يرفع الأمر إليه، فكان المؤثر في بقاء الإجارة كلا المعنيين انتهى ووجه بقاء الإجارة: أن الإجارة كما تنتقض بالأعذار تبقى بالأعذار ولو رضي الوارث وهو كبير ببقاء الإجارة، ورضي المستأجر جاز، فيجعل الرضاء بالبقاء إنشاء للعقد، فجوازها بالتعاطي. (ملتقط من الفتح والعيني والدر المختار ورد المحتار) أحد المتعاقدين وهذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي: لا تبطل بالموت كالبيع. وإن عقدها لغيره: أي إذا عقد الإجارة لغيره بأن كان وكيلا أو وصيا له أو كان متولي الوقف ومات المباشر للعقد، لا تنفسخ؛ لبقاء المستحق حتى لو مات المعقود له بطلت؛ لما ذكرنا، وتنفسخ بموت أحد المؤجرين أو المستأجرين في حصته فقط، وبقيت في حصة الحي، وقال زفر: تبطل فيهما؛ لأن الشيوع مانع، قلنا: الشروط يراعي وجودها في الابتداء لا البقاء كالشهادة في النكاح كذا في "الفتح" مع زيادة. كالوكيل إلخ قال في "التكملة": أطلق في الوكيل، فشمل الوكيل بالإيجار والوكيل بالاستئجار، قال في "الذخيرة" : وأما الوكيل بالاستئجار إذا مات تبطل الإجارة؛ لأن التوكيل بالاستئجار توكيل شراء المنافع، فيصير مشتريا لنفسه، ثم يصير مؤجرا من الموكل انتهى أقول لعل هذا إذا لم يسلم إلى الموكل، أما لو سلم لا تبطل، فتدبره. انتهى تكملة والمتولي في الوقف، وتفسخ بخيار الشرط والرؤية وبالعذر عندنا خلافا للشافعي قال في "الفتح" نقلا عن الغير إن ما قال في "الذخيرة" مستقيم على ما ذكره الكرخي من أن الملك يثبت للوكيل، ثم ينتقل إلى الموكل لا على ما قاله أبو طاهر من أنه يثبت للموكل ابتداء، وبه جزم في "الكنز" وهو الأصح كما في البحر" فلا يستقيم، وتعقبه شيخنا بأنه غير مستقيم على ما ذكره الكرخي أيضا لاتفاقهم على عدم عتق قريب الوكيل؛ لأن ملكه غير متقرر والموجب للعتق الملك المتقرر انتهى أقول: فالحاصل أن الوكيل سواء كان للمؤجر أو للمستأجر لا يبطل العقد بموته، فاحفظه. عدم الجواز يصح والمتولي إلخ أطلقه، فعم ما لو كان المتولي موقوفا عليه و به صرح القهستاني. (فتح بقدر الحاجة) تفسخ الخ: لما فرغ عن بيان الفسخ بالعيب شرع في بيان الفسخ بخيار الشرط والرؤية وغيرهما، يعني إذا شرط المؤجر أو المستأجر خيار الشرط، أو كل منهما خيار الشرط ثلاثة أيام، فله أن يفسخ الإجارة به عندنا، وكذا إذا استأجر شيئا لم يره، فإذا رآه له أن لا يقبله ويفسخ الإجارة، وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز الفسخ بهما، أما في الأول؛ فلأن المستأجر لا يمكنه رد المعقود عليه بكماله إن كان الخيار له؛ إذ لابد من تلف شيء في مدة الخيار، وإن كان للمؤجر فلا يمكنه التسليم أيضا على الكمال؛ لأن ما مضى من المنفعة مدة الخيار لا يمكن تسليمه، وأما عدم الجواز في الثاني؛ فلأن الإجارة شراء المنافع، فلا يجوز أن يشتري ما لم يره للجهالة. ولنا في الأول: أنه عقد معاوضة، ولا يجب قبضه في المجلس، ويحتمل الفسخ بالإقالة، فيجوز شرط الخيار فيه كالبيع، قال في "العيني": وهذا أي الاختلاف في خيار الشرط مبني على أن إضافة الإجارة إلى الزمان المستقبل كما إذا أضافها إلى شهر رمضان، وهو في شعبان يجوز عندنا، فيصح اشتراط الخيار، ولا يجوز عنده، فلا الخيار. [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٨٦/٢] ولنا في الثاني: أن هذه الجهالة لا تمنع الجواز؛ لأنها لا تفضي إلى المنازعة؛ لأنه إذا رآه و لم يوافقه رده، فإذا رآه ثبت له خيار فسخ؛ لأن العقد لا يتم إلا بالرضاء، ولا رضا بدون العلم، وقال علي: "من اشترى شيئا لم يره فله الخيار إذا رآه"، ولأن الإجارة شراء المنافع، فتناولها الحديث. واعلم أنه اختلف في أنه يشترط في الفسخ بخيار الشرط وخيار الرؤية الرضاء أو القضاء كما يشترط في خيار العيب أم لا؟ وظاهر ما في الدر المختار: أنه يشترط فيهما أيضا، قال العلامة ابن عابدين في رد المحتار" بعد ما بحث فيه: والحاصل أنه لا يشترط القضاء أو الرضاء في خيار الشرط والرؤية، وأما في خيار العيب، ففي نحو انهدام الدار كلها يفسخ بغيبة صاحبه بخلاف انهدام الجدار ونحوه كما مر انتهى بقدر الحاجة، ثم اعلم أن خيار الرؤية يثبت للمستأجر، وأما للمؤجر فلا، قال في "رد المحتار: وأما خيار الرؤية فلا يكون للمؤجر كما في البيع. وبالعذر إلخ [وقال الشافعي: لا تفسخ بالأعذار إلا بالعيب (تكملة)] يعني تفسخ الإجارة بالعذر الذي هو العجز عن المضي في موجب العقد إلا بتحمل ضرر زائد لم يستحق المستأجر لذلك بنفس العقد، ثم العذر إذا تحقق تنفسخ بنفس العذر عند بعض المشايخ، وعند عامة المشايخ يحتاج فيه إلى الفسخ ، وهو الصحيح، ثم الفسخ =
Book of Ijarah. Rescission of Ijarah. And [due to] cessation of water of the estate and the mill, and it is rescinded by death of one of the two contracting parties if he contracted it for himself, and if he contracted it for another, it is not [rescinded] like the agent, it is rescinded by his death. The first section about which the mashayikh differed: It is said in 'Mulla Miskin': The mashayikh differed concerning these three issues. Some said: It rescinds by itself and does not need rescission. It is said in al-Fath: Because the subject matter, which is the usufructs, has ceased, so it becomes like destruction of the sold item before delivery. The first, i.e., what the author said, is more correct because the usufructs have ceased in a manner that their return can be imagined, so it resembles the absconding of the sold item before delivery. Al-Ayni said: This indicates that ijarah is not rescinded by these things. And some said: It is rescinded due to loss of the purpose, and the first is more correct because the usufructs ceased in a manner that their return can be imagined. (Taken from the commentaries) 'And it is rescinded' etc.: That is, if the two contracting parties contracted ijarah for themselves, and one of them dies, whether the lessor or lessee, the ijarah is rescinded and does not need rescission. Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad said: It is not voided by death of either or both, like sale. Our proof: The usufructs and the rent become the property of the heirs, and the previous contract did not come from them, so it is annulled. And it is restricted to death to exclude insanity, because ijarah is not rescinded by it, even if continuous. And this ruling, i.e., rescission of contract without rescission, is conditioned on there being no necessity. But if necessity arises, the ijarah remains with the named rent, and the matter is raised to the judge to do what is most beneficial, like when the lessor dies on the road to Mecca and there is no judge on the road, then it remains until Mecca, and the matter is raised to the judge to do what is most beneficial: he leases it for him if trustworthy, or sells it at market value, and pays him the return fare if he proves payment. It is said in al-Walwaljiyya: This is when he is in a place where he fears being cut off, and there is no judge or authority to refer the matter to him, so the effect on the continuation of ijarah is both meanings. The reason for the continuation of ijarah: Just as ijarah is annulled by excuses, it continues by excuses. And if the heir, being an adult, consents to the continuation of ijarah and the lessee consents, it is permissible, and the consent to continuation is considered a new contract, so its permissibility is by mutual giving. (Taken from al-Fath, al-Ayni, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Radd al-Muhtar) 'One of the two contracting parties' – this is our view, and al-Shafi'i said: It is not voided by death like sale. 'And if he contracted it for another': That is, if he contracted ijarah for another, such as being an agent, executor, or mutawalli of a waqf, and the direct contractor dies, it is not rescinded because the entitlement remains, so much so that if the one for whom it was contracted dies, it is rescinded for the reason mentioned. And it is rescinded by death of one of the lessors or lessees only in his share, and it remains in the share of the living. Zufar said: It is voided in both because co-ownership is a barrier. We say: Conditions are considered at the beginning, not throughout, like testimony in marriage. Similarly in al-Fath with addition. 'Like the agent' etc. It is said in al-Takmila: He spoke generally about the agent, so it includes the agent for leasing and the agent for hiring. It is said in al-Dhakhira: As for the agent for hiring, if he dies, the ijarah is voided because hiring by an agent is hiring for purchase of usufructs, so he becomes a buyer for himself, then becomes a lessor from the principal. I say: Perhaps this is if he has not delivered to the principal; but if he has delivered, it is not voided, so reflect. End of Takmila. And the executor and mutawalli of the waqf, and it is rescinded by option of condition, option of sight, and excuse, according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. It is said in al-Fath, quoting someone: What is said in al-Dhakhira is correct according to what al-Karkhi mentioned that ownership is established for the agent then transfers to the principal, not according to what Abu Tahir said that it is established for the principal initially, and that is affirmed in al-Kanz and it is the more correct as in al-Bahr, so it is not sound. Our teacher commented that it is not sound according to what al-Karkhi mentioned either, because they agree that the relative of the agent is not freed because his ownership is not established, and what necessitates freeing is established ownership. I say: The conclusion is that the agent, whether for the lessor or lessee, the contract is not invalidated by his death, so memorize it. 'Non-permissibility' is correct. 'And the mutawalli' etc. he made it general, so it includes when the mutawalli is a beneficiary, and al-Qahistani stated this. (Fath bi qadr al-haja) 'It is rescinded' etc.: When he finished explaining rescission by defect, he began explaining rescission by option of condition and option of sight and others. That is, if the lessor or lessee stipulates an option of condition, or each of them stipulates an option of condition for three days, he may rescind the ijarah by it according to us. Likewise, if he hires something he has not seen, then when he sees it, he may refuse to accept it and rescind the ijarah. Al-Shafi'i said: Rescission by both is not permissible. As for the first, because the lessee cannot return the subject matter completely if the option is for him, since something must be lost during the option period; and if the option is for the lessor, he also cannot deliver completely because the usufruct that passed during the option period cannot be delivered. As for the impermissibility in the second, because ijarah is purchase of usufructs, and it is not permissible to buy what one has not seen due to ignorance. Our proof for the first: It is a commutative contract, and delivery is not required in the session, and it can be rescinded by mutual rescission, so stipulating an option is permissible like sale. Al-Ayni said: This difference regarding option of condition is based on the fact that adding ijarah to future time, like adding it to Ramadan while in Sha'ban, is permissible according to us, so stipulating the option is valid, but not according to him, so no option. (Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/286) Our proof for the second: This ignorance does not prevent permissibility because it does not lead to dispute, since if he sees it and is not satisfied, he returns it, and when he sees it, the option of rescission is established because the contract is not completed except with consent, and there is no consent without knowledge. Ali said: "Whoever buys something he has not seen has the option when he sees it." And because ijarah is purchase of usufructs, so the hadith applies to it. Know that there is disagreement about whether consent or court order is required for rescission by option of condition and option of sight, as is required in option of defect. The apparent meaning in al-Durr al-Mukhtar is that it is required in both. Allama Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar, after investigating, said: The conclusion is that court order or consent is not required in option of condition and option of sight. As for option of defect, in cases like total collapse of the house, rescission occurs in the owner's absence, unlike partial collapse of a wall etc., as previously mentioned. End of needed portion. Then know that option of sight is established for the lessee, but not for the lessor. It is said in Radd al-Muhtar: Option of sight does not apply to the lessor, as in sale. 'And by excuse' etc. [Al-Shafi'i said: It is not rescinded by excuses except by defect (Takmila)] That is, ijarah is rescinded by an excuse which is the inability to proceed with the contract except by bearing an additional harm that the lessee did not incur by the contract itself. Then when the excuse is realized, it rescinds by itself according to some mashayikh, and according to the majority of mashayikh, it needs rescission, and this is correct. Then the rescission =
