Liability for Eating Provisions in a Hire Contract
Ruling on the rider eating from the provisions during the journey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a rider eating from provisions in a hire contract and explain why the Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i custom-based argument.

Core Idea
Eating provisions reduces the carried amount, so compensation is wajib; contested custom does not override.

In a hire contract for a riding animal, the hirer pays for the animal and usually provides provisions (zād) to be carried. If the rider consumes some of those provisions, does he owe compensation? The Hanafi school says yes, while some Shafi'is argue that custom exempts him. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the basis for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: The rider must compensate (radd 'iwad) for what he eats from the provisions.
The ruling is based on the hirer's right to have the full provisions carried throughout the journey.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Some Shafi'is hold that no compensation is required, citing the custom ('urf) of travelers who eat without returning.
Custom is used to interpret the contract's implicit terms.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof relies on 'urf: since travelers commonly eat from provisions without compensation, the contract is presumed to include that permission.
The argument is that the absolute (muṭlaq) contract is qualified by custom.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that custom must be uniform and consistent; here it is contested. Some travelers do return what they eat. Non-return may be because they were sated, not because of a legal exemption. The hirer has a right to the entire quantity; eating reduces it, so compensation is due.
The Hanafi position is reinforced by analogy with water: if water is consumed, compensation is owed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis require compensation; Shafi'is may not. This affects the financial obligations of the parties.
The Hanafi position is muftā bihī (relied upon for fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمقدار زاد فأكل منه رد عوضه، وتصح الإجارة وفسخها والمزارعة والمعاملة والمستأجر العمل: سواء اتحد العمل أو اختلف كخياط مع قصار (فتح) صح هذا الفعل استحسانا؛ لأن هذه شركة الصنائع لا إجارة. محملا بفتح الميم الأول وكسر الثاني أو بالعكس: الهودج الكبير. (مسكين) صح: أي استحسانا والقياس أن لا يجوز، وهو قول الإمام الشافعي؛ لأنه فيه جهالة، وجه الاستحسان أن المقصود هو الراكب وهو المعلوم، والمحمل تابع وما فيه من الجهالة تزول بالصرف إلى المتعارف وله المتعارف من الحمل والزاد والغطاء وغير ذلك مما هو معلوم عند أهل العرف، لا يقال: هذه متكررة مع قوله: وإن استأجر حمارا و لم يسم ما يحمل، قلنا: هناك لم يبين ما يحمل، فكانت الجهالة فاحشة وههنا بين ما يحمل فكانت يسيرة؛ لأنه بين الحمل، ولم يبين قدره. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۷۷/۸] (عيني) ورؤيته: أي رؤية المكاري المحمل والراكب وما يتبعهما. أحب لأنه أقرب لحصول الرضا، وعند أحمد: لا بدون المشاهدة.
And the amount of provisions: if he eats from it, he must return its equivalent.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the liability of a rider who eats from the provisions (zād) that are part of the hire contract for a camel. The ruling states that if the rider eats from the provisions, he must compensate (radd 'iwad). This is the Hanafi position. The commentary elaborates that some Shafi'is hold that no compensation is required because the custom of travelers is to eat without returning. However, the Hanafi response is that the rider owes the carriage of a known quantity of provisions throughout the journey; eating reduces that quantity, so compensation is due, just like water. Custom is not uniform: some travelers return, some don't. If non-return is due to being sated, that does not establish a custom. If the condition to return is explicitly agreed, it is valid by consensus. If condition to not return is stipulated, it is invalid by consensus.

Key Terms
عوض ('iwad): Compensation or replacement for something consumed.
عرف ('urf): Customary practice that can qualify contractual terms.
جهالة (jahāla): Uncertainty or ambiguity that can render a contract invalid if excessive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, why must a rider compensate for eating from the provisions during a camel hire?
A) Because the camel needs the food
B) Because the owner of the camel has a right to the full provisions
C) Because the rider explicitly agreed to pay
D) Because custom requires it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a rider who eats from provisions in a hire contract to compensate, rejecting the Shafi'i custom argument because the custom is not uniform and the hirer's right to the full load is paramount.

Validity of Adding Ijarah and Related Contracts to Future Time
Ruling on validity of idafah in ijarah contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding ijarah, muzara'ah, and mu'amalah to a future time, and distinguish idafah from ta'liq.

Core Idea
Idafah (adding to future) makes ijarah valid; ta'liq (suspension) makes it invalid.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that hire contracts can be validly concluded for a future date, a unique feature based on the gradual nature of ijarah. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion with conditional contracts and clarifies the scope of validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts covered
The ruling applies to ijarah (hire), its cancellation (faskh), muzara'ah (sharecropping), and mu'amalah (musaqah, tree partnership).
2
Understand the ruling
These contracts are valid when added to a future time (idafah). The Hanafi school considers them sahih.
3
Distinguish idafah from ta'liq
Idafah is a definite future start (e.g., 'from next month'), while ta'liq is a conditional suspension (e.g., 'if tomorrow comes'). Idafah is valid; ta'liq is invalid.
4
Recognize the rationale
Ijarah takes effect gradually (shay'an fa shay'an), so attaching to a future time is possible. Muzara'ah and mu'amalah follow the same principle.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Other schools (like Shafi'i) may require the contract to take effect immediately. Hanafi istihsan allows idafah despite apparent gharar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتصح الإجارة وفسخها والمزارعة والمعاملة والمستأجر العمل: سواء اتحد العمل أو اختلف كخياط مع قصار (فتح) صح هذا الفعل استحسانا؛ لأن هذه شركة الصنائع لا إجارة. محملا بفتح الميم الأول وكسر الثاني أو بالعكس: الهودج الكبير. (مسكين) صح: أي استحسانا والقياس أن لا يجوز، وهو قول الإمام الشافعي؛ لأنه فيه جهالة، وجه الاستحسان أن المقصود هو الراكب وهو المعلوم، والمحمل تابع وما فيه من الجهالة تزول بالصرف إلى المتعارف وله المتعارف من الحمل والزاد والغطاء وغير ذلك مما هو معلوم عند أهل العرف، لا يقال: هذه متكررة مع قوله: وإن استأجر حمارا و لم يسم ما يحمل، قلنا: هناك لم يبين ما يحمل، فكانت الجهالة فاحشة وههنا بين ما يحمل فكانت يسيرة؛ لأنه بين الحمل، ولم يبين قدره. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۷۷/۸] (عيني) ورؤيته: أي رؤية المكاري المحمل والراكب وما يتبعهما. أحب لأنه أقرب لحصول الرضا، وعند أحمد: لا بدون المشاهدة.
And the hire and its cancellation, muzara'ah, and mu'amalah (musaqah) are valid when added to the future.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the validity of attaching contracts like ijarah (hire), its cancellation (faskh), muzara'ah (sharecropping), and mu'amalah (musaqah, tree partnership) to a future time. The Hanafi position is that these contracts can be validly concluded for a future date, e.g., saying in Sha'ban: 'I hire you this house from the first of Ramadan.' The rationale is that ijarah comes into effect gradually (shay'an fa shay'an), so adding to the future is possible. Faskh is considered accordingly. The text also notes a view from Abu Bakr that both phrasings (explicit future addition vs. conditional) are valid. Muzara'ah and mu'amalah are treated like ijarah because they are types of hire. This contrasts with conditional (ta'līq) formulations like 'if tomorrow comes, I hire you,' which are invalid because they are suspensive conditions.

Key Terms
إضافة (idāfah): Attaching a contract to a future time, e.g., 'I hire you from next month.'
تعليق (ta'līq): Suspending a contract on a future condition, e.g., 'If tomorrow comes, I hire you.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, which of the following statements about adding a hire contract to a future time is correct?
A) It is invalid because the future is unknown
B) It is valid if stated explicitly, e.g., 'I hire you from next month'
C) It is valid only if the future date is conditional
D) It is invalid for muzara'ah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ijarah and similar contracts can be validly added to a definite future time (idafah), but not suspended on a condition (ta'liq).

Hiring Camel with Sedan: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Rulings on specific ijarah contracts with istihsan and custom-based resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a hire contract with unspecified load via istihsan and state the compensation rule for consumed provisions.

Core Idea
Custom (urf) resolves minor uncertainty in contracts; the hirer must compensate for consumed provisions.

The Hanafi school often uses istihsan to achieve justice when strict analogy (qiyas) would lead to hardship. In this passage, we see two such cases: hiring a camel with a sedan and riders, and a hirer eating from the provisions he was hired to carry. The underlying principle is that minor uncertainty (jahalah yasirah) resolved by custom does not invalidate a contract, and obligations arising from the contract must be fulfilled unless custom clearly indicates otherwise. This lesson will walk through the Hanafi position, the Shafi'i objection, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on hiring camel with sedan
Read the first part of the passage and identify the ruling: the contract is valid by istihsan. Note that the sedan (mihmal) and two riders are mentioned, but the load amount is not specified.
The Hanafi position relies on the fact that the rider is known and the sedan is subsidiary; custom determines the load.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
The passage mentions that by qiyas, the contract would be invalid due to uncertainty (jahalah). This is the view of Imam al-Shafi'i. Understand his reasoning: any uncertainty in the subject matter of ijarah invalidates the contract.
Shafi'i school generally requires precise specification of the subject matter.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response: istihsan and custom
The Hanafi response distinguishes between gross and minor uncertainty. Here, the uncertainty is minor because the main object (riding the camel to Makkah) is known, and the load is subsidiary. Custom (urf) fills in the details.
Istihsan allows departure from qiyas when the outcome would be harsh or contrary to public interest.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf for the first issue
The practical consequence: Hanafis deem the contract valid and enforceable; Shafi'is deem it invalid. This affects whether the hirer can sue for breach, etc.
The dispute also extends to compensation for eaten provisions, as seen next.
5
Analyse the compensation for eaten provisions
Read the second part of the passage. The hirer eats from the provisions he was supposed to carry. Hanafis rule he must compensate; some Shafi'is say no, based on custom. The Hanafi response: custom is not uniform, and the obligation to carry a known amount remains.
If the hirer had stipulated return, it is valid by consensus; if stipulated no return, invalid by consensus.

العمل بالنصف صح، وإن استأجر جملا ليحمل عليه محملا، وراكبين إلى مكة صح، يقعدان فيه

المستأجر
العمل: سواء اتحد العمل أو اختلف كخياط مع قصار (فتح) صح هذا الفعل استحسانا؛ لأن هذه شركة الصنائع لا إجارة. محملا بفتح الميم الأول وكسر الثاني أو بالعكس: الهودج الكبير. (مسكين) صح: أي استحسانا والقياس أن لا يجوز، وهو قول الإمام الشافعي؛ لأنه فيه جهالة، وجه الاستحسان أن المقصود هو الراكب وهو المعلوم، والمحمل تابع وما فيه من الجهالة تزول بالصرف إلى المتعارف وله المتعارف من الحمل والزاد والغطاء وغير ذلك مما هو معلوم عند أهل العرف، لا يقال: هذه متكررة مع قوله : وإن استأجر حمارا ولم يسم ما يحمل، قلنا: هناك لم يبين ما يحمل، فكانت الجهالة فاحشة وههنا بين ما يحمل فكانت يسيرة؛ لأنه بين الحمل، ولم يبين قدره. تكملة البحر الرائق: ۷۷/۸] (عيني) ورؤيته : أي رؤية المكاري المحمل والراكب وما يتبعهما. أحب لأنه أقرب لحصول الرضا، وعند أحمد: لا بدون المشاهدة. ولمقدار زاد إلخ عطف على قوله : ليحمل؛ لأن معناه لأن يحمل أي للحمل] يعني إذا استأجر جملا ليحمل عليه مقدارا من الزاد، فأكل منه في الطريق رد عوضه، وقال بعض الشافعية: لا يرد؛ لأن عرف المسافرين أنهم يأكلون الزاد ولا يردون والمطلق يحمل على المتعارف بخلاف الماء حيث يكون له الرد؛ لأن العرف جرى برده، ولنا: أنه استحق عليه حمل مقدار معلوم في جميع الطريق، فله أن يستوفيه فصار كالماء، والعرف مشترك، فإن بعض المسافرين يردون، فلا يلزمنا عرف البعض، أو يحمل فعل من لا يرد على أنهم استغنوا فلا يلزم حجة، ويرد بعضهم وهم المحتاجون إليه تكملة البحر الرائق: ۷۷/۸] وهذا الاختلاف إذا لم يشترط الرد، وأما إذا شرط الرد صح بالإجماع، ولو شرط عدمه لم يصح بالإجماع. (عيني)
The Book of Ijarah
Miscellaneous Issues
Work for half is valid. And if one hires a camel to carry on it a sedan [mihmal] and two riders to Makkah, it is valid; they both sit in it. And he has the customary load, and seeing it is loved, and if he increases the provisions and eats from it, he returns its substitute. And the hired [camel] is valid among people.
Ijarah and its rescission, and muzara'ah, and mu'amalah.
Ijarah and it is musaqah.
The hired [party] Work: whether the work is the same or different, like a tailor with a washerman – this act is valid by istihsan, because this is a partnership of crafts, not ijarah. 'Mihmal': with fatha on the first meem and kasra on the second, or vice versa: the large howdaj. (Miskin) He said: valid by istihsan, and by qiyas it is not valid, and it is the statement of Imam al-Shafi'i, because there is uncertainty in it. The reason for istihsan is that the intended is the rider, who is known, and the sedan is subsidiary, and the uncertainty in it is removed by referring to what is customary, and he has the customary load, provisions, covering, and other things known among people of custom. It cannot be said: this is repeated with his statement: 'And if one hires a donkey and does not specify what to carry', we say: there he did not specify what to carry, so the uncertainty was gross; here he specified what to carry, so it was minor, because he specified the carriage but did not specify its amount. Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 77/8] (Ayni) 'And seeing it': i.e., seeing the carrier, the sedan, the rider, and what accompanies them. 'It is loved' because it is closer to achieving satisfaction. And according to Ahmad: it is not valid without viewing. 'And the amount of provisions, etc.' is a conjunction to his statement 'to carry', because its meaning is for carrying, i.e., for carriage. That is, if he hires a camel to carry on it an amount of provisions, and he eats from it on the way, he returns its substitute. And some Shafi'is said: he does not have to return, because the custom of travelers is that they eat provisions and do not return, and the absolute is carried on the customary in contrast to water, where he must return because custom goes with its return. And for us: that he [the hirer] is entitled to carry a known amount over the entire journey, so he may exact it, so it becomes like water. And custom is shared, for some travelers return, so the custom of some does not bind us, or the action of those who do not return is carried on that they were satisfied, so no evidence is binding, and some do return, namely those in need of it. Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 77/8] And this difference is when return is not stipulated. But if he stipulates return, it is valid by consensus, and if he stipulates not to return, it is not valid by consensus. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage deals with two rulings from the masa'il mutafarriqa of ijarah. First, the validity of working for half share (like mudaraba-like partnership). Second, the case of hiring a camel with a sedan (mihmal) and two riders to Makkah, where the load is unspecified but referred to custom. The Hanafi position is that such a contract is valid by istihsan, because the rider is known and the sedan is subsidiary, and custom removes the uncertainty. This is contrary to qiyas and the view of Imam al-Shafi'i who deems it invalid due to gharar. The passage also discusses the obligation to compensate if the hirer eats from the provisions he was supposed to carry. Hanafis rule that he must compensate because he is obligated to carry a specific amount; the custom of travelers is not uniform. There is a consensus if return is stipulated. The passage ends by transitioning to a broader discussion of contracts added to future time.

Key Terms
محملا (mihmal): A sedan chair or howdah placed on a camel for passengers.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that sets aside a strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or public interest.
جهالة (jahalah): Uncertainty or ignorance in a contract that may lead to invalidity; classified as gross (fahishah) or minor (yasirah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is hiring a camel with a sedan and two riders to Makkah valid despite the load not being precisely specified?
A) Because the contract is a partnership, not ijarah.
B) Because the uncertainty is gross and thus ignored.
C) Because the sedan is subsidiary and custom (urf) resolves the ambiguity.
D) Because the riders are unknown.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan and custom to validate contracts with minor uncertainty, and upholds obligations like compensation for consumed provisions unless custom is uniform to the contrary.
